O vos, tres chiers filz, je vos ai acomplit cest livre qui est li derriens de la science de medicine ensamble l’emplissement de lui, et ai fait la fin per ses expositions et par ses declarations.	You dear children, I have completed this book which is the culmination of the science of medicine, bringing together its completion through my explanations and declarations.
Et m’est venu en vision que je le vos acomplisse avec cest traitier, qui est partie de l’uevre de mains, c’est a savoir «cyrurgie».	And it came to me in vision that I would complete it with this treatise, which is part of the work of hands, namely "surgery".
Et por ceu que l’uevre de mains est fortraite en nostre region et est etraingie dou tout en tout, si est perie li science et decopee, et n’est riens demorez de li fuers que les petites descriptions en livres des anciens que les mains ont muees.	And because the work of hands is well established in our region and has spread everywhere, it has lost its science and been divided up, and nothing remains from it except for small descriptions in books written by the ancients that were handled by hands.
Et de ceu est venue li error et li vanitez, et sont closes les ententions et est aloignie li science.	And because of this, there has come error and vanity, and closed are the minds, and the science is far away.
Or me semble que je la vuel vivifier ensamble l’ordination de cest traitier selonc la voie d’exposition et de declaration et de l’abreviation;	It seems to me that I can revive this treatise as a whole according to the method of exposition and declaration, and abbreviation;
et venrai ensamble les formes des ferremens de cautere, et des autres estrumens de l’uevre avec l’ajostement de la declaration et de preparation de li, sicom il est mestier.	And I will gather together the forms of the metal cauterizing tools, and other surgical instruments for use, along with their appropriate presentation and preparation, as necessary.
Et por la raison de ceu que nuls boins maistres de mains n’est trovez en nostre tens, est li ars de medicine eslongié.	And because no good masters are found in our times, the art of medicine has been neglected.
Et covient celui qui s’en entremet sormonter en la science d’anathomie, si com Galiens dit, tant qu’il saiche la juement des menbres, et les formes et les conjunctions et les separations d’aus, et aient connissance des osses et des nerf et des brais et le nombre d’ous, et le demenement et des voines movans et des reposans, et dou leu de lor issue.	And he who intervenes should ascend in the science of anatomy, as Galen says, so long as they know how to judge members, and their forms and connections and separations, and have knowledge of bones and nerves and muscles, and the number of bones, and their movement and the moving and resting veins, and where their exit lies.
Et por ceu dist Ypocras que li nons avec le non est mout, et avec l’uevre est poc;	And as Hippocrates said that inaction with no action is much, and with work is less;
et meismement en l’art de main.	And similarly in the art of manual skills.
Nos vos disons en l’introite de cest livre que qui n’est conissans des choses devant dites, si se gart qu’il ne chiece en error et qu’il n’ocie les homes;	We will inform you at the beginning of this book that if someone is unaware of the matters previously mentioned, they might go wrong and idle people.
ensi que j’ai veut maintes fois plusors de ces qui s’entremettent de ceste science et si s’abandonent sen science et sens experiment.	As I have seen many times, those who interfere with this science and abandon their knowledge and experiments.
Car je vis un fol mire qui copa I apostume de scrophules ou col d’une femme, et copa les arteres dou col;	For I saw a foolish surgeon who excised an abscess or neck sore of scrofula in a woman, and cut the arteries from her neck;
por coi tant de sanc issit hors que li femme cheit morte entre ses mains.	because so much blood came out that the woman died in her hands.
Et vis I autre mire qui traït une piere d’un home d’eaige, et li piere estoit grans;	And I saw another surgeon treating a stone in an elderly man, and the stone was large;
si emporta avec li une piece de la vessie, et fut mors li hons dedens III jors.	he took out with it a piece of the bladder, and the man died within three days.
Et je i avoie ja esteit apelez por lou traire, et vis la disposition dou malaide et la grandor de la piere, et soi bien s’on lou tailloit il en morroit.	And I have already been called to extract, and saw the position of the organ and the size of the stone, and indeed if they had cut him he would have died.
Et vis I autre mire qui prist en cure I duc de nostre terre qui avoit la jambe brisie, et avec la briseure ot plaie;	And I saw another surgeon who treated our local count who had his leg broken, and with the breaking came an injury;
et li mires plains d’ignorance estraint la brisure sus la plaie as esteles par fort lieure, et ne lassa a la plaie point de xalain, et le lassa ensi I termine;	and the surgeons full of ignorance bound the breaking above the injury as it had been by strong ligature, and did not allow any salve to touch the wound, and they left him like this at the end.
et li comanda qu’il ne la desliast mie;	And instruct him not to dislocate it again;
et demora ensi que li jambe fut toute enflee et li piez et vint a perdition.	So he should stay like this, until the leg was fully extended and the feet reached their position, or else it would lead to ruin.
Je fuis apelez por venir a lui, et me hastai por venir deslier la jambe;	I rushed to be called for him, and I hurried to come and reset the leg;
et quant je l’oi desloie si fut em pais et ne sentit point de dolor.	And when I heard it dislocated so smoothly without any pain being felt.
Mais toute voie li corruptions estoit ja confermee ou membre, et ne la poi saner;	But all the corruption was already confirmed throughout his body or limb, and he could not be cured;
et ne cessa li corrution d’aler par le membre tant que li membres fut dou tout perdus.	And the corruption continued spreading through the limb as long as any part of it was still intact.
Et vis .i. autre mire qui effondra .i. apostume enchancreit, et puis enflama per le malice de sa signorie.	And there is another method that collapses an abscessed wound, and then inflames it through the wickedness of her lordship.
Car chancre, quant il est purs d’umor melancolique, ne covient mie qu’on i(l) touche de fer s’il n’est en teil leu c’on puisse toute oster ce que est corrumpus.	For a chancre, when it is full of melancholic humor, it should not be touched with iron if it cannot all be removed, what has been corrupted.
Et por ceu, treschier filz, vos est besoig que vos sachiez que oevre de mains est devisee en II divisions:	And because of this, dear children, you need to know that the art of medicine is divided into two parts:
c’est asavoir, huevre ou il a peril en plusors dispositions;	This means "It's like this, where there are risks in various positions.
et je mostrerai en chescun leu de cest livre ou il a paour et peril.	And I will show you in each section of this book where there is danger and risk.
Por coi il est besoig que vos vos en gardez, si que li fol mire ne puissent mal parler de vos.	Because it's necessary that you keep them in mind, so that the illiterate don't have reason to speak poorly of you.
Si prenez vos armes en cusenson, et entreprenez vos malaides legierement et fermement, et usez de la millor voie si que per la graice de Deu vos venez a salut et soiez loez;	If you take your weapons with caution, treat your patients lightly yet firmly, and employ the best method so that through God's grace you may reach salvation and be content;
et lassiez les maladies espoantables de grief saniteit;	and leave insurmountable complaints without health or cure;
et ostez vos armes de ceu que vos fait douter, et aiez foit en vos si que vos puissiez venir de cestui monde a l’autre de gloire.	and use your weapons against those who make you doubt, and have faith in yourself so that you may come from this world to the other with glory.
Galiens dist en aucuns de ses amonestemens:	Galiens states in some of his admonishments:
«Ne prenez mie en cure male maladie, que vos ne soiez apelez fol mire.	Never undertake an inappropriate treatment for your illness, lest you be called mad instead of healed.
» J’ai deviseit cest traitier selonc III chapitres.	I have composed this treatise according to three chapters.
Li premiers chapitres est des cauteres de feu et dé cauteres de medicine ague, et est li chapitres ordenez de lou chief jusques as piez;	The first chapters deal with fire cautery and medical cautery, and are arranged from the head down to the stones";
et des formes des estrumens, et des ferremens de cautere, et de tout ceu qui est necessaire en l’ueuvre.	and the forms of the instruments, and the metal of the cautery, and all that is necessary for the work.
Li secons chapitres si est de taillier et de percier, et des ventouses et des plaies, et des estractions des saiettes, et des semblans choses;	The second chapters are about cutting and piercing, and suction cups and wounds, and the extraction of arrows, and similar matters.";
et est li chapitres ordenez et les formes des estrumens.	and these chapters are organized with the forms of the instruments.
Li tiers chapitres est de restorer les dislocations et des torcions, et des semblans choses;	The third chapter is about restoring dislocations and twists, and similar matters.";
et est ordeneiz des lou chief jusc’as piez, et des formes des estrumens.	And arranged are the commands for lifting the head until the neck, and concerning the shapes of the instruments.
Ainsois que nos nos remembriens de l’uevre, il covient que je die la qualiteit de l’aide et dou nuisement de chescune complexion.	Just as we remember our work, it is necessary for me to tell you about the quality of each remedy and its harm associated with each temperament.
Je dis que li qualiteis de l’aide, et dou nuisement, est li plus longe parole et subtilz science et li secrez reponus;	I say that the qualities of help, and harm, is the longest speech and most subtle science and the hidden responses;
et de ceu parlerent li plusors des saiges, et s’acorderent a ceu;	And many wise people spoke about this, and they agreed on it;
et me soffisent poc lor paroles, car je redous la longesce.	And their words bother me somewhat because I fear the length of them.
Je dis que cautere aide universement a toute complexion ou il a matiere, fuer que II complexions:	I say that the cautery helps universally with all constitutions where there is matter, because there are two constitutions:
c’est a savoir complexion chaude sens matere, et complexion seche sens matere.	This means to know hot constitution with matter and dry constitution with matter.
En complexion chaude et seche ensamble matiere, deviserent aucun et dirent que cautere i est grans aide;	In the combination of hot and dry constitutions with matter, they devised nothing and said that the cautery is great help;
et li autre dirent le contraire:	And others said the opposite:
que cautere ne vaut a maladie que vient de chalor et de sechour.	that cautery only works on diseases that come from heat and dryness.
Car li nature dou feu si est chaude, et ne doit mie estre cureiz de chaude maladie par chalor, ne per sechour;	For the nature of fire is so hot, and it should not be treated with hot diseases through heat or dryness;
et dist cil qui dist lou contraire que cautere fait grant aide a maladie chaude et seche que vient en cors des homes.	And those who say the opposite state that cautery provides great aid to hot and dry diseases that originate within the body.
Car quant tu comperes le cors de l’ome et sa moistor a la complexion dou feu, tu trueves le cors froit.	For when you compare the body of the person and their moisture to the aspect of fire, you find that the body is cold.
Et je m’acorde a ceste parole.	And I agree with this word.
Car je l’ai troveit aucune fois per experiment.	For I have found it true on every occasion by experiment.
Et toute voie, ne s’en entremette mie fuers que cil qui l’a esproveit, et qui conoit par lonc usaige le chapistre des cauteres, et la diversiteit des complexions des homes, et les dispositions et les causes de lor maladies, et les sorvenues et l’espaice dou tens;	And in all matters, do not interfere except for those who have experienced it themselves, and who understand through long use the chapter of cautery, and the variety of people's complexions, and their conditions and causes of illnesses, and their symptoms and timing.
des autres complexions n’avons nos mie paour, meismement em maladies froides et moistes.	For other types of complexion, we have none for them either, especially in the case of cold and damp illnesses.
Et tuit li mire s’asemblerent et s’acorderent au cautere.	And all the instruments gathered together with the cautery.
Et sachiez, filz, que cautere ensamble feu si est des secrez des cures, et de plus grant bonteit que cautere de medicine ardant.	Know, children, that when a fire cautery is assembled, it contains the secrets of healing, and offers more benefit than a burning medical treatment.
Car li feus est simples, et ne vient mie fuers que au membre qui est cuis, et ne nuit a autre membre se poc nom.	For fire is simple, and does not come forth from any member except that which is cooked, and it harms no other member if you do not name it.
Les medicines ardans vienent de membre a autre en aloignant, et font venir au membre maladies de grief sanation;	The hot medicines travel from limb to limb spreading disease instead of healing;
et par aventure ocit lou malaide.	and by chance cause harm to the patient.
Li feus por sa hautece et por la bonteit de sa substance ne fait mie ceu, s’il n’i a superfluiteit.	The fire for its height and due to the goodness of its substance does not make this if there is no excess.
Et ceu vos ai je troveit par experiment et par la longesce dou servise et de l’estude que j’ai mis en l’art, et esteit sus la verteit des choses;	And this is what I have found through experimentation and the length of my service and study in the art, and it corresponds to the truth of things;
et por ceu je m’escuse de la longesce de la parole, car il ne me plait mie que je vos oste le secreit qui est reponus ou feu, et la qualiteit de l’uevre, coment il deboute les maladies des cors, si com li philosophe le dit en demostrant;	And because of this, I apologize for the length of my speech, as I do not want to withhold the secret which lies in the fire and the quality of work, how it expels diseases from the body, as the philosopher demonstrates through demonstration;
or le recevez en vos pensees.	Receive it in your thoughts.
Et sachiez, fil, que il s’acorderent en quel tens doient estre faites les cauteres, et eslirent prientens.	And know, child, that they agreed on when the cauterizations should be done, and read prayers.
Et je dis que cautere est covenable en tous tens, por ceu que li nuisemens sorvenans est desoz mis par l’aide dou cautere;	And I say that cautery is applicable in all circumstances, for the nuisances arising are minimized by the aid of the cautery;
et meismement se li cauteres est por dolors necessaires fors et hastans que ne puent atendre le tens que plus grans malice ne veigne au membre.	And indeed, if the cautery is for necessary pains that cannot wait until the time when greater harm does not come to the limb.
Et n’i pensez onques, chier fil, si com font li fol mire;	And never think it, dear child, as foolish people do;
car a la maladie qui est sanee par cautere n’a point de revenue;	for the disease cured by cautery does not recur;
et il le dient ensi;	and they say it like this;
mais il n’est mie si com il cuident, por ce que cauteres nen est que medicine qui mue la complexion, et seche les humors que sont cause de la dolor, et vaut mues que medicine por le hastement de sa valor, et por la vertut de son oevre et de sa signorie.	but it is not as they think, for cautery is only a medicine that changes the complexion, dries out the fluids that cause pain, and is worth more than medicine for the swiftness of its effect, and by virtue of its work and its power.
Et possans chose est que li maladie viegne aucune fois selonc la complexion dou malaide et lou leu de la maladie et sa vertut;	And it is possible that disease comes in any way depending on the nature of the patient's illness and its strength;
et sont assemblees en lui les superfluitez par l’aquisition des viandes et des semblans choses, se ce n’est cauteres administrez em leu ou il ait poc de superfluitez et de moistor, si com cauteres de dens por la dolor, et les semblans choses, et teil dolor ne revient mie;	And they gather in him the excesses through the consumption of meats and similar things; if this is not done with cauterization where there is little excess and moisture, such as dense cauterizations for pain, and similar things, so that the pain does not return;
mais ce avient poc.	But this happens little.
Et mout de gens n’entendent mie por coi cauteres est apelez li derriens de medecine, et c’est voir;	And few people understand why cauterizations are called after medicine, and it's to see;
mais il ne croient mie que cauteres vaille aprés medicine, mais lor ententions est fause, et est cauteres li derriens de medicine por ceu que quant nos aministrons manieres de cures en aucune maladie et elles ne valent, adonc administrons nos le cautere, et il vaut.	But they do not believe that cauterizations are after medicine; their understanding is false. Cauterizations are considered after medicine because when our methods of treatments in any disease don't work, then we administer the cauterization, and it does work.
Adonques apert bien que cauteres est li derriens de medicine, ne mie selonc l’entention des folz mires.	Therefore, it is correctly understood that cauterization belongs to the later stages of medicine, not according to the understanding of those who misunderstand.
Li ancien dirent que cauteres d’estrument d’or est muedres que de fer, et ne dirent ceu fuers que por la qualiteit de l’or et por la hautece de sa substance;	The old ones said that cauterizers made of gold utensils are more effective than those made of iron, and they stated this due to the quality of gold and its highness in terms of substance.
et dirent que li leus de cautere ne fait mie porriture, mais ceu n’est mie voir car je l’ai esprovei, et ai troveit que c’est voir en aucuns homes;	and they say that the edges of the cauterizer do not cause putrefaction, but it is not visible because I have proven it and found out that it can be visible in some people;
et cauteres d’or vaut mues que de fer, si com il lou dirent.	And gold cauterizers are better than iron ones, as they said.
Et toutevoie quant tu chaufes estrument d’or, tu ne seis mie quant il est chaus par la color de l’or, et s’est tantost refroidiez;	And still, when you heat gold utensils, you do not know when they are heated by the color of the gold, and it is suddenly cooled;
et s’on le chaufe trop;	and if it is overheated;
si font au feu;	if they use the fire;
et ensi i a assez d’empechement.	And thus there is enough hindrance.
Et por ce usons nos de cautere de feir que nos l’avons mues apparilliet a nostre oevre.	And because we use our metal cautery that has been adapted to our work.
Or vos ai ordeneit cest chapitre des lou chief jusc’a piez, por ceu que li voie soit plus legiere a trover.	So I have organized this chapter on the shoulder until this point, so that finding it may be easier.
dou cautere olivaire	The olive cautery
Cist cauteres vaut a moistor et a froidor sus lou cerveil, et en i a dous c’on fait par la cause d’une maladie qui est apelee «soda», et par la cause de maintes humors qui dessendent dou chief as eulz, et as oreilles, et por multitude de songes et dolor de dens et dolor de gorge, et meismement a toutes maladies qui vienent de froidor si com paralisie et sode et apoplexie et semblans maladies.	A fire cautery is suitable for moisture and coldness on the head. There are two kinds that we do this due to the cause of an illness called 'soda', and because of many fluids that descend from the body like sweat, and from ears, and through a multitude of dreams and toothache and sore throat, and also towards all diseases that come from cold such as paralysis, soda poisoning and apoplexy, and similar illnesses.
Li forme de cest cautere si est que li malaides soit espurgiez par medicine solutive mondifiant le chief III nuis ou IIII, selonc ceu que li vertus et li eaige et li acostumance dou malaide le puet soffrir;	The form of this cautery is such that the patients should be purified by a dissolving medicine, modifying it every third or fourth day according to what the properties and the strength and the habituation of the patient can bear;
et puis fai rere lou chief dou malaide.	and then resume applying the medicine to the patient's wound.
Et puis le fai seoir croisiet entre tes mains, et mettre ses mains sor som peis;	And then have him sit cross-legged between your hands, and place his hands on some hot stones;
aprés met la racine de ta palme sus la racine de son neis entre ses II eulz;	after placing the root of your palm on the root of his nose between his second eyelids;
et lai ou venra tes dois moiens, si saigne d’enche puis eschaufe le cautere qui est apelé «olivare», de coi ci est li forme:	and leave it where your two thumbs come to rest; if there is bleeding, apply heat from the fire cautery called "olivare", which has this form:
Et le met sor le leu signiet d’encre, et fai en dessendant et en estraignant ta main poc et poc en trestornant;	And mark its place with ink on the left side, and apply it as you descend and steadily hold your hand a little at a time while turning.
puis lieve ta main isnelement, et rewarde le leu se tu vois l’os I sol petit;	Then ease your hand slightly, and reward the left side if you see a small bone sink into it;
et se tu ne lou vois, si rencomence le cautere tant que tu voies l’os si com je lou t’ai dit;	And if you don't see it, resume the cautery until you see the bone as I have told you;
aprés pren I poc de seil, et met en awe et molle coton dedens, et met sor le leu, et li laisse III jors;	After taking some silk, and place wet and soft cotton inside, apply it to the left side, and leave it for three days;
aprés met sus cotun moilliet en burre;	After put on butter-soaked cloth;
et laisse sus tant que li eschaudure soit ostee;	and leave it until the scab is removed;
aprés cure la plaie de l’oignement qui est apelez «tetrafarmaçon», tant qu’il soit sanez.	After treat the wound with ointment called 'tetrafarmac', until it heals normally.
Et se dirent li ancien, que quant plus demoure overte li plaie, plus s’espurge;	And if the old men said, that when a wound stays open longer, it discharges more;
et por ce si aide mues.	and because of this, they move in such a way.
Et dirent aucun de ces que on doit tant lassier le cautere que partie de l’os soit arse, et puis rese on ceu qui est ars de l’os, et soit curez.	And it was said by some that one should let the cautery burn until part of the bone is burned, and then remove what has been burned from the bone and treat it.
Et dient li autre c’on doit le cautere tant lassier sus, et bouter si fort c’on abaite de l’os ausi large comme I vertoil que les femmes mettent en lor fusez por ceu que les humors issent mues hors;	And the other says that we should apply the cautery there and press so strongly against it as to match the width of a woman's belly button when she is pregnant, because fluids escape when this happens.
et doit on lassier la plaie longement overte;	And should we leave the wound open for an extended period;
aprés le doit on curer et sodeir.	Afterwards, should one clean and stitch it up.
Et ces II manieres de cauteres ne me semblent mie estre bones dou tout en tout, fuers qu’en aucuns homes ou il ait voie de paor;	And these two ways of using cauterization do not seem to be entirely good for everyone, except in cases where there is the risk of fear;
et mues me semble que je lou doie laissier;	It seems to me that I should leave it alone;
car li chiés li est afoiblis par les solutions continuees de nature, si com nos le tesmoignons ens autres membres;	For the shoulder is weakened by continuous exposure to nature's elements, as we have witnessed in other limbs.
et meisme quant li chiés dou malaide est foibles par nature, et li premiere semblance de cautere est plus salve et muedre por moi, et de celi use je oevre en donques emsamble salut.	And likewise when the shoulder muscles are weak by nature, and the first sign of cauterization is more healed and smoother for me, and using this method I perform my work thus gathering together healing.
de l’anciainne dolor dou chief	of the old pain in the head
Quant en tout le chief vient dolor croniques, et dure longement, si doit user li malaides yeris et pilules qui sont apelees «cochie», et d’espurgement de chief et d’oiles et d’emplastres;	When chronic pain in the head comes about and lasts for a long time, then one must use the head's remedies and pills that are called "couchies", and treatments for clearing the head and ears and bandages;
et s’on li fait le cautere que nos avons devant dit, et il ne vaut.	and if one performs the cauterization as we have previously said, and it proves effective.
Pren warde se li chiés dou malade est de fort nature, et qu’il ne soit trop froit;	Take heed that if the shoulder of the sick person is very frail, and do not let it become too cold;
adonques le cauterize desoz celui cautere un poc que nos avons dit desus.	Then apply heat from this fire cautery a little as we have said above.
Aprés fai cautere sus chescune corne dou chief jusc’a l’os, si com devant avons dit, et fai I cautere ou leu qui est apelez «vasselz»;	After you apply the heat to each horn up to the bone, as we said before, and apply heat at the part of the head called "wattles".
et est I leus en coi on met ventouses;	and place it in the area where suction cups are applied;
et alige ta main si que tu ne voises mie jusc’a l’os:	and move your hand gently so that you do not see up to the bone:
li malaides sent trop plus grant dolor en cest cautere que as autres, et je em parlerai aillors;	The patient feels much more intense pain in this heat treatment than in others, and I will speak of it elsewhere;
et covient que li cauteres des cornes soient plus subtis que cil dont on cautere la moieneteit dou chief, et c’est li forme:	It is necessary that the heatings of the horns be more subtle than that used to heat half the head, and this is its form:
dou cautere dou chief	For the fire cautery,
Quant en une partie dou chief vient dolor sodaine, et est estendue li maladie jusc’a l’oil, et li chiés est espurgiez par medicines mondifians, et on a fait les autres cures que j’ai dit en la division des maladies, et tout ceu ne profite mie:	If pain suddenly occurs in part of the head and extends the illness to the eye, and the head is treated with purifying medicines, and other treatments are done as I said in the section on illnesses, but none of this helps:
adonques li fai cauteres selonc II manieres, c’est a savoir de medicine ague et de feir.	Therefore, apply cautery according to two methods, namely that of cold medicine and fire.
Li cauteres de medicine ague si est que tu preignes une doce d’alz, et oste l’escorce et le recope I poc as II chiés, et puis fent la temple ou li dolor tient en teil maniere que tu puisses reponre la doce d’alz desoz le cuir;	Apply the fire cautery if you take a handful of herbs and peel and coat them once or twice on each shoulder. Then make a cut where the pain holds in such manner that you can place the herb mixture directly under the skin;
et quant elle sera reponuee si le lie et l’estraint bien et le laisse ensi XII houres;	and when it is placed, if it is held well and left like this for twelve hours;
et puis le deslie et trait fuers la doce d’ail, et laisse la plaie ensi II jors ou III;	then release the hold and remove the garlic mixture, and leave the wound like this for two days or three;
puis met sus cotun plongiet en burre tant que porreture en isse.	Then place a cotton wad soaked in butter until the pain eases.
Aprés le cure d’oignement tant qu’il soit sanez;	After the ointment treatment as long as it is effective;
et se tu vues si fai ceu d’aucunes medicines comburans que j’ai escrites ou dozime traitier des medicines comburans.	And if you see it fitting to use some of these burning medicines that I have written about or the tenth treatise on burning medicines.
Li cautere de fer si est selonc ceste meniere.	The iron cautery works like this.
Chaufe le cautere de coi ci est li forme:	Heat the cautery as shown here:
Et est apelez «clos» por ceu que li chief est fait a la forme d’un clo ou il ait I poc de corbeure, et em mileu a une petite apparance;	And is called "bowed" because the head has the shape of an ogee arch, having a slight curve at the top and appearing small in the middle.
et le met sor le leu dolorous, et tien ta main et trestorne le feir un poc legierement, tant que li moitiez de l’espés dou keur soit arse;	and place it in the painful area, hold your hand and gently twist the iron until half of the thickness of the ear is burnt;
et lieve ta main que li artere n’arde, que est defuers, et decorre habundance de sanc.	and lift your hand so that the artery doesn't burn, it's exposed, and a large amount of blood flows out.
Aprés met coton en awe de seil, et met sor le leu par III jors;	After that, put cotton in salt water, and place it on the wound for three days;
puis i met coton moilliet em burre, et puis cure le leu d’oignement tant qu’il soit sanez;	then put wet cotton in butter, and then treat the wound with ointment until it heals;
et se tu vuelz cauterize ceste emigraine avec le cautere qui est apelez «cultellare», a tout la pointe, et te garde de coper l’artere en ceste emigraine qui n’est mie anciaine.	And if you wish to cauterize this head wound with the cautery that is called "cultellare", across its entirety, and beware not to cover the artery in this head wound which isn't old.
de emigraine	From headache
Quant tu cures emigraine si com nos avons devant dit en divisions des maladies, et ne profite mie, et vois que li cauteres devant dis de la medicine et dou fer ne li soffit mie, adonques covient il que tu eschaufes le cautere qui est apelez «cultellare» tant qu’il soit blans;	When you treat a head wound as we have described in the divisions of diseases, if it does not heal and you observe that the cauterizations mentioned previously in medicine do not suffice, then it is necessary for you to heat the cautery which is called "cultellare" until it is white;
et seigne ainsois sor le leu doillant une ligne de demi doi de lonc, et oste ta main une fois, et l’estrain que tu ne coper l’artere et que ne viegnes jusc’a l’os;	And thus, while holding the length of half a diem in your hand, and having your fingers poised once, pull it out until you do not cover the artery and stop right up to the bone;
et te warde de la mandibule que muet quant on menjut, et li ners n’ait regart que la muet et que spasmus ne veigne a malaide, et te warde de decorrement de sanc de l’artere quant elle sera copee, ou copement ait grant paour et meismement a celui que ne s’i conoit, et qui n’est estudians et esprovez;	And beware of the mandible that closes when you bite, and let only the jaw move and no spasms affect the patient, and be cautious about blood discharge from the artery when it is cut, or if cutting causes great fear and even to those who do not understand, and who are neither studied nor experienced;
et laisse l’uevre em mi voie;	and let the work come in my way;
mais je vos dirai coment on restainche sanc quant li artere est copee, et je vos mostrerai a leu ou il afiert en cest livre.	but I will tell you how to staunch blood when an artery has been cut, and I will show you where it is explained in this book.
Et se tu vois que cist cauteres ne soffise mie a la maladie, et li malaides est soffrans, cauterize le enmi le chief ausi com nos avons dit, et cure la plaie tant qu’elle soit sanee;	And if you see that this cautery does not work against the disease, and the patient is suffering, apply the fire to within the head as we have said, and treat the wound until it heals;
et se tu vues, aministre le cautere que nos avons dit ou chapistre de l’estraction de l’artere, avec le cautere qui ait II coutelz;	And if you see this, administer the cautery that we have said or from the chapter on extraction of the artery, with the cautery that has two knives;
et est cist cauteres millors de celui et plus aidans.	And these cauteries are better than others and more beneficial.
de la dolor des oreilles de part froidor	From the pain of the ears from coldness
Quant en l’oreille vient dolor de froit, et on i a ovreit de medicines solutives et des autres cures que nos avons dit en la division, et li dolors ne se muet, adonques eschaufe cest cautere qui est apelez «poins», de coi ci est li forme:	When pain in the ear comes from cold, and one has applied solutions of medicines and other treatments that we have mentioned under division, and if the pains do not subside, then heat this cautery which is called "points", as follows:
Aprés pointoie tout entor l’oreille malaide, ou entor les II se la dolor tient en ambedous, et t’esloigne un poc ensus de la racine de l’oreille puis que tu as signiet le leu d’enche;	After this, point everything around the patient's ear, or in both places where pain is felt, and move away slightly from the root of the ear after marking its line;
et ait X poins entor chescune oreille;	And has ten points within each ear;
aprés cure le leu tant qu’il soit sanez.	after treatment until it becomes clean.
de la torture de la bouche	From the pain in the mouth
Torture qui doit estre curee par cautere nen est fuers que de celles que muevent de fleume, si com nos avons dit en divisions des maladie;	The torture that must be treated with cauterization only leaves those that move from blood, as we have said in the divisions of diseases;
et ne faire point de cautere as semblances que vienent de sechor et de spame de ners.	and do not use cauterization on appearances that come from scarring and inflammation of nerves.
Quant tu cures ceste semblance de torture qui muet de fleume d’ydres et d’espurgemens de chief et de gargarisme, et ceu ne vaut, adonc covient que tu cauterizes le malaide de III cauteres:	When you treat this type of torture that comes from blood in urine and purges of the head and gargling, if it doesn't respond, then it is necessary for you to cauterize the patient with three applications.
l’une en la racine de l’oreille, et l’autre un poc defuers la temple, et le tier en l’ajostement des II levres;	The first one at the root of the ear, and the second slightly beyond the temple, and the third at the adjustment between the two lips;
et met le cautere en la partie qui apert saine, et li fai cautere endroit le chief de l’oreille desus un poc desoz la corne dou chief, et un autre en la temple ausi longe com uns poce;	And place the cautery at the healthy opening part, and apply the cautery to that spot over the tip of the ear a little below the head's horn, and another one on the temple as long as a hand.
et laisse le cautere tant sus que li moitiez dou keur soit arse;	And let the cautery remain there until half of the cheek is burnt;
et c’est li forme dou cautere:	And that is how it looks like using the cautery:
Et est li semblance dou cutellaire que nos avons mise devant, mais il est un poc plus subtilz et covient que li coutelz soit un poc plus gros;	And it is similar to the knife operation we showed before, but it's a bit more subtle. It requires that the knives be slightly larger;
aprés cure lou leu si com j’ai devant dit, tant qu’il soit sanez.	After the treatment of the wound as I explained before, until it is sound.
Quant apoplexie est ancieinne et tu la cures ensi com nos avons dit, et il ne profite mie, et li malaides n’ait fievre, adonques li fai IIII cauteres:	When the apoplexy is old and you treat it as we have said, and if it does not benefit, and if the patient has fever, then make four cauterizations.
II sus les II cornes dou chief, et I emmi le chief, et I ou leu qui est apelez «vasselz» si com nos avons devant dit, et lou derrien cautere sus la bouche de l’estomac;	On the second horns of the head, and I touch the top of the head, and I move to where the neck is called 'wattles' as we have previously mentioned, and on the back cautery at the mouth of the stomach;
et soit curez si com nos avons dit devant.	and so treat it in the way we have said before.
de litargie	from liturgy
A cest maladie covient doner au malaide yeres grans et pilules mondifians le cerveil;	For this illness, one should give the patient large grains and round pills to improve their brain function;
aprés reis lou chief dou malaide tout, et li met sus l’occipite l’emplaustre de sinapi qui est escrit ou traitier des emplastres;	After the head of the patient is well rested, and one places the sinapical plaster on the occipital part, as written or prescribed in the treatment for plasters;
et c’est li maniere dou cautere:	and this is how the cautery works:
si lou fai si com j’ai dit.	if you do it as I have said.
S’il est sanez ensi, boin est;	If he is healthy like this, it is well;
et s’il ne l’est, se li fai III cauteres des emmi le chief en dessendant jusc’a col, et ait d’espaice entre chescun cautere I doi de gros;	And if it isn't done, you should make three burns below the neck down to the collarbone, and leave an interval of one digit's width between each burn.
et le cure si com les autres, et se tu i vues ajoster, et li malaides est soffrans, se li fai I cautere en mileu;	And the treatment is like with the others, and if you find it fitting, and the patient is suffering, then you should make one burn in the middle.
et se mestiers est, II autres sus les II cornes, et le cure tant qu’il soit sanez;	And if there's need for it, two more burns on the two horns, and treat until it is clean;
et soit li cauteres qui est apelez «olivare», si com j’ai devant dit.	And so, let the cauterizations known as 'olive' be as I have described before.
de la froidor dou chief	from coldness of the head
Il covient que li chief soit mundifiez de yeres et de ceu que nos avons devant dit;	It is necessary that the head be cleaned of old blemishes and what we have discussed beforehand;
aprés reis le chief dou malaide, puis li fai cautere emmi le chief et sus chescune corne, et I derrier et III sus l’espinee dou col;	After cleaning the head of the patient, then make burns below the head and on each horn, and one behind and three near the spine at the neck.
et se tu en as plus mestier, et li cors est moiste et li malaides est soffrans, et li maladie est fors, se li fai IIII cauteres sus l’espinee dou dos;	And if you need more skill, and the body is moist and the patient suffers, and the disease is present, make four fire cauteries on the spine of the back;
et li laisse tant que li plus dou keur soit ars, et lieve ta main;	And let it until the very softest wound heals, and lift your hand;
aprés le cure tant qu’il soit sanez, et soit li cauteres qui est apelez «olivare» que nos avons devant dit.	After the treatment until it is clean, and apply the cautery which is called "olivare" as we have previously mentioned.
de l’epilempsie	From epilepsy
Li epilentiques ne doit useir de cautere fuers que cil qui est fleumatique, et covient premier mondifier le cerveil de yeres et d’autres cures que nos avons dites en la division quant li malaides est grans et soffrans de penre medicine.	The epileptics should only use a cautery for those who are phlegmatic, and first modify the brain with years and other remedies that we have mentioned in the section when the patient is large and suffering from physical medicine.
Et se c’est uns enfes qui ne lou puisse soffrir, se li fai gargarisme et mastication mondifiant le cerveil sovent avec bones viandes;	And if it's a child who cannot bear the pain, give gargling and chewing with many good meats often to the brain;
aprés li reis lou chief em mileu, et i fai I cautere selonc ce que nos avons dit devant, et I cautere sus lou vassel, et sus chescune corne;	After the king of the head in the middle, and I make a fire treatment according to what we have said before, and one fire treatment on the vessel, and on each horn;
et se li malaides est fors et soffrans, se li fai cauteres si com j’ai dit a celui qui ait paralisie et mollification de cors, sus l’espinee dou dos et dou col, et soit li cauteres olivier selonc la maniere que j’ai dit.	And if the limbs are outside and suffering, you should apply cauterization as I have described for those with paralysis and muscular atrophy, on the spine across the back and neck area. You should perform an olive oil-based cautery according to the method that I explained.
Se li malaides est enfes, se li fai .i. cautere subtil selonc ceste maniere:	If the patient is an infant, then you should perform one subtle cautery in this manner:
Quant par la cause de melancolie sunt les superfluitez ou les moistors corrumpues et fleume grosse, adonques lou cauterize de teils cauteres com nos avons dit a celui qui ait paralisie.	When due to the cause of melancholy are excesses or fluids corrupted and full of pus, then the part cautery of the fire cautery as we have said to those who have paralysis.
Et se par la cause de melancolie est li superfluitez declinans a melancolie, et est li cors dou malaide moistes, adonc li done a boivre chose par coi li cervelz soit mundifiez, selonc ceu qu’il est devant en la division.	And if due to the cause of melancholy is the excess descending into melancholy, and the parts are moist with malaise, then this should be drunk so that the brain may be purified, as was discussed in the previous section.
Aprés reis lou chief dou malaide;	After you have examined the head of the bone;
aprés fai I torteil de lin bien fait, ausi com I cercle, si le met emmi le chief;	After that, make a linen thread well done, like a circle, and place it around the head.
et li malaides sié croisiez, et soit bien tenus de toutes pars;	And when the limbs have settled, ensure they are firmly held in all directions;
aprés presente le linement, et vaut mues de burre de berbis ancien;	After applying the liniment, and apply a paste of old bee's wax;
et lou chaufe a feu tempreement, si que li dois s’on li boute le puisse soffrir;	And heat it gently over the fire, so that it can be applied without causing pain or discomfort;
aprés vuide le cercle par dedens emmi le chief, et lou laisse refroidier;	After emptying out the space inside through the mouth, and letting it cool down.
et fai ce a malaide chescune semaine une fois avec autre governement boin, tant qu’il soit sanez.	And do this to the patient once every week with different types of governance until it is cleansed.
Ou se tu vues cauterize lou en faisant poins plusors a tot le cautere.	Or, if you see that it is being cauterized by making marks on the entire surface of the cautery.
Ceste maniere de cautere amoistit le cerveil igaument;	This way of cautering moistens the brain more;
et puis met sus coton moilliet en burre et en graisse de geline.	Then place on it wet cotton in butter and animal fat.
de l’awe des eulz	of the eyes
Quant awe vient premierement as eulz par les signes que j’ai dit en la division, adonques encomence et done boivre au malaide chose mundifiant le chief, et le warde de toutes moistors, et lou fai suer ou bain plusors fois a jeun.	When the onset comes to the eyes first through the symptoms I have mentioned in the division, then start and continue making the patient drink things that purify the head, and keep him/her away from all moisture, and make them sweat or take baths several times on an empty stomach.
Aprés li comande a rere son chief, et li fai cautere emmi le chief, et li fai II cauteres sus les II temples se li dessendemens de l’awe est as II eulz ensamble, ou en I se li dessendemens est en I;	After that, he commands it to rest on its head, and he applies the cautery through the head, and applies two cauterizations on the two temples where the descent of the arrow is at both eyes together, or in one it descends in one.
et cope a tout le cautere toutes les voines et les arteres que sont desoz le keur, et soient li cautere lonc selon lou large de la temple;	And apply the entire cautery to all the veins and arteries that are around the knee, and make sure to cauterize them long according to the width of the temples;
et te warde de decorrement de sanc, et se tu vois trop de sanc issir, si li estainche de teil pooir com tu as.	And beware of bleeding out, and if you see too much blood coming out, stop it by pressing with a piece of cloth as you can.
Et je t’enseignerai en l’estraction des arteres et a l’incision la cautele coment tu l’estencheras;	And I will teach you about the extraction of arteries and incisions in the cautery, how to extinguish it;
et aucune fois fait on cautere ou hatereil desoz les II os derrier.	And never apply the cautery or heat over the two inner bones.
dou cors des larmes	of the tears' two courses
Quant les larmes des eulz sont ancienes et acostumees et sont sus les voines, ou delez les arteres que sont en l’aparance dou chief defors;	When the tears of the eyes have been long and accustomed, and are above the veins, or overlie arteries that appear under the head's surface;
et on voit que c’est des superfluitez froides fleumatiques, adonques li fai le cautere que j’ai dit en l’encomencement de l’awe dessendant as eulz:	And it is seen that these are cold phlegmatic excesses, then do the cautery which I have said at the beginning of this work when descending to the eyes:
I cautere emmi le chief, et II cauteres sus les II temples, et II cauteres ou haiterel desoz les II os;	I apply the cautery to the head, and two cauteries on the two temples, and two cauterizations over the two inner bones;
et s’il i a besoigne plus, si le cauterize saigement desus le sorcil a tout I petit cautere.	And if there is need for more, cauterize carefully above the eyebrow with every small cautery.
dou cors des larmes par dedens les eulz	of the tears within the eyes
Quant tu le medicines selonc ceu que nos avons dit en la division, et il ne profite mie, adonques done a boivre a malaide III nuis cochies;	When you administer the medicine according to what we have said in the division, and it does not benefit, then give the patient three oxen' intestines to drink;
aprés li reis le chief, et li fai cautere ou mileu dou cautere olivaire;	After the king's head, and I make him cauterized with or in the middle of an olive oil cautery;
et fai II cauteres dou cautere qui est apelez «clavilis» sus les II sorcis, un poc desoz les chevous;	and do two cauterizations with the cautery called 'claw' on both eyebrows, a little below the hair.
et te warde de l’artere que tu ne la coper.	and beware not to cover the artery as you work.
Et c’est li forme dou cautere qui est apelez «clavilis»:	And this is the shape of the cautery which is called "claw".
Quant li papiere de l’oil est mollifie de maladie et de moistor, adonques la cautarize de cest cautere qui est apelez «olivare».	When the paper treated with oil becomes diseased and moist, then cauterize it with this iron known as "olive".
de coi ci est li forme:	of which here is its form:
Et se tu vues si fai II cauteres sus les II sorcis ausi lons com li sorcilz sont;	And if you see that you do two cauterizations on both eyebrows as long as the eyebrows are.
et n’i lassiez mie la main fors que tant que li tierce partie de la papiere soit arse, selonc la maniere que j’ai dit.	And do not let your hand rest until a third part of the paper is burned, according to the method I have described.
dou poil qui point l’oil	The hair which pricks the eye
Aucune fois avient que li poil des oilz sont convertit au pardedens, et poignent l’oil, et i fait on cauteres selonc II manieres:	No instance has occurred where the hair of the nose turns into the paranasal region and enters the nose; in such cases, one performs cauteries according to two methods:
c’est a savoir de feu, ou de medicine ardant.	This means that it involves using fire or burning medicine.
Ou cautere de feu comande au malaide qu’il laisse les poilz tant qu’il soient lons et igals;	With the fire cautery, instruct the patient to allow the hairs to grow until they are long and uniform;
et s’il le poignent a lor nassance, se li estraint les eulz qu’il ne se muevent tant qu’il naissent.	And if they prick at their base, hold the eyes steady so that they do not move until they are born.
Quant il naissent et i sont igalz, adonques met le malaide en ton sain;	When they are born and if they are uniform, then put the patient in their healthy position;
aprés seigne sus la papiere des eulz une figure que soit ausi com li fuelle dou mirte, et soit li comencemens dou signe delez les poilz;	After on Sir upon the parchment of the eyes make a symbol that is as such like the leaf of myrtle, and let it be the beginning of the sign opposite the hairs;
puis i met coton moilliet en glaire d’uef et muscillaige de persillion sus l’oil, puis eschaufe le cautere de coi ci est li forme:	Then place moist cotton soaked in egg yolk and garlic paste on the eye, then apply the fire cautery tool as shown here.
Aprés cauterize sus la figure que tu as signiet poc et poc mout de fois, que li keurs soit ars lai endroit;	After that, gently and gradually apply the cautery to the symbol you have made, until the marks are burnt in that spot;
et li signes de la santeit de l’uevre est que tu voies la papiere retraite, et les poilz levez a la pointure de l’oil;	And the signs of health in the operation are that you see the paper retracting, and the hairs lifted to the edge of the eye.
adonques lieve ta main, et laisse ensi III jors, puis i met coton moilliet en burre tant que li eschaudure soit ostee;	Then lift your hand and leave it like this for three days, then apply moist cotton with butter until the scab is removed;
aprés le cure d’oignement tant qu’il soit sanez.	After the application of ointment until it is properly absorbed.
Et se aprés ceu vienent li poilz, et li papiere est mollifie adonques rencomence le cautere sus cel leu meisme, si com tu as fait premiers;	And when these have come about, and the skin has softened, then resume the cauterization on that same area, just as you did at first.
et se li poil sont defuer, si le cauterize tant que li papiere soit levee a son leu natureil, et soit igals, et ne poignent mie li poil l’oil.	And when the hair is burnt off, then cauterize until the skin rises to its natural position and remains even, not allowing the hair to touch the eye.
Li cauteres de medicine ardant est que tu comandes au malaide qu’il laisse les poilz tant qu’il soient grans et igalz, puis fai de parchemin la forme de la foille de mirte;	The fire cauterizing of medicine is that you instruct the patient to let the hairs grow until they are large and even, then make of parchment the shape of the bay leaf;
puis pren de savon fransois et de vive chalz, de chescun une .З., et broie ensamble bien;	Then take French soap and fresh lime leaves, each one spoonful, and grind them together thoroughly;
et le fai hastanment, si qu’il ne refroide, puis en espant sus la forme que tu es fait sicom la foille dou mirte, et met sus la papiere des eulz;	And make haste, so that it does not cool, then blow upon the shape you have made like a leaf of myrtle, and place the eyes on paper.
et se li maladie tient en I oil soulement, si doit on ovrer en I, et se en ambedous ausi;	And if the illness lasts only in one part of the body, you should open it there; and if it is present equally in both.
et met desoz l’oil coton moilliet en abin d’uef;	And put some damp cotton over the eye like an egg.
et li chiés dou malaide soit en ton sain et met ton doi mostrant sus la medicine, et presse I poc et lou muef toutes les fois que li malaide sent mordication de la medicine, car il sent mordication ausi com de feu.	And have the body of the illness on your healthy side and place your hand showing on the medicine, and press the paste with every application when the illness feels the medicine's bite; for it feels the bite also like fire.
Quant tu as ceu fait longement, si oste la medicine a ton doit.	When this has been done for some time, once you have exposed the medicine to your finger.
Et quant li mordication sera passee, si leve le leu d’awe, et rewarde se tu vois la papiere levee ausi com s’ele estoit levee par constraignement de feu ou par incision;	And when the bite has passed, lift the part away and reward if you see the paper lifted also as it would be by constraint of fire or by incision;
et s’il est ensi, si est bien.	And if it's like this, then do so well.
Se ceu non, si remet encor de la medicine sus lou leu ou li medicine n’ait ovreit, tant que tes ovraiges soit igalz, et tes eulz mis a point;	And if not, try again with medicine at the shoulder or until the medicine has worked, as long as your actions are equal, and your eyes focused;
puis met sus coton moilliet en burre tant que li keurs ars soit cheus, aprés cure le leu de l’oignement qui est apelez «dyafenis» et d’autre, tant qu’il soit sanez.	Then place wet cotton and butter until the ears are covered with wax, after treating the shoulder with ointments known as 'dyafenis' and others, until it is clean.
Et se t’est mestier que tu te warde bien a ton ovraige par grant warde qu’il ne chiece point de la medicine as eulz.	And if it requires that you take good care of your work by great caution so that no medicine leaks into the eyes.
Et se li papiere devient mole aprés, et li poil poignent en l’oil, si recomence la medicine sus celui leu qui est mollifiez de la papiere proprement, ensi com tu as fait devant;	And if the paper becomes moist and the hair sticks in the eye, then apply medicine to that shoulder which is softened by clean paper properly, just as you did before.
aprés le cure tant qu’il soit sanez;	After treating it until it is clean;
et c’est li forme de la fuelle dou mirte:	and this is the shape of the leaf of the wormwood:
Et saichés que li eul des homes sont divers en grandor et en petitece, et selonc ceu soit tes constraignemens;	And know that eyes of men vary greatly in size and smallness, and according to this be your constraints;
et ne soit mie reponue li droite voie a celui cui est li estude de cest art.	And do not have the right way respond to him who studies this craft.
de la cure de fistule par cautere	regarding the treatment of fistula with a cautery
Quant tu cures fistule si com nos avons dit en divisions des maladies, et tes cures ne profitent mie, adonques covient il que tu li fais cautere selonc ceste maniere.	When you treat a fistula as we have said in the divisions of diseases, and your treatments are not beneficial, then it is necessary for you to apply cautery according to this manner.
Comande au malaide qu’il mette son chief en ton sain;	Instruct the patient to place his head in your well-being;
et teigne li menistres son chief entre tes mains en teil maniere qu’il ne se mueve, ne ne demoinne son chief;	And guide the ministers so that his head is between your hands in such a way that it does not move or slide from his head;
aprés met coton moilliet en abin d’uef ou en jus de persillion sus l’oil;	after put wadded cotton in the shape of an egg or garlic juice on the eye;
aprés chaufe le cautere qui est teilz:	after heat the cautery which is heated:
et est chevez au chief si com li forme d’une penne de vouteul, ensamble la queil soit li cautere;	and place it over the head as if it were a feather of a sparrow, so that when you have the cautery;
se tu vues, si soit apointé des l’un chief dusc’a l’autre, et se tu vues, si soit ausi com une tente;	If you observe, it might look pointed from one end to the other, and if you see, it may also appear like a tent.
mais toutevoie, cist qui est chevez vaut mues por ton ovraige.	However, this is what happens in your work due to the nature of things.
Aprés presse la fistule s’ele est overte, et en trai la porriture, et la seche;	After pressing, if the fistula is opened, you treat the putrefaction and dry it out.
et s’ele est close, si la oevre, et trai fuers la bowe;	And if it's closed, let it heal naturally, and remove from the body;
aprés met sus le cautere chaut forment, et tien ta main au cautere a la partie dou neif ensus de l’oil, que ta mains ne faice folie;	After placing the fire cautery in position, hold your hand on the cautery at the part below the nose above the eye, so that your hand doesn't make a mistake.
et met le cautere en la graisse de l’oil, et la corromp.	And place the cautery in the oil's grease and it will burn.
Se tu viens au comencement dou cautere jusc’a l’os, si serait bien.	If you come to the beginning of the cautery up to the bone, it would be well.
Se ceu non, si rencomence le cautere encor une fois, et autre se tu en as mestier, et le laisse III jors;	If not, then apply the fire cautery once more, and if necessary, do so again, letting it be for three days.
aprés i met sus coton moilliet en burre, et lou cure de l’oignement desiccatif tant qu’il soit sanez, et se XL jors passent qu’il ne soit sanez, si met sus medicine ague corrosive tant que li os soit descovers;	After placing damp cotton and butter on it, apply the ointment dressing until it heals. et lou reis selonc ceu que il venrait en son chapistre.	And let the ruler follow as it comes in his chapter.
Et i a une maniere de cautere de fistule que aucun des anciens dirent.	And there is a method for cauterizing fistulas that none of the old ones mentioned.
Entens a fistule, et fens le leu;	Understand about fistulas, and make the wound;
aprés met en la fendure I camahan subtil de coi ci est li forme:	After placing in the slit a slender stick with this shape:
et i font a la quantiteit d’une .З. de plonc;	and it should be as large as a thimble;
et tien ta main ou camahan fermement, et ne se mueve li malaides nes point, que li plons fondus ne corre a son oil;	And hold your hand or clench it firmly, and do not move the spots at all, that the wounds may heal properly.
et covient c’on mette sus l’oil a malaide coton moilliet en abin d’uefz ou en awe:	And it is proper to place on the eye a moistened cotton cloth in anticipation of pus or blood:
li plonc si art lou leu de fistule, et lou saine per mervillouse saniteit.	The pus flows from the place of the fistula, and the healthy one through marvellous healing.
Et se li fistule est sanee per le cautere que nos avons dit, c’est boin.	And if the fistula is healed by the cautery as we have said, it's good.
Se ce non, si covient aministrer pertus au neif, et ramener la fistule au cors dou neif selonc ceu qu’il covient en som propre leu.	If not, it is necessary to administer pertussis to the child and return the fistula to the body of the child according to what is proper in its own nature.
des crevaices en levres	of mouth ulcers
Mout de fois avienent crevaices en levres que sont apelees «poil», et meismement en levres des enfans.	Occasionally, mouth sores appear on the lips which are called "whiskers", and similarly on the lips of children.
Quant tu cures ces crevaices de ceu que nos avons dit en divisions, et li cure ne profite, adonques eschaufe .i. petit cautere cultellaire selonc ceste forme:	When you treat these mouth sores with the methods we've discussed in divisions, and if treatment doesn't help, then use a small surgical tool like this to gently burn them:
Et le met hastanment en celles crevaices tant qu’il viegne jusc’a font;	And place it quickly in those cuts until it becomes as full as possible;
aprés cure le leu de cerote tant qu’il soit sanez.	After the treatment of the waxed area, while it remains healthy.
de l’aposteme de la goule	from the phlegm in the throat
Quant apostume vient en la racine de la goule ou en l’uve, ou ou palais, ou as racines des dens, aprés fait porriture et ront et est enveillis et devient fistule;	When an abscess comes in the root of the throat or in the oyster, or in the palate, or at the roots of the teeth, after it has turned rotten and swollen and becomes inflamed and develops into a fistula;
et tu le cures si com nos avons dit en divisions, et il ne profite mie:	And you treat them as we have said in sections, and they do not benefit.
adonques covient il que tu aies I cautere selonc la quantiteit de la fistule;	Therefore, it is necessary for you to have the cautery according to the size of the fistula;
aprés le bote ou pertus de la fistule, et tien ta main tant que li fer chaus viegne au font de li, et ou derrien leu;	After the plug or obstruction of the fistula, and hold your hand until the metal reaches the bottom of it, and wherever else there is.

et s’il est curez ensi, c’est boin;	And if it is treated like this, it is good;

dou movement des dens	movement of the teeth
Quant les gencives sont mollifies par moistor et les dens muevent, et tu le cures per medicines et ceu ne vaut, adonc met le chief dou malaide en ton sain;	When the gums become softened by moisture and the teeth move, and you treat it with medicines but it doesn't work, then apply pressure to the head of the bone until it returns to its healthy state;
aprés eschaufe le cautere dont li forme venra ci aprés en teil maniere que tu mettes une cainne sor le dent;	After rubbing the cautery, in such manner that you place a stick over the tooth;
et met dedens le cautere chaut hastanment, et tien tant ta main que li malaides sente la chalor venant a la racine dou dent;	And place the heated cautery quickly inside, and hold your hand until the patient feels the heat reaching to the root of the tooth;
aprés lieve ta main et rencomence le cautere selonc ta volenteit;	After ease your hand and repeat the heating with the cautery according to your will;
aprés emplisse li malaides sa bouche d’awe salee, et la teigne une houre et raiche fuers.	After fill the patient's mouth with ashes, and let it stay for an hour and then remove it.
Et en teil maniere li dens qui estoit movans si est confermez, et li gencive mollifie restrainte, et li moistors corrumpue sechie.	And in this manner the moving tooth is repositioned, and the softened gum becomes restrained, and the moisture that was present dries up.
de la dolor des dens	from the pain of teeth
Quant dolor de dens vient por froidor, ou il i a froidor ou veir, et les cures de medicine ne valent, adonc i ait mestier de cautere selonc II manieres:	When toothache comes from cold or there is coldness or inflammation and medicines do not help, then it needs to be treated with the use of a cautery in two ways:
et cautere de burre et cautere de feu.	And the wax cautery and the fire cautery.
Cautere de burre si est telz que tu preignes burre de vaiche, et le bout en une cuillier de fer ou d’arain;	Wax cautery is such that you take butter from a cow, and the tip in a iron or spider's leg spoon;
aprés pren coton et envolope sus la pointe d’une tente, et la moille en burre bulit, et met sus le dent dolant hastanment et tien tant qu’il soit refroidiez;	Then take cotton and cover it on the tip of a tent, and soak butter with its moisture, then apply it to the aching tooth until it cools down;
et ensi fai sovent tant que sa vertus viegne a la racine de la dent, et se tu vues si moille laine et coton en burre froit, et met sus le dent doillant, et met sus I fer chaut tant que li feus viegne au chevement dou dent.	And thus do it often until the butter's power reaches to the tooth root. If you see moist wool and cotton after cooling butter, apply it to the aching tooth, and place hot iron on it until the heat of the fire spreads through the tooth.
Li cauteres ensamble feu si est telz que tu preignes uns cainne de fer ou d’arain, et soit grosse si que li feus ne viegne a la bouche dou malaide;	The fire cautery is such that you take a piece of iron or spider's leg, and make it big enough so that the heat does not come to the edge of the wound.
aprés chaufe le cautere, de coi li forme venra ci aprés, et le met sus le dent et tien ta main tant que li cauteres soit refroidiez;	After heating the cautery, from which its form will come afterwards, place it on your teeth and keep your hand there until the cautery has cooled.
fai ceu sovent, car li dolor sera ostee celui jor meisme ou l’endemain.	Do this often, because the pain will be reduced either on that day or the next day.
Et covient que li malaides emplisse sa bouche de boin burre en l’empressement de cel cautere, et puis le raiche fuer;	And it is necessary for the patient to fill their mouth with good butter in anticipation of that cautery, and then push it out.
et c’est li forme dou cautere:	and this is the form of the cautery:
Et fai cautere dou queil chief que tu voudras, et selonc ceu que tu as pooir;	And make a cautery according to what you want, and according to what you have the ability for;
et c’est li forme de la caine:	and this is the form of the cane:
des scrophules	regarding the treatment of scrophula
Quant les scrophules sont de fleume et de moistors froides, et ne sont obeissans a digestion par medicines, adonques eschaufe le cautere cheveit de coi ci aprés vient li forme, et ait II aovertures por les fumees a issir au cautere de l’autre partie;	When the scrophules are due to cold blood and moisture that do not respond to digestion with medicines, then heat the cautery as described below which will show its form, and make two openings for the vapors to escape from the other side of the cautery;
et met le cautere chaut sus l’apostume une fois, ou II se mestier est, tant qu’il viegne au font de l’apostume;	And place the cautery on the abscess once, or twice as required, until it reaches to the bottom of the abscess;
et se li apostume est petis si met cautere selonc la quantiteit de l’apostume, et le laisse ensi III jors;	And if the abscess is small, apply the cautery according to the size of the abscess, and leave it like that for three days;
et met sus coton moilliet em burre tant que li arsure soit ostee;	And place on cotton soaked in butter until the splinter is extracted.
aprés cure le leu d’oignemens et de tentes tant qu’il soit sanez.	After the wound has healed and the stitches have been removed, until it is completely healed.
Li forme de la cainne:	The form of the cane:
Quant les moistors vainquent sus les chenals dou pormon, et meismement quant ce vient de froide complexion, adonc covient que li malaides soit voidiez premiers par medicines solutives;	When the moisture invades the channels of the heart, and especially when it comes from a cold constitution, then it is necessary for the body to be cleansed initially with diuretic medicines;
aprés li fai cautere a la racine de la gorge, et te garde que tu ne venir mie jusc’a la gorge, et n’ardre dou keur mais c’un poc.	After applying the cautery at the base of the throat, and make sure not to touch up to the throat, but only apply it moderately.
Aprés li fai I autre cautere a la jointure dou col au chief de l’espinee, et soit li cauteres qui est apelez «clavile» de coi nos avons la forme devant;	After this, I perform another cauterization at the joint of the neck and head of the spine, and it is from these cauteries that we derive the term 'clavicle' which we describe in front;
et cure le leu si com nos avons devant dit tant qu’il soit sanez.	and treat the head as previously described until it is healed.
de la toust	In respect to cautery by fire, it commands the diseased person to allow hair growth until it becomes long and uniform; and if they prick at their origin, it holds the eyes steady so they do not move until they grow.
Quant tous et maladie de pormon sont de moistors froides, et li malaides nen ait fievre ne sechor, et est li maladie anciaine, se li fai .II cauteres sus la forcele en leus vuis;	When all illnesses of the stomach are due to cold moisture, and patients do not have fever or dryness, if it is an old disease, then you should perform two cauterizations on their kidneys through their urinary passages;
et I autre cautere emmi le pis entre II mameles;	and apply another cauterization between the buttocks, at the place of the anus.
et soit li cauteres qui est apelez «clavile» selonc la forme qui est devant dite.	And it is from these cauteries that we derive the term 'clavicle', according to the description provided earlier.
Et se tu vues, fai cautere en poignant a tot le cautere qui est apelez «poins» de coi li forme est ci devant en la maladie des oreilles;	And if you see fit, perform cauterization by pressing on the entire area called 'points', as described earlier in the illness of the ears.
et soient li poins jusc’a XXX, ou enqui entor.	Let the points grow until they reach XXX, or perhaps somewhat beyond.

de la dislocation de l’ajutoire	From the dislocation of the shoulder
Quant li chiés de l’ajutoire est desaloiez par cause de moistor, et on le remet a leu, et il n’i puet demorer ains revient adés et desalue par petit movement qui avient, si com nos avons esproveit, adonques covient il que tu ramoinnes la dislocation premierement.	When the head of the shoulder is dislocated due to moisture, and it is reset but cannot stay in place, repeatedly dislocating with slight movement as we have experienced, then you must first reset the dislocation.

Car li jointure est refermee, et est ostee li moistor et est sanez li malaides.	For the joint is closed, and the moisture is removed and healed are the patients.
Quant en l’estomac vienent froidures et mout de moistors tant qu’il l’estraient a sa complexion, et sont multipliet li catharre a lui, et es manieres de cures acostumees et il ne profite mie, adonc covient que li malaides soit sovinez sus son dos, et estende ses jambes et ses mains.	For when colds and dampness affect the stomach as long as they correspond to its constitution, and multiply his urination, and use of accustomed treatments, but he does not benefit from them, then it is necessary for the patient to be wrapped in a blanket on his back, and stretch out his legs and arms.

et soient li cautere si parfont qu’il porpreignent les II pars dou keur, et soit li figure des cauteres selonc ceste forme sens ajostement:	And let the fire cautery extend sufficiently to turn both parts of the knee, and let the pattern of the cauteries follow this form without adjustment:
Et se tu vues cauterize d’un grant cautere enmi l’estomac selonc ceste forme;	And if you see that it has been burned down by a large cautery up to the stomach according to this form;

Aprés le cure de la cure que nos avons eut devant, tant qu’il soit sanez.	After the treatment we have undertaken, as long as he remains healthy.
Quant au foie vient dolor de froit et de moistor et de grosse ventositeit, tant qu’il est fuer mis de sa complexion natureil per les superfluitez;	As for the liver, it experiences pain due to coldness, moisture, and excessive winds; until its natural constitution is restored through elimination.

dou cautere de pleuresin	apply the weeping cautery
Li ancien dirent que on doit faire a pleuresin cauteres de racines d’aristologe, et en teil maniere:	The old ones said that one must do wet cauteries with roots of aristolochia, and in this manner:

de la mice	Of mice

Aprés le cure quant il a geteit porriture par lonc tens, et ce vaut mues que li autre des cures devant dites.	After the cure when it has healed from a long disease, and this justifies that the other remedies should be applied as previously mentioned.
de ydropisie	From dropsy
Cautere ne vaut a ydropique, fors c’a la maniere qui est apelee «asclytes».	The cautery is not effective against dropsy, except in the way it is called "asclytes".
Quant tu la cures selonc les manieres que nos avons dit en divisions, et ta cure ne profite mie, adonques covient il que tu li faices IIII cauteres entor la boude, et I sus l’estomac, et un sus le foie, et I sus la mice, et II derrier le dos sus l’espinee, et I endroit le pis;	When you treat it according to the methods we've discussed in sections, and your treatment doesn't work, then it is necessary for you to make four cauterizations inside the abdomen, one above the stomach, one on the liver, one below the intestines, and two behind the back on the spine, and one place near the anus;
et soit li cauteres bien pres de l’espés dou keur.	and make sure that the cauterizations are close to the kidney's edge.
Aprés laisse le cautere aovert por giter porriture lonc tens, et ne lassier mie la cure dou malaide aprés le cautere;	After leaving the cautery in place to promote decay for a long time, and do not stop treating the disease with remedies after cauterization;
et sanation se hasterait, et seront ensamble les II ententions avec l’aide de Deu.	And healing would hasten, and the two intents would come together with God's aid.

et cil por le dos soit olivaire, selonc ceu qu’il est ci devant mis.	And for the back, it's olive-shaped, as was shown before.
de l’enfleure des piez	of swelling around the joints
Quant li piez sont enflez a celui qui est ydropique, et sont plain d’awe citrine, il covient que tu cauterizes sus le dos dou piet entre l’auriculaire et l’anulaire;	When the joints swell in someone who is tubercular and filled with yellow bile, it's necessary to cauterize on the back of the foot between the index finger and the ring finger;
et lieve ta main avec le cautere sens torner.	And with your hand, apply the cautery lightly without turning.
Et n’entrer mie trop em parfont, ensi sarrait fuers li awe citrine, et soit li cauteres selonc cest forme:	And do not enter too far on the circumference, otherwise it would remove the yellow crystals, and apply the cautery according to this shape:

de la menoison	From memory
Quant solution de ventre vient de froidor et de moistor, tant que li vertus retentive et digestive qui est ou stomac et en l’intestine est afleboie, et ne puet estre curez par manieres de cures;	When the belly's solution comes from cold or moisture, as long as the restorative and digesting properties are at work in the stomach and within the intestines, and cannot be treated through conventional treatments;
et tu vois le malaide bien soffrant et de fort vertut, si fai I grant cautere sus l’estomac selonc ceu qu’il en a parleit ci devant ou cautere de l’estomac, au cautere circule;	and you see the patient suffering greatly and with much virtue, if perform the great stomach cauterization according to what they spoke of previously or the stomach cauterizer, in the circulating cauterization;

And if you see the moister being abundant and the patient suffering, do this: one cautery on the wrist, and one cautery on each elbow, and two small cauterizations on the stomach close to the large one. For the cure is beneficial when there's good help.
de la cure des emorroydes	Regarding the treatment of hemorrhoids
Quant les emorroydes sont ou fondement, ou une ou plusors, et sont ancienes et sont de grosses humors froides et moistes corrumpues, et sont curees si com nos avons dit en divisions, et il ne profite mie, si fai cauteres:	When the abscesses are at their origin or multiple, and are old with large cold wet corrupted pus, and are treated as we have said in sections, yet it does not benefit, if apply cauteries:

de plaie mal curee	from poorly treated wounds
Quant li malaides ne puet soffrir tailleure ne overture, que nos raconterons en son leu, si vient teil maladie que ne puet estre sanee fuer que par cautere.	When the patient's body cannot endure cutting or incision, as we will describe in its place, if there arises a disease that cannot be cured except by cautery.
Quant a aucun vient fistule, et est enveillie et giete porriture et moistors corrumpues, si la doies prover a tot une tente subtil, et garde que tu saiches a tot la tente combien elle a de parfont.	If there is no fistula, and it decays and festers due to corrupted pus and moisture, if you need to test it with a complete method, and ensure that you know the entire technique as to how many parts it has.

et te warde d’ardre lé nerf qui sunt enqui, et des grans voinnes.	And you must beware of burning the nerves which are nearby, and large veins.

aprés cure le leu tant qu’il soit sanez, et se li leus est saielez, et les matieres sont ostees lonc tens, adonc saiches que li leus est sanez entierement;	After the treatment as long as it's clean, and if the area is inflamed, and the contents have been hardened for a long time, then you know that the area has completely healed;
et se les matieres ne sont ostees, saiche que li leus est troez, et corrumpus li os au font;	And if the contents are not hardened, know that the disease is still present, and the bone has been damaged at its root;

de la hainche	From the hip
