et doutai ausi que se je tailloie sa main, qu’il ne morist, car li vertus de l’ome estoit foible;	And I also doubted that if I were to amputate her hand, she would not die, for the power of the medicine was weak;
et il se despera toz, et revint en sa terre, et se hasta de coper sa main, et fut sanez;	And he became desperate completely, and returned to his land, and covered his hand with bandages, and he recovered health;
et je n’ai ceu conteit fuers que por ceu c’on faice autreteil, s’on en a mestier.	And I have told you this only for those who might need to do something else, if necessary.
Aucune fois vient aposteme en leu charnut, et demore si longement qu’il fait grant assemblee de bowe;	No pus comes out in the inner flesh, and stays so long that it causes a large collection of worms;
et puis ront et perce, et en saut li bowe, et demoure li leus vuis, ausi com uns vasselz;	And then burrows and pierces, and the worms jump into it, and the pus remains in the patient's veins, as if they were vessels;
et li cuir qui est desus est ausi subtilz com I drapelz deliiez, et ne corront mie jusc’a l’os, ne jusc’au nerf, et telz maladie si est apelee «sain», et n’est mie apelee «fistule»;	And the skin above is as fine as the fabric of a sieve, and does not go all the way to the bone or nerve, and such disease is also called "empty" and is not called "fistula";
mais s’elle est si alongie qu’elle viegne jusc’a l’os em parfont, si est apelee «fistule»;	But if it is so long that it extends almost to the bone from end to end, then it is called a 'fistula';
et li cuire si est que tu cope celui cuir tout entor, et meismement quant il est subtilz, ausi com uns drapelz;	And in cooking, if you sear the skin all over evenly, and likewise when it is thin, like a piece of fabric;
et ne s’aert mie por sa corruption.	and does not swell from its decay.
Et se tu as fiance que li cuirs s’aerde, et li corruption n’est mie en parfont, et li cuir est espés de char, si le cure de clistere ensi:	And if you find that the skin is reddening and decay is not fully present, and the skin is full of flesh, then you should treat it with castor oil in this way:
regarde se li seins est grans, et li bowe qui en ist est de puant odor, adonques le clisterize de medicine egiptiaine qui est ensi faite:	Examine if the testicles are large, and the scrotum is filled with a foul smell, then you should use castor oil made in this way:
prenez aisil, et oile, et litargire, igalment, et metez cuire en I vassel au feu, tant que li medicine soit rouge, et deviegne ausi espesse com miel;	Take alisil, oil, and lard, equally, and cook them in a vessel on the fire until the medicine turns red, and becomes as thick as honey;
et puis pren de ceu selonc ta necessiteit, et le font en aigue et en miel, et en clisterize lou sein, et estraint le pertus;	And then use it according to your need, and apply it with water and honey, and with chloride of lime in the womb, and restrain the contraction;
et laisse la medicine ens par II houres, puis l’estrai en espreignant;	And leave the medicine on for two hours, then remove it by pinching;
fai ce mout de fois, tant que li seins soit mondefiiez, et soit ostee li puor;	Perform this action as many times as the breasts are full and drained, and when the milk is expelled;
et aucune fois est clisterizeis d’aigue de cendres, quant ceste medicine n’est presens, et est que tu preignes cendres de fust de vigne, et giete aigue desus, puis la coule, et en clisterize, tant que tu saiches que li seins est bien mondez;	And do this without the medicine present, once every time you use ashes of wood from a vine, and pour water over them. Then let it drip and use it as an enema, until you know that the breasts are well drained;
et se li malaides ne le puet soffrir, ne la medicine egiptiaine ne l’aigue de cendres, si le clisterize d’aigue et de miel ou il ait un poc de litargire broiet;	And if the patient cannot bear the Egyptian medicine or water from ashes, or an enema of water and honey, with a little boric acid;
ou tu la clistirize de miel et de vin melleit, que li mielz ait proprieteit de mundifiier et de laver, et li vins fait aerdre le sain;	For you mix with honey and wine which the honey has the property of purifying and washing, and the wine makes warmth for the healthy;
et quant tu as ce fait, et tu as fiance que li seins est bien mundifiiez, si le clisterize de ceu que fait naistre char en li, et est que tu preignes emplaustre diafinit, et le font avec oile roset et en vin;	And once you have done this, and you have ensured that the intestines are well purified, when you insert into it what causes meat to be born in them, and then you take to cover the membrane with a fine cloth, and do this with rose oil and in wine;
ou tu le clisterize d’aucunes medicines et d’oignemens, dont j’ai dit les proprietez ou traitier des oignemens;	Or you will insert it with some medicines and applications, of which I have spoken about their properties or treated the applications;
et se li pertus dou sein est petis, et li cainne dou clistere n’i puet entrer, si l’eslarge d’un fer un poc, et met ens une tente de l’oignement egiptiein, ou oignement basilicon, tant k’il soit eslargiez;	And if the opening of the intestine is small and the stick of the catheter cannot enter it, then widen it with a small iron rod, and insert a tent covered with an Egyptian ointment or basilicon balm until it is widened.
et se li plaie est trop large, si la cout et i laisse tant soulement I leu ou li clistere puisse entrer, et se li pertus que giete bowe est au desus, si le cope ou plus bas leu que i est.	And if the wound is too wide, so that the stitches only barely allow it to be closed up until the tendon or muscle can fit inside, and if the torn tendons are located above the wound, so that they are stitched higher than where I am.
Car quant li bowe est en parfont, si n’i laisse enjanrer char;	For when the arrow is fully removed, one must not leave any wound in the flesh;
et se tu ne pues coper lou sein desoz si com tu vues, si appareille en tel maniere que li bowe corre au plus bas leu que i est, car quant li bowe est parfont, si n’i laisse enjanrer char et se tu ne pues coper lou sein desoz si com tu vues, si apareille en teil maniere:	And if you cannot cover the wound from below as you see fit, equip yourself in such a way that the arrow goes to the deepest point it can reach within your body. For when the arrow is removed completely, one must not leave any flesh exposed, and if you cannot cover the wound from its location as seen, then arrange your equipment accordingly:
que li bowe corre legierement aval, et n’i lassier rien de la bowe;	So that the arrow slides smoothly downwards, and leave nothing of the arrow behind;
et pren medicines consolidatives por mettre sor le sain, et estent sus I drapeil de lin que cuevre tout le sain;	And take in medicine to consolidate, putting it over the healthy area, and they are on a linen cloth that covers all the healthy part;
puis cope as forces endroit le pertus dou sein I poc plus large dou premier, pues estent oignement souef sus I autre drapel selonc la quantiteit dou pertus, et le met sus le pertus dou sain por aligier la bowe, et n’oster mie le grant drapeil fuers que aprés maint jor une fois;	Then cut the edges of the scar on the breast as wide as possible from the first one, then apply ointment on the other cloth according to the width of the scar, and place it over the healthy area to ease the bowing, but remove only a large cloth for once after many days;
et celui qui est sor le pertus dou sein, oste sovent por oster la bowe, et saiches ceu que corra de la bowe, se c’est venin ou poc ou assez, ou digeste, ou indigeste;	And that which is on the scar of the breast often needs to remove the bowing, and know what comes from the bowing, whether it's poison or less, or enough, or digested, or undigested;
et pren warde se li patiens sent dolor ou nom, et s’il i a aposteme ou non, et quant ta medicine s’est en teil maniere estendue et tu vois la nature que saut sus le pertus dou sain, si saiches que li seins s’aert ja, et aproche li santez;	And take care if the patient feels pain or not, and whether there is pus or not, and when your medicine has spread in this manner across you see the nature that jumps on the scar of healthy tissue, then know that the breast is healing already, and brings health near;
et puis le deslie le matin, ou le tier jor, et quant tu delies la plaie, si chainge I autre drapeil, et renovele l’oignement.	And then free it in the morning, or on the third day, and when you release the wound, change to another dressing, and renew the ointment.
Et se li seins giete bowe indigeste aprés maint jor, saiches que li seins ne s’aert mie.	And if after many days, the breasts release an undigested liquid, know that the breasts are not well.
Et se venins subtilz cort aprés lonc tens, si ne te desperer mie de la santeit, car li santez aproche.	And if venomous snakes bite after a long delay, do not lose hope for recovery, because health is approaching.
Car il i a homes cui tarde enjanremens de char en ses plaies, et de ces que font le contraire;	For there are men who delay in cleansing their wounds with honey, and among those who do the opposite;
et se bowe indigeste saut dou sein aprés maint jor, saiches que li seins ne s’aert mie;	and if there is undigested matter that remains in the chest for several days, know that the lungs are not functioning properly;
et se li seins tarde d’aerdre, et est porloigniez, si ajoste medicines sechans moistes en substance et seches en vertut, si com oignement diafinit, car il i a grant partie de vitriole, et c’est li derriene medicine;	and if the lungs are slow to breathe and are distant, then adjust your remedies with both wet and dry substances, such as an oil that evaporates, because there is a large portion of vitriol, and this is the last remedy;
pren oignement dyafinit, et le font avec oile roset, et l’arose de viel vin igal en substance;	take oil that evaporates, and apply it with rose oil, and soak it in old wine of similar strength;
puis le confit et en use;	then the surgeon applies and uses it;
et ceu meisme fait mielz cuit engroissiez, quant oignemens dyafinit n’est presens, ou tu pren mirre et aloen et encens, et le broie, et le poudre sus le miel quant il est sor le feu;	and similarly creates a thicker version of cooked honey, when no remedies are present or when you take myrrh and aloes and incense, and grind them, and add the powder to honey once it is heated;
et puis en glue I drapel, et l’estent sor le sein, et aucune fois i aministre on aristologe longe, et racines de lis celeste, qui est ausi com farine de veces et centoire;	and then apply it in a paste, and leave it on the skin, and each time administer a physician's long measure, and the roots of the celestial lily which is also like powdered sesame and cinnamon;
et en use de simples ou de compostes:	and uses simple remedies or compounded ones:
broie les, et en fai poudre, et met sus le miel que j’ai dit, et en use;	grind them, make it into powder, and put it on the honey that I mentioned, and use it;
et se li cure est alongie, et n’est curez par ceste cure, adonc saiches que la corruptions est em parfont, et fait empression en l’os, ou as membres durs, ou as liemens;	and if the treatment takes a long time and doesn't improve with this treatment, then know that corruption has spread throughout, it makes an impression in the bone, or affects hard parts of the body, or causes impairments;
si le cure de la cure de fistule, si com nos avons dit ci devant.	if the treatment of pus removal, as we have said before.
de l’aposteme de l’ungle	from the abscess under the nail
Panarice est un aposteme que naist desoz l’ungle dou pouchiet de la main, ou dou piet, ou par aventure naist en autres dois;	Panarice is an abscess that arises under the nail of the hand's palm, or under the foot, or accidentally forms in other toes;
et quant il est envielliez, et on n’i prent garde, si i vient I aposteme chaus, et corront et giete bowe tant qu’elle corront la racine de l’ungle, et par aventure la corront toute;	And when it grows old, and if no care is taken, then the abscess bursts outwards, and runs and spreads across as long as its roots are under the nail, and by chance it might spread all of it;
et vient li corrosions jusc’a l’os, tant qu’il i vient dolor puant, et est li chiés dou doi larges, et est li color fuxe.	And the corrosion reaches up to the bone, as long as it brings stinking pain, and the shoulder joints become broad, and is the color turns pale.
Quant tu le cures si com nos avons dit en la division, et li cure ne profite mie, si covient que tu copes a i. fer toute la superfluiteit qui est demoree de l’ungle, puis cauterize la plaie aprés.	When you treat it as we have instructed in the section on treatment, and if the treatment does not help, then it is necessary that you remove all the excess from under the nail. Then, cauterize the wound afterwards.
Li cauteres est mout grans aide se li os est sains, et li ungle est sainne;	The cautery is greatly helpful if the bone is sound, and the nail is healthy;
et se li ungle apresse la char ens, et l’encomence a poindre, et la blece, si covient que tu mettes lou rait desoz l’ungle que point la char, et la boute en haut, et cope celi char subtilment et legierement, et met sus le remenant de la char medicines ardans et corrosives por oster tout;	And if the bone compresses the flesh at its tip, and it begins to point, and irritates it, then you should place the needle under the bone where the flesh tips, and keep it in a high position, and cut that flesh delicately and gently. Then put on top of the wound medicines hot and corrosive to remove all;
puis le cure d’oignemens tant qu’il soit sanez.	then proceed with surgery as long as it is sterile.
Et se li corrosion est en l’os, si le cope, et trai fuer, car tant com li os corrumpus i est, si ne puet saner;	And if the corrosion has reached the bone, cut it through forcefully, because the more corroded the bone is, the less it can heal;
et se tu vois le doi corrumpre, si le cope en I des nous si com il est devant dit, puis le cure tant qu’il soit sanez;	And if you see that the bone is corrupted, cut it out as soon as possible in a way similar to what has been explained earlier, then proceed with surgery as long as it remains sterile.
et s’il est ferus, et boutez, et il sent grant dolor, si covient que tu le sainnes premier;	And if the bone is hardened and you can't cut through it easily, insert forceps, and since it causes great pain, it's best to first cure that area.
puis cope l’ungle dou spatumile agut en taillant de travers desus, et warde que li taille ne viegne jusc’a la char qui est desoz l’ungle, car li malaides sentiroit trop grant dolor;	Then cut the nail of the thorn by making a crosscut above it, and be careful that the cut does not go too deep to the flesh beneath the nail, because the patient would feel too much pain.
et s’il avient, si met chose sus qui apaise.	And if it happens, place something above that soothes it.
la dolor dou sourdoit de la main	The pain was originating from the hand.
Li dois ajostez qui naist en mains d’aucuns homes par aventure est toz charnus, et par aventure i a teil ou il a osses, et aucune fois i a ungle, et aucun d’aus naissent en la racine de la jointure, ou li naissance est en aucuns nous des dois.	I must adjust those who are born with unusually thick limbs in some men, and sometimes they have part or they have bones, and at no time do they have nails, and none of them are born at the root of the joint where the birth is in neither of our thumbs.
Cil qui naist en aucune nout dou doi ne se muet, et cil qui naist a la jointure dou doi, par aventure se muet;	That which is born on any node of the knee does not move, and that which is born at the junction of the knee, by chance, moves;
la taille de celui qui est charnus si est legiere, en teil maniere:	The cut for one who has thick flesh is so light, in such a way:
taille le en sa racine d’un large spatumile.	Cut it at its root with a wide thorn.
Cil qui naist en la racine de la jointure si est grief a curer:	That which is born in the root of the joint is trouble to cure:
si te tien dou coper.	so hold it with copper.
En celui qui naist ou doit au derrien nout, si covient que tu copes premier la char reondement jusc’a l’os, puis cope l’os a une soie convenable a ceu, puis le cure tant qu’il soit sanez.	In the one born or destined in the buttocks corner, it is necessary that you first remove the fat roundness up to the bone, then cut the bone with a suitable tool, and only then treat until it's clean.
Li soudemens que vient as dois ensamble vient par naissance, ou par soudement de plaie, ou par arsure de feu, ou par semblans choses.	The fuses that come together at the joints originate through birth, or through the healing of wounds, or through heat application, or through similar circumstances.
Si couvient que tu copes celle soudeure, si que li doit repairent selonc lor formes naturelz;	If it is necessary that you repair this scarring, so that it must be restored according to their natural forms;
puis met entre dous tentes ou drapelz moilliez en oile roset, qu’il ne se soudent;	Then place between two wet tents or sheets in oil, so that they do not fuse;
ou tu met entre dous pieces de plonc subtilz, tant que li leus soit soudez, si com il covient.	or you place between two pieces of fine lead, until the limbs are fused, as it should be.
Se soudemens vient a aucun de ses dois avec la paume, si cope celle sodure si com il covient.	Sewing should be done with both hands facing down, if you make that seam as it should be.
des vils	Infernal creatures
Vis sont voinnes grosses envoloupees pleines de superfluitez melancoliouses, que vienent em plusors membres dou cors;	Their veins are large and filled with excessive melancholic fluids that come from several members of the body;
et plus avient en jambes de ces qui vont a piet et qui travaillent et portent, que a autres.	And more happens in legs of those who walk and work and carry than in others.
Il covient donques que tu li aministres aucune fois espurgement de cole, et puis le saine de la basilique.	So you should then administer a single purge to him, and then heal him with basilica treatment.
Li cure de fer si est selonc II manieres:	The treatment with iron is done in two ways:
l’une est c’on les cope, et traie on fuer le sanc noir;	One way is to apply it and draw out the black blood;
et li autre maniere si est que tu lieves la voinne, et la trai toute fuer.	And another way is to open the vein, and guide it with all strength.
Li taille si est selonc ceste maniere:	The size is according to this method:
arose li premier la jambe d’aigue chaude mout fort, tant que li gros sans soit subtiliiez, puis estrain la jambe dou malaide des desus la cuixe jusc’a la partie desoz le genoil;	Firstly, immerse the leg in hot water for a strong soaking, until the large veins become fine. Then gently squeeze the leg from the knee upwards until it reaches the ankle region;
puis cope la voinne en I leu, ou en II ou en III, d’une taille large, puis eslieve et trair fuer le sanc noir a ta main, des l’un chief jusc’a l’autre, tant que tant de sans en isse com li vertus dou malaide puet soffrir;	Then cut the vein either in position I, II or III, using a large incision. Proceed to liberate and push forcefully the black blood towards your hand from one end until the other, as long as as much of the veins can withstand the effects of the herbs;
et puis la lie, et li comande qu’il se teigne de viandes enjanrant cole noire;	Next, apply it and instruct that it be rubbed with blackened meat to darken it;
et recomence l’evacuation et la sainie quant les voinnes sont plainnes, et nuist au malaide.	And restart evacuation and cleaning when the veins are full, and harm the patient.
Li alevemens de li est selonc ceste maniere:	The operations for this are as follows:
reis la jambe dou malaide, s’il i a mout de poil, puis le met ou bain, et li arose la jambe d’aigue chaude tant qu’elle deviegne rouge, et enflent les voinnes;	Lift the leg from the patient; if there is hair, then immerse it in water; and have the leg lifted by the patient until it turns red, and swell the veins;
et se tu n’as point de baing, si le chaufe au feu, et puis le cope endroit la voinne dou lonc au chief dou genoil, ou en la partie desoz a la cheville;	And if you don't have water to bathe with, heat it over fire and then apply it along the vein from its long part up to the knee or at the ankle in the foot part;
puis aoevre le cuir a l’oncine, et escorche la voinne de chescune part, tant qu’ele apere quant on la sent;	Then scrape the skin with an onion, and strip each vein from both sides until you see it when you touch it;
et on la voit rouge et noire, et quant elle entre ou cuir si semble ausi com une corde blainche;	And it appears red and black, and when it enters the skin as if it were a white string;
puis boute le rait desoz, tant qu’ele soit alevee dou cuir, et puis la pent a l’oncine legier, puis le cope en I autre leu ensus III dois;	Start by heating the metal rod, until it is raised above the skin, then place it on the wrist lightly, then guide it in an 'I' shape for another three inches;
puis escorche le cuir sus la voinne tant qu’ele apere, puis la lieve au rais, si com tu as fait, et la pent a un autre uncine, si com tu as fait premiers;	Then scrape the skin over the vein until you can see it, then lift it with your fingers just like you did before, and press on another inch, in the same manner as you did initially;
puis cope une autre taille, ou plusors se tu en as mestier, puis la lieve, et la cope au doi dou piet, puis la trai et lieve jusc’a la seconde taille;	Then use another size or several if needed, lift it, and press on the second finger knuckle, then guide and lift until you reach the second size;
puis l’estrai de taille en taille, tant qu’elle isse toute fuer, puis la cope;	Then stretch it size by size, until all strength has been squeezed out, then press on;
et se tu ne la pues traire et lever, si i boute une aguille a tout I fil fort double, et la lie et la trai, et i boute desoz I rait, et torne ta main d’une part et d’autre, tant qu’il en isse;	And if you can't pull and lift it, then insert a needle at the end of a single thick thread, tie it and guide it, then heat a metal rod, and turn your hand from side to side until it comes out;
et garde qu’elle ne cope, car s’elle cope, si ne la puet on traire ne lever, et en vient nuisement au malaide;	And make sure it doesn't stick, because if it sticks, one can neither milk nor lift her, causing harm to the patient;
et quant tu l’as toute traite, si met sor le leu de la plaie laine moillie en vin et en oile roset;	And when you have treated her completely, place moist wool in the wound with wine and oil rose.
et le cure tant qu’il soit sanez.	Continue to clean until it is purified.
Et se li vis est contraite et torte et envoloupee ensamble, et ele n’est mie droite, si com nos avons dit, si covient que tu la fendes tortement, mais ne la coper mie;	And if the body is twisted and curled together into one bundle, and it is not straight, as we have said, then you must cut it in a twisting manner, but do not make it stick.
et la trai si com nos avons devant dit.	And milk her just as we have previously described.
Li forme dou fer dont on cope la vis si est corbes, et ne trenche mie, qu’il ne cope la voinne;	The shape of the iron that one uses to twist the body is curved, and do not cut, so as not to pierce the vein;
et est de grosse corbeure, car s’il estoit subtilz, si coperoit la voine, mais soit gros si com nos avons dit, et ci est li forme:	And it has a large curve because if it was subtle, it would impede the vein, but being large as we have said, and this is its form:
de la voinne civile	of the civil vein
Ceste voinne est enjanree en jambes, en chaudes parties ou il ne naist herbes ne arbre, et en terre ou il n’a point de moistor;	This vein is found in the legs, in warm areas where no herbs or trees grow, and on dry land where there is no moisture.
et par aventure naist autre part qu’en jambes, et ceu avient de la porriture que vient desoz le cuir, si com il vient dedens le cors serpens et vers, enjanrez entre cuir et char.	And sometimes it appears in other places than the legs, and this happens due to corruption that arises under the skin, if it comes from within the body like snakes and worms, being trapped between the skin and flesh.
Et se li signes de l’encomencement de ceste voinne si est qu’il vient en la jambe une tres grans enflammation, puis se chainge li leus, et comence li voinne fors issir, ausi com une racine d’une plante.	And if the symptoms of this vein's beginning show that there is a very large inflammation in the leg, then the veins change, and the vein starts to exit outwards, like the root of a plant.
Quant li chiés apert, si covient que tu envoloupes entor une piece de plonc des une З et demi jusc’a II З., et la noe, et laisse le plonc pendant a la jambe, et totes les fois qu’il en ist point au defuer, si l’envoloupe entor le plonc, et la nowe;	When the shoulder is opened, it must be covered internally with a piece of plaster about 1/3 and up to 2/3, you tie it, and leave the plaster hanging down the leg, and every time there's need for more outside, you cover inside the plaster and tie it again.
et s’elle est trop longe, si en cope une partie, et envoloupe le remenant, et ne la coper mie en sa racine, tant qu’elle soit toute issue;	And if it's too long, if you remove a part, envelop the rest and reattach it, making sure not to cut at its root until it is fully exposed.
car se tu la copes, si rentre en la char, et fait venir aposteme et porriture ou leu, et male maladie;	for if you remove it, should it enter the flesh, and cause pus or decay or injury to the body, leading to a bad illness;
por la queil chose il covient qu’elle soit traite poc et poc jusc’a chief, et n’en remaigne rien ou cors;	for that reason, it is necessary for her treatment to be gradual and step by step until completion, leaving nothing or any remnants behind;
et est aucune fois ceste voinne quant elle est traite de V paumes de lonc, ou de X, et uns hons vint ja a moi, a cui elle issit de X paumes de long, et quant tu la copes, si boute I rais ou pertus, et la perce jusc’a fons, si que tout en isse;	and when this vein has been treated for the length of one or several hands, and a person comes to me with it protruding from X palms in length, where its origin was determined at X palms long; if you remove it, should there be one or more raisings or abscesses, and it is punctured until the bottom, so that everything can come out;
et soit vuidie li matiere qui est dedens, et amenistre au leu medicines enjanrans porriture aucun jor, puis le cure si com les apostemes.	And let the matter inside be emptied out, and apply remedies to the wound for any pus every day, then treat it as with abscesses.
Et aucune fois a ceste voinne mains rains, et meismement quant elle apert en la jointure dou piet, ou ou piet, et i vient mout de pertus, et dont il saut rains;	And the veins in this place must be handled carefully, and likewise when it opens at the foot or ankle, or where the foot or ankle is, where there is much pus, and where you must avoid injury;
cure le donques si com nos avons dit devant.	Treat accordingly as we have explained before.
des vers qui naissent entre cuir et char	worms that come forth between skin and flesh
Ceste maladie est apelee en nostre terre «maladie de buef», por ceu qu’elle avient maintes fois as bués, et est un petis vers qui naist entre cuir et char, et va par tout le cors montant et dessendant, et le sent om bien a l’aler de membre en membre, tant qu’il desront le cuir ou il vait, et saut fuer;	This disease is called in our land "Calf Disease", because it often affects cattle, and it's a small worm that emerges between the skin and muscle, traveling throughout the body upwards and downwards, and is felt at the onset by each part of the body, until it reaches the skin where it was going, then escapes;
et est enjanrez de porriture d’aucunes humors, si com vienent vers et serpens et lumbris et ascarides ou ventre;	And it is infected with pus from various fluids, if snakes, worms, roundworms or parasites come near and enter the belly;
et doute on de son malice, car quant il va par le cors, et il monte au chief, et il vient a l’oil, par aventure rentre, et destruit l’oil;	And there is confusion about its nature, for when it travels through the body, and ascends to the head, and reaches the eye, by chance it returns, destroys the eye;
et ceu avient maintes fois.	And this happens many times.
Quant tu le vues curer et traire, si ne puet on fuers que quant il vait:	When you see it being treated and drained, one cannot but notice that when it goes:
si covient donques que tu lies le leu desus et desoz d’un fort liien bien estroitement, puis cope sus et le trai fuer, et se li vers est em parfont en la char, et tu ne le trueves, si le cauterize de feu sus, tant qu’il muire;	Therefore, it is necessary that you bind above and below the wound with a strong tight ligature, then cut upwards and drain it, and if the exit is within the flesh, and you don't find it, then apply fire to sear it from above until it heals;
et li plus grans nuisemens que il fait, si est qu’il corront l’oil, si com nos avons dit;	And the greatest harm he causes, if they run the eye, as we have said;
et se tu le vois venir ou chief pres de l’oil, si estraint desoz lui le sorcil forment, puis cope sus, et le trai fuer;	And if you see him coming or his head near the eye, then bind over him with your hands, then lift up, and pull powerfully;
et covient user le malaide de mundifiement de cors de medicines solutives por les males humors porries, et se warse de viandes enjanrans porriture.	And it is necessary to use the medicinal agent for purging of the body's humors with dissolving medicines, and be wary of meat that causes putrefaction.
de la dolor qui vient de ventositeit	The pain coming from windiness
Ceste maladie est apelee en nostre terre «vakirir», et est une dolor que vient en aucuns membres, et pues se mue de membre en membre;	This disease is called in our land "vakirir", and it is a pain that comes to any limbs, and then moves from limb to limb;
et je vis ceu que je vos di.	And I have seen what I told you.
Je fui apelez a une femme malaide, et me descovrit som bras, et vis une petite enfleure en la voinne dou brais;	I was summoned to help a sick woman, and she showed me her arm, and I saw a small swelling in the vein under the arm;
et I poc aprés, li vis monter ausi com un ver a l’espaule, plus tost que nulle chose, ausi com vif argent quant il cort de leu a autre;	And after this, my face rises as if a worm in the shoulder, more quickly than anything else, as hot silver when it is cut from one place to another.
li dolor se departit de celui leu, et se ficha en l’espaule, et puis un poc aprés corrut par tout le cors, tant qu’ele vint en l’autre brais;	The pain leaves that place and penetrates the shoulder, then a little later spreads throughout the body, until it reaches the other arm;
puis me contait qu’elle tornioit adés entor le cors, si com je la vis.	It was conveying to me that she was twisting inside the body, just as I saw.
Je me mervillai mout coment elle se movoit ensi de membre em membre, car je n’avoie onques veut ceste maladie selonc ceste maniere.	I was marveling much how she moved thus from limb to limb, for I had never seen this disease in such a manner.
Toutevoie, je avoie veut maint que bien avoient veut movoir dolor de leu a autre, mais je ne l’avoie mie veut, si com je le vis en la femme;	Nevertheless, I wanted many times to move the pain from one place to another, but I did not want it like I saw in the woman;
et je me pensai que c’estoit por ceu que li femme avoit sec cors, et les voinnes descovertes, et por ceu apparoit celle ventositez constrainte;	And I thought it was because the woman had a wet body and her veins exposed, and that is where the constriction of wind appears;
et n’aperent mie selonc ceste raison a ces qui sont delicious, et qui ont moistes cors et voinnes reponues.	And cannot be seen according to this reason among those who are delicate, and have moist bodies and veins that respond.
Et quant tu vues curer ceste maladie, et li malaides sent celle dolor, s’elle t’apert si com nos avons dit, si la lie desus et desoz hastanment, et puis cope sus tant que cele ventositez constrainte au leu isse fuer;	And when you see to treat this illness, and the patient feels that pain, if it opens like we said, open it from above and below quickly, then start sewing as long as that constraining wind force comes out of the place.
et cauterize le leu;	And apply the cautery to the area;
et se tu ne la vois a tes eulz, si le cure de ceu qui deboute les ventositez, si com pilules fetides, et pilules de serapin, et semblans autres.	And if you do not see it at your eyes, treat the one who expels the winds, like stinking pills, and snake pills, and similar others.
des saiettes	Des saiettes" in this context likely refers to "extracting arrows". In medieval medical practices, physicians would often deal with wounds caused by arrows or projectiles, requiring them to be removed from the body.
Les saiettes sont diverses, selonc lor semblances et selonc les leus dou cors ou elles chient.	Arrows are diverse, depending on their appearance and according to the location of their impact on the body.
Li diversitez de lor si est qu’il i a de celles qui ont grans pointes, et petites, et chevees, et soudees;	The variety is such that there are those with large points, and small ones, and hairy, and fused;
et de celles qui ont II angles, et de celz qui ont lengues, et de celles ou il a pieces;	And of those with two angles, and of those with tongues, and of those where there are fragments;
et celle qui chiet en aucun membre si chiet selonc II manieres:	And the one who urinates in no member but does so according to two ways:
ou en membre principeil cheveit, si com cerveil, cuer, foie, pormon, rains, intestine, vessie, et semblans membres.	or in the primary organs if it urinates, as with the brain, heart, liver, spleen, lungs, intestines, bladder, and other similar organs.
Quant elle chiet donques en aucun leu de ces membres, et li signe de mort, que je te dirai ci aprés, t’aperent:	And when it urinates then not in any part of these organs, and the sign of death that I will tell you later, becomes apparent:
si covient que tu te warses de l’estraction de ceste saiette, car li mors vient aprés en plusors dispositions;	So it is necessary for you to be prepared for the extraction of this arrow, because death comes after in various circumstances;
et quant cist mal signe ne t’aperent mie, et li saiette n’est mie em parfont, si la trai, et cure la plaie.	And when that bad sign does not become apparent and the arrow is not fully extracted, you should retrieve it, and treat the wound.
Et li signe dou cerveil quant li saiette i chiet et perce l’os, et saut li syfac fuer qui est sus le cerveil, est quant scotomie et sode et esvertin et roujor ens eulz, et enflammation et roujor de lengue, et spasme et permixtion d’entendement, et vomissemens de cole;	And the sign of brain injury when an arrow has pierced and gone through bone, causing a blow to the head is where blindness, stiffness, vertigo, heat in the eyes, inflammation and reddening of the tongue occur, along with spasms and confusion of mind, and vomiting of bile;
et per aventure ist sans fuer des narines, ou des oreilles;	And perhaps there is weakness in the strength of the nostrils, or the ears;
et par aventure pert la parole et la voix;	And sometimes affects speech and voice;
et saut de la plaie moistor blanche semblant a poulz, et en saut ausi com bruee de char;	And the wound shows white moisture like pus, and also burns like a charred flesh in its movement;
et se cist signe t’aperent, si te tien de la cure, et trai la saiette s’elle n’est ens.	And if you notice this sign, take care of the treatment, and pull out the arrow if it is still there.
Li signe de la siette quant elle chiet ou cuer, sont qu’elle est pres de la mamele senestre, et sent ausi com s’elle estoit fichie en chose dure, ne mie vuide;	The sign of the arrow when it hits or pierces near the left nipple is that it's close to the breastbone. It also feels like if it was stuck in something hard, not empty;
et par aventure li siette se muet ausi com li poulz, et en cort noir sanc, et vient froidor et suor froide, et sincope:	And perhaps the seat also moves as with the hair, and in black blood, and comes coldness and cold sweat, and fainting:
saiches adonc sens doute ke li mors dessent.	Therefore, you can understand that many die from doubt and fear.
Et li signe de la saiette que nevre lou pormon est que sans plains d’escume saut de la plaie, et li gorge enfle, et li malaides mue color, et sospire haut et quiert le froit ar.	And the sign of an arrow that never leaves its path is when blood spurts from the wound without foam, and the throat swells up, and the patient's face changes color, and they sigh loudly while their body grows cold.
Et se li saiette chiet en la coverture dou pis, si est delez les petites costes;	And if the arrow passes through the undercoat of the buttock, it goes out beyond the small ribs;
et giete grant alainne et grant dolor et sospire;	And causes great pain and agony, along with sighing;
et li muevent tuit li membre des espaules.	And it moves the entire limb from the shoulders.
Et se li saiette chiet ou stomac, par aventure si saut de la plaie aucune chose de la viande indigeste.	And if an arrow or stomach penetrates it, perchance something of the undigested meat comes from the wound.
Et se li saiette chiet ou ventre, et en saut point de fien par l’intestine rout, si n’a point d’esperance en la cure, ne en l’estraction de la saiette.	And if an arrow or stomach pierces it, and if there is no meat in the intestines after jumping from the wound, then there's no hope for treatment, nor extraction of the arrow.
Et se li saiette chiet en la vessie, et li urine en saut et vient defuer, et li malaides sent fort dolor:	And if the arrow passes through the bladder, and the urine springs out and goes in all directions, and the patient feels intense pain:
saiches que li plaie est mortelz.	You will know that the wound is mortal.
Li autre membre, si com li faice et li colz et li gorge et li espaule et li adjutoire et li espinee dou dos et li forcele et li cuixe et les jambes, et li membre semblant, sont sauf selonc plusors dispositions.	The other body parts, such as the limbs (including arms and legs), neck, throat, shoulder, elbow, back, spine, knees, and feet, as well as any similar parts, are safe according to various positions.
Quant li saiette est en lou nerf ou l’artere, et elle n’est venimouse, si com je vos dirai qu’il m’avint, por ceu que vos faciez autretel.	When an arrow is in the nerve or artery and it isn't venomous, as I will tell you that this happened to me, because what you did was different.
Il avint a I home c’une saiette li chut ou larmier en la racine dou neis:	It happened to a house where an arrow hit or pierced near the nose:
je la tentai, et la traï d’autre part desoz la graisse de l’oreille, et fut sanez sens nusement.	I tried it and from the other side removed it across the ear wax, and was able to remove it without any difficulty.
Et traï a un jeu une saiette que li chut en la graisse de l’oil desoz la papiere desoz, et li saiette estoit reponue, et n’en poi ataindre que la pointe devers lou fust, et estoit li saiette grans d’un arc turcois, a tout I fer legier sens oreilles;	And tried an arrow that had hit in the wax near the eye under the paper wax, and the arrow was stuck, and could not reach even its tip towards the shaft, and the arrow was as large as a Turkish bow, all through without piercing any ear.
li jeus fut sanez, et ne li vint nulz mavais accidens.	The attempt was successful, and no unfortunate incidents occurred.
Et traï une saiette de la gorge a un crestien, et estoit li saiette arabique a oreilles:	And tried an arrow from the throat to a Christian, and it was the Arab arrow with ears:
je soiai les barbions, et subtiliai tant que je la traï, et fut sanez li crestiens.	I shaved them, and trimmed them as I carried them, and they were healthy for the Christians.
Et traï une saiette a I home, que li estoit cheue ou ventre, et pensai qu’il moroit;	And pulled an arrow at his home, where it was stuck in his back or belly, and thought he would die;
et puis qu’il ot passez XXX jors, si ne mua point sa disposition;	and then after thirty days, if its condition did not change;
je taillai sus la saiette, et l’engignai, et la traï fuer, et n’ot point de mavais accident.	I cut the arrow shaft, set it, and carried it forcefully, and there was no bad accident.
Et si vis I home cui une saiette chut ou dos, et fut li plaie soudee sus;	And if someone at home has an arrow fall or hit their back, and the wound heals internally;
et demora li saiette dedens li, et ne chainja point ses dispositions naturez, ne ne trova nuisement en aucune de ses oevres naturelz.	And the arrow stays inside, and does not alter its natural disposition, nor finds any harm in any of its natural works.
Et vis I autre homme, cui il chut une saiette en sa faice, et fut soudee li plaie;	And see another man, who was struck by an arrow in his face, and was stitched up the wound;
et demora ensi sens soffrir grant dolor;	and then endured without suffering great pain;
et mout d’autres semblans.	And many other similar things.
Et traï une saiette a I home des princes le roi, que li estoit cheue enmi lou neiz, et estoit un poc declinans a la destre partie;	And there was an arrow for the king in the middle of his chest, it had penetrated him up to the heart, and was slightly tilted towards the right side.
et estoit li saiette toute reponue.	And the arrow was fully inserted.
Je fui apelez a la cure aprés ceu qu’elle fut cheue III jors.	I was called for treatment after it had been three days since it was penetrated.
Si trovai la plaie mult estroite.	I found the wound very tight.
Je la quis a tout une subtil tente, et ne la sentis mie;	I examined her with all subtlety and did not feel anything;
et il sentoit pointure et dolor desoz sa destre oreille.	And there was a wound and pain spreading across his right ear.
Je pensai que c’estoit de la pointe de la saiette Je mis sus lou leu emplaustre atratifet digestif, por ceu que li leus n’enflast;	I thought it was due to the tip of the arrow. I placed a therapeutic plaster on his chest because his lungs were not inflamed;
et m’aparut li leus de la saiette.	And I saw the head of the arrow.
Je i mis l’emplaustre mains jors, et resouda li plaie derechief, et demora ensi li malaides lonc tens, tant qu’il sentit la saiette I jor dedens son neis;	I applied the poultice to his hands for several days, and healed the wound quickly. The patient then remained in this state for a long time until he felt the arrow inside his nose;
et il le me dist.	And he told me.
Je mis sus la plaie medicine ague corrosive par mains jors, tant qu’elle fut overte, et la tentai, et sentis le chief de la saiette qui s’aerdoit au leu;	I applied corrosive medication to the wound with my hands until it opened. I tried and felt the tip of the arrow which was moving towards his shoulder;
puis ajostai en l’overture de la plaie par celle medicine ague, tant que li chiés de la saiette m’aparut visablement;	Then I adjusted the wound opening with that corrosive medicine, until the head of the arrow became visibly apparent;
et trespassa bien li termines entor IIII mois, et puis eslarja si li plaie que je i boutai les tenailles, et le meus d’une part et d’autre, et ne pot issir;	And it passed through the inner parts for about four months, and then opened so that I could use my pliers, on both sides, and it did not come out;
adonques ne cessai de subtiliier et d’engignier de manieres d’estrumens, tant que je la pris I jor as tenailles bien faites, selonc ceu que sa forme venra en la fin de cest chapistre, tant que je la traï, et restourai la plaie.	Therefore do not stop refining and engineering ways for instrument tools, until I take just one day using well-made tongs. According to how its form emerges at the end of this chapter, whether I am grasping or moving it around, and then I return to the wound site.
Et li mire jugent que li cartillaige dou nez ne puet restorer:	And those who specialize judge that the cartilage of the nose cannot be restored:
je la restourai adonques, et fut soudee li plaie, et fut sanez li malaides entierement.	So I would return to this situation, and healed the wound, and fully restored the patient's health.
Or t’ai dit la qualiteit de l’estraction d’aucunes saiettes, si que tu mettes ta cure sus ceu que je ne dis mie, car li livres ne puet mie tout porprendre;	And now I'll tell you about the quality of extracting certain arrows, so that when you apply my advice, remember what I don't explicitly say; for books can never encompass everything.
mais li saiges maistres compere sus bien poc grant chose, et sus ceu que li est present et defaillant, trueve nueve oevre, et nuef estrument, au dessendement des choses estrainges qui avienent en cest art.	However, even wise masters may not have much information about minor things; they'll find nine new works and six instruments for removing foreign bodies that occur in this craft.
Je dis que les saiettes n’issent des membres ou elles sont fichies fuer que selonc II manieres:	I state that arrows do not penetrate limbs except according to two manners:
ou par lou leu ou elles entrent, ou par d’autre part;	either by their head or they enter, or from another side;
et celle que saut fuer par lai ou elle entre, c’est saiette entrans en leus charnus, et saut fuer aucune fois maintenant.	And the one that pierces through its head or enters, it is an arrow entering into their flesh, and never does this happen again.
Et s’elle ne saut maintenant, si la laisse tant que li chars soit porrie entor, et soit alegie li issue;	And if it doesn't pierce now, leave it until the flesh is cooked inside and becomes tender, and wait for the outcome;
et ausi s’elle est fichie en l’os, et elle ne puet issir, si la laisse ensi aucuns jors, et la muef chescun jor;	And likewise if it is stuck in the bone and cannot come out, leave it like that for a few days, and remove it every day;
et adonques elle saut, et s’elle ne saut, si perce entor a tout I foret subtil, tant que li leus entor soit eslargiez, et puis la trai.	And then it pierces through, and if it doesn't, it penetrates inside until all the delicate parts are touched, as long as the bones are broad inside, and then remove it.
Et se li saiette est fichie en l’os dou chief, et vait jusc’a l’un des ventres dou cerveil, et aucuns des accidens que j’ai dit apert au malaide:	And if the arrow is stuck in the bone at the shoulder, and extends up to one of the lungs within the head, and all the incidents that I have described become clear to the patient:
si ne la traire mie, mais la laisse tant qu’elle soit igalz aprés aucuns jors, car se li saiette vient jusc’a syfac, c’est li mors.	If you do not treat it but let it grow until after a few days its growth is equal, because if the arrow reaches that furrow, it's death.
Et se li saiette n’est fichie fuer qu’en l’os soulement, et ne vient jusc’a syfac, et demoure li malaides aucuns jors sens mavais accident, si l’engigne dou traire.	And if the arrow is only stuck in the bone and does not reach so far, yet remains within the patient for several days without any bad incident, then use the device to remove it.
Et s’elle est mout fichie ensi et ne puet issir fuer, si i aministre tareres entor, si com je t’ai dit;	And if it is stuck in such a way and cannot come out force, if I administer leeches internally, as I have told you;
puis cure le leu tant qu’il soit sanez.	Then treat the wound until it heals properly.
Et se li saiette est reponue en leu dou cors si c’on ne la puisse veoir, si la quier a tout la tente;	And if the arrow is returned to the body's wound so that it cannot be seen, one should seek it with all their effort.
et se tu la sens, si la trai a aucun estrument covenauble;	And if you sense it, lead it to any suitable tool;
et se tu ne pues por l’estrecement de la plaie, et por la parfondesce de la saiette, et il n’i a os ne nerf ne voine, si la fens tant que li plaie soit grans;	And if you cannot do it by the tightening of the wound, and by the depth of the arrow, and there is no bone, nerve or vein, cut as long as the wound becomes large;
et trai la saiette se tu pues, et s’il ait en la saiette oreilles a coi elle tient, si oste la char qui est ens fichie de II pars au mues que tu pues, et puis brise ou ploie les oreilles de la saiette, tant que tu la puisses traire;	And pull the arrow if you can, and if there are holes in the arrow that hold it, remove the flesh which is stuck from two sides as much as you can, and then break or bend the ears of the arrow, as long as you can pull it.
et subtilie bien que tu ne brisier la saiette, que tu la trairoies plus griement.	And do it carefully so that you don't break the arrow, making its removal more painful.
Et se tu ne pues a une fois, si la lai jusque li leus entor soit porris, puis la trai, car li estraction iert alegie.	And if you can't do it in one go, leave it until its entire length is rotted away by maggots, then try to pull it out, as extraction requires effort.
Et se li decorremens de sanc te fait contraire, si amenistre ceu que nos avons dit de la cure en son chapistre;	And if the bleeding causes you to be against it, then apply what we have said about treatment in our chapter about the cure;
et te warde de l’incision dou nerf et de la voinne, et met engien coment tu pues mues traire la saiette sens peril, ou tost ou tart, ou fermement ou belement;	And you must know about the incision near the nerve and vein, and use means so that you may draw out the arrow without risk, quickly or cautiously, firmly or gently;
et met le malaide selonc la forme qu’il estoit quant li saiette li chut ens, car c’est li plus grans aide que i soit, et se tu ne pues, si lou met selonc ceu que li signe lou te mostrent.	And guide the patient according to the shape they were in when the arrow fell inside, because this is the greatest help that it be as such; and if you cannot do so, follow what the sign tells you.
Li saiette que vient fuer d’autre part, ou il apert aucune chose de li, ou li cuir est enflez endroit si c’on le voit ou sent aparamment:	The arrow that comes from the other side, or where it opens something in him, or if the skin is swollen at such a place as we can see or feel differently:
taille donques sus, tant que les tenailles i puissent prendre, et puis l’estrai:	So grasp it up high, while you can take the pliers there, and then pull:
si saut fuer maintenant.	If it jumps now.
Et s’elle est retenue en l’os, si tornoie ta main rondement, tant qu’elle entre en l’os, et eslarge l’os, puis la trai.	And if she is held in the bone, twist your hand round as long as she enters the bone and widens the bone, then pull her out.
Et s’elle ne puet issir, si la laisse encor, et puis rencomence l’estraction tant qu’elle isse fuer;	And if it cannot come out, leave it still, and then continue the extraction until it comes out fully;
et se li fust de la saiette i est, se le boute a tout le fust;	and if the arrow is inside him, push the whole shaft of it through;
et se li fust chiet, et tu vues aministrer boutement, si i aministre I estrument cheveit, si que li pointe de la saiette entre en la cheveure de l’estrument;	and if the shaft is cut, and you see it administered with force, if you use a proper tool, so that the arrowhead enters through the end of the tool;
et puis boute fuer, et se li saiette est chevee, se i boute I estrument a pointe entrant ens, por alegier l’estraction.	and then push forcefully, and if the arrow is pierced, use the tool with a pointed end entering first to facilitate extraction.
Et se li saiette est entouchie, si covient que tu copes toute la char entor ou li venins est, se tu pues, puis cure la plaie si com il couvient.	And if the arrow is encased, it must be that you remove all the flesh around or where I am entering, if possible, then treat the wound as appropriate.
Et se li saiette chiet ou peis ou au ventre ou a la vessie ou au costeit, et elle est prochiene, et tu pues coper sus, se i cope;	And if the arrow is inside or close to the lungs or bladder or ribcage, and it's nearly within you, if you can cover it up, then do so.
et te garde de coper la voinne et lou nerf, et puis l’estrai, et puis cout la plaie, se mestier est;	And protect against covering the vein and the nerve, and then extract it, and then suture the wound, for this is a skilled trade.
et la cure tant qu’elle soit sanee.	And the treatment until it has healed.
Li forme des tenailles dont on trait les saiettes sont semblans au bec d’oiseil, et vez ci la forme:	The shape of the pincers used for arrows is similar to the tip of a bird's beak, and here is the form:
Et en sont mout de manieres:	And in those many ways:
grans, moienes, et petites, selonc la quantitei de la saiette.	Great, medium, and small, according to the size of the arrow.
Li forme dou boutant cheveit est ausi com li penne d’un oisel, por bouter a la pointe de la saiette, si com ci est li forme:	The shape of the arrowhead resembles the feathers of a bird, because it tapers to the tip of the arrow, as this is its form:
li forme des tenailles por bouter et por sachier si est ci:	The shape of the pliers for pushing and pulling as such is like this:
des voinnes dou cors communes	from the horns of common veins
Des voinnes dont on se saine sont XXXI, de coi il a ou chef XVI, c’est a savoir:	Of the veins from which we bleed, there are thirty-one, of which twelve are at the head, namely:
II batans qui sont aprés les oreilles, qui sont apelees les dous «herbech»;	Two smaller ones located behind the ears, which are called "the two herbs";
et les II arteres qui sont en II temples apparans;	and the two arteries in the two visible temples;
et II voines que sont en II larmiers des II eulz, que sont apelees «aspires»;	and two veins that are in the two corners of the two eyes, which are called "sponges";
et li voine que est emmi le front;	And the vein that is within the forehead;
et li voinne que est au chief dou neis;	and the vein that is in the head near the nose;
et les II guindeges qui sont ou col;	and the two jugulars which are at the neck;
et les II voinnes que sont en levres desus de la bouche, et ce sont les voines que sont apelees «augeherich»;	and the two veins that are in the cheeks above the mouth, and these are the veins that are called "aughers";
et II voinnes que sont desoz la lengue.	and two veins that are beneath the tongue.
Les voinnes dont on saine communement sont V en chescun bras:	The veins we usually treat are five in each arm:
l’une est li cephalique, et est dou senestre costeit, et l’apelent li laie gens «voinne dou chief»;	one is the cephalic vein, and it's at the left rib, and they call this 'the head vein';
et li moiene est apelee «faste», et est composte de la cephalique et de la basilique, et l’apelent li laie gens «voinne dou cuer»;	and the median is called 'the fast' and is made up of the cephalic and basilica veins, and they call this 'the heart vein';
et li basilique si est ou destre costeit, et l’apelent li laie gent «voinne dou ventre», et est sus le foscile, et est celle dont on saine, qui apert manifestement sus le pouchet.	And the diaphragm is either on the right side or inside the chest, and they call this area "the windpipe", and it is on the ribcage, and this is what we heal, which clearly opens up on the belly.
Et li salvatelle est li voine qui est entre l’auriculaire et l’anulaire, et si a II rains;	And the artery is the vein that's located between the index and ring fingers, and if you measure it twice;
et en la jambe et ou piet sont III voinnes:	and in the leg and at the ankle there are three veins:
l’une si est desoz la corbeure dou pochet dou senestre costeit, et li seconde sophene qui est a la cheville dou destre costeit;	one is below the bend of the belly on the left side of the rib cage, and the second is superficial which is at the ankle on the right side;
et li voine qui est apelee «nesse», que est en la cheville de l’autre costei;	and the vein that's called "the nesse", which is at the ankle on the other side;
et en l’autre jambe sont III voinnes desoz celles.	and in the other leg there are three veins below those.
Li sainie des voinnes que sont aprés les oreilles si aide as catharres anciens, et a emigraine;	The cleansing of veins located behind the ears aids with the surgeons of old, and for migraines;
et li qualiteis dou sainier, si com je te dis, et est que tu reises lou chief dou malaide, et frote lou leu ou les voinnes sont d’un drap aspre;	And the qualities of a surgeon, such as I tell you, and it is that you rub the head of the malady, and scrape or rub the area where the veins are with a hard cloth;
puis estrigne li malaides son col a une vis, tant que les II voinnes aperent derrier les oreilles en II leus dependens dou chief:	Then sharpen the neck of the malady like a screw, until the two veins appear behind the ears in two places depending on the head:
quier les donques a ton doi, et ou tu sens lou poulz desoz ton doi, si seigne d’enche;	Kneel down there, and where you feel the pulse under your hand, mark it with a sign;
puis pren la lancette, et la boute par desoz la voine jusc’a l’os, puis lieve ta main a tout la voinne amont, et cope et lou cuir et la voinne bien II dois dou traver, et fai issir dou sanc tant que tu vues;	Then take the scalpel and cut through the vein just to the bone, then lift your hand all along the vein upwards, and open up the skin and the vein properly two inches deep, and let out the blood until you see it;
puis l’estrain et lie, tant qu’ele soit sanee;	Then strain and bind until it's healed;
et j’ai ja dit l’incision et le cautere ou premier livre.	And I have already spoken about the incisions and cauterizations in the first book.
Li sainie des II arteres que sont en II temples, si vaut a emigrainne anciene, et sode, et obtalmie acostumee, et au cors des larmes agues as eulz;	The health of the two arteries that are in the two temples, if it involves ancient gout, and sodine, and ophthalmic usage, and within the body of feverous tears.
et li qualitez dou sainier si est si com je dis:	And the quality of the surgeon is as I describe:
et est que li malaides estraigne son col, tant que les II voinnes aperent apertement;	And let the patient strain their throat until both veins appear clearly;
et sent lou polz desoz ton doi, et puis seigne d’enche;	Feel the pulse on both sides, and then proceed to examine;
puis lieve lou keur sus la voinne en haut a ton doi indice, et boute la lancette desoz, et lieve la voine en haut, et la cope, si com tu as fait en II autres voinnes, et fai corre dou sanc selonc ta necessiteit;	Then gently press on the vein above your thumb at the base of your neck, and hold the scalpel against it. Lift the vein upwards and then cut it, just as you would with other veins, making sure to follow the flow of blood according to your need;
puis deslie lou malaide, et met ton doi sus la voine une houre, puis met sus coton;	Then release the patient, place your finger on the vein for an hour, then place it on cotton;
et puis la lie forment, et la laisse tant qu’elle soit sanee;	and then form the pus, and leave it until it has healed;
et nos en avons jai parleit et de lor copement et de lor estraction, ou comencement dou livre.	and we have discussed this and their management as well as their extraction, or the beginning of the book.
Li sainie de la voine dou front si vaut autant com li sainie de la cephalique as maladies de la faice ancienes, et a emigraine, et a roujor;	The venous swelling of the forehead is as valuable in diagnosing conditions like the ancient diseases of the face, and migraines, and hives;
et li qualitez si est que li malaides estraigne son col en tordant, tant que li voine apere;	and its quality is that the patients twist their necks in discomfort until the vein appears;
puis pren l’estrument qui est apelez «fosseur», dont ci est li forme:	then take the tool called 'spreader', as depicted here:
Et met la pointe sus la voinne, et fier sus de ta main, ou d’autre chose, et laisse dou sanc issir selonc la quantiteit que tu vues;	And place the tip on the vein, and press with your hand or another object, and let the blood flow according to the amount you see;
puis delie au malaide le col, et lie la voine tant qu’elle soit saneel et aucune fois l’uevre on d’un flaime large.	Then release the patient's neck, and bind the artery until it is sound and when operation has made a broad flame.
Toutevoie, il ne covient mie que li flaimes soit trop agus;	Otherwise, it is not good that the flames be too large;
et le saine de travers, car li os est pres, et par aventure brise li flaimes quant il est subtilz.	And let the flame burn across them, for the bone is close by, and if it happens that the flame burns through when they are fine.
Li sainie des II voines que sont en II larmiers si aide as eulz, et a la tigne, et a la roujor, et a l’oriuel en l’oil, et as maladies de la faice;	The healing of the two veins that are in the two sinuses helps with the eyes, and at the elbow, and at the knee, and around the ear in the ear, and for diseases of the face;
et li qualitez de lor sainie si est que li malaides estraigne son col en tordant d’aucun liien, si com devant;	And the quality of their healing is such that the patient tightens their neck by twisting with some ligament, as before.
puis le saine, et soit li sainie dou traver, un poc dou lonc dou flaime un poc large, car il n’i a point de char.	Then heal it, and let the healing pass through, somewhat along the length of the flame, somewhat wide, for there is no flesh.
Et se li flaimes est subtilz, par aventure si brise;	And if the flames are fine, by chance they might break;
puis fai corre dou sanc, tant com tu en as mestier, et puis lie sus couton, et le lie bien.	then drain the blood as much as you need to, and then bind it with cotton, and bind it well.
Li sainie de la voine dou neis si vaut a ague, et a sode forsenee, et a maladies de faice, si com emigraine et roujor que vient en la faice, et meimement quant elle est anciene;	Surgery for the nose near the eyes is worth for water (discharge), and for sudden coldness, and diseases of the face, such as migraine and inflammation that comes in the face, and also when it's old;
et li qualitez de la sainie si est que li malaides estrigne son col, puis estrain son neis a ta main senestre, et pren lou flaime subtil lonc, et le fiche emmi la levre en l’espaice qui est entre les II narines, car li voinne n’apert mie bien enqui, et li sans comencera maintenant a corre;	The quality of the surgery is that the patient's throat is narrowed first, then their nose is stretched to your left hand. Take a fine flame long and stick it in between the two nostrils, as the vein doesn't open properly there, and the process will start now to drain;
et n’aler mie trop em parfont, et fai corre dou sanc selonc ta necessiteit, puis la lie une nuit, car elle est mout tost restoree;	And do not go too fast, and make the cure according to your need, then let it rest for a night, for she is very quickly restored;
et c’est li forme dou flaime:	and it's the form of fire:
Li sainie des II guindeges si aide a l’estrecement de l’alainne, et a l’encomencement de meselerie, et a mout de maladies, et a empetigine, et a corrodens, et a herpes, et estiomenes;	The treatment of the two intestines helps with narrowing of the arteries and the onset of melena, and many diseases, and in empyema, and corrosion, and herpes, and indigestion;
et li qualitez de la sainie si est que li malaides estraigne son col desoz l’une et l’autre, si com nos avons dit;	and the quality of this treatment is that the patient's throat narrows from one side to the other, as we have said;
et soit li maistres estans sus lou chief dou malaide, et li malaides siece sus I siege, puis saine la voine dou lonc un poc largement, puis trai dou sanc tempreement, ou tant com mestier est;	and let the master be above the patient's throat, and the patient bends over the edge, then cure the artery length-wise for a bit wider, then drain the blood moderately, or as much is necessary;
puis refai autreteil en l’autre voinne, puis deslie lou liien, et estraint andous les voines moienement, que li malaides n’estrangle;	Then reopen another vein, then undo the ligature, and gently hold the veins in place, so that the patient doesn't choke.
et le laisse jusc’au matin, que li plaie soit sanee.	And let it be until morning, so that the wound heals.
de la sainie des leivres	Of surgical treatment of wounds
Li sainie des voinnes des levres desus si aident a cole en la bouche, et a corruption de gencives, et fendures de levres, et dou neis et entor.	The care of veins in the mouth aids in collection within the mouth, and contributes to gum decay, and splits in lips, and nosebleeds and internal bleeding.
Et li qualitez de la sainie si est de faire seoir lou malaide devant toi, et estraint son col si com j’ai dit;	And to ensure quality of healing, have the patient sit in front of you, and hold their neck as I've described;
puis torne la levre, et regarde as II voinnes, dont l’une est a la destre levre et li autre a la senestre, et les conoist on par ceu qu’elles sont noires, et par ceu que entor elles a voines menues noires:	Then turn the lip, and look at the two veins, one is in the right lip and the other in the left, and you know them by the fact that they are black, and because there are small black veins around them:
cope donques l’une et l’autre, et se tu ne les conois, et tu en es en doutance, si cope la plus grosse de chescune part, et tout ausi fai des II voinnes que sont desus et desoz, car c’est une meisme maniere.	Treat both then, and if you do not recognize them, and are in doubt, treat the larger one of each side. And do it similarly for both veins above and below, because it is the same method.
de la sainie desoz la lengue	Of surgical treatment of the tongue
Li sainie des voinnes que sont desoz la lengue si aide aprés la sainie de la cephalique, et c’est a l’estrecement de la gorge, et as maladies de l’uve, et as maladies de la bouche;	The health of the veins that are under the tongue requires aid after the treatment of the head vein, and this is focused on the constriction of the throat, and diseases of the iris, and diseases of the mouth;

ou em poignant a tout I flaime mirtin large, ou olivaire subtil si com coutez trenchans, et est apelez «anesil»;	either by applying to every flame the large mirthin tool, or the subtle olive tool if it's for arm incisions, and they are called "aneil";

Li sainie de la basilique, qui est une de ces voinnes, si aide as maladies que sont desoz la gorge, et ou col, et ou peis, et ou ventre;	The health of the basilica, which is one of these veins, aids in diseases that are localized around the throat, and in the neck, and in the stomach, and in the abdomen;

eschui la donques.	Therefore, this is it.
