et li voinne si est a la cheville, et par desus lou piet en vont mout de rains;	And if the vein is at the ankle, and above it runs much blood;
saine la donques ou plus large rain, ou a la cheville, que mues vaut.	Then heal it or make it wider where necessary, or at the ankle, for that is beneficial.
Et se tu la saines sus lou piet, si te warde des ners qui sont desoz, et la saine de traver ausi com en copant;	And if you heal it above the heart, be cautious of the nerves that are nearby, and also heal across in the same manner as when sewing.
et soit li flaimes anesil.	and let the flames be inside-out.
Et se li sans n’en puet issir, si remet lou piet en l’aigue, et laisse bien vuidier la voine.	And if it cannot pass without difficulty, then place the foot in water, and allow for thorough bleeding of the vein.
Et se li sainieres faut la premiere fois, si rencomence la seconde au desus un poc, car li leus est salz;	And if it needs healing for the first time, then try again with the second dose above a bit more, because the lungs are salty;
ne ne douter de nerf, si com nos avons dit, et ensi fai de la sophene de l’autre piet igalment.	Nor should you doubt of nerves, as we have said, and do the same on the other side equally.
Li leus de la voinne sciatique est a la cheville de fuer, et sa sainie vaut a la dolor de la hainche, quant c’est por sanc chaut.	The veins of the sciatic region are at the ankle bone, and their health corresponds to the pain in the hip; when it is due to blood congestion.
Et li qualitez de sa sainie si est que li malaides entre ou bain, et estraigne desus la cheville IIII dois en tordant, car autrement n’apert li voinne;	And the quality of its healing is such that the patient feels better or bathes, and twists above the ankle four times, because otherwise the vein does not open;
et s’elle apert, si le saine en toutes les manieres que tu pues, et en traversant;	And if it opens, heal it in all the ways you can, and across;
et vaut mues que tu la copes, car li leus est saus, et elle est mout reponue a mains homes.	And treat as you grasp it, for the hands lack force, and she is very responsive to human hands.
Et se tu ne la trueves, si saine aucun rain de li qui apert ou dos dou piet, et vers lou petit doi, et te warde des ners;	And if you do not find it, heal no bone that opens or under the heel, and towards the little toe, and beware of the nerves;
et fai tant corre dou sanc que tu vues, et puis deslie lou lien, et met sus coton et l’estraint;	And make such a flow of blood that you see it, and then release the knot, and place cotton and tighten it;
ele est maintenant sanee.	It is now healed.
des sainies de ventouse	of suction healings
Ventouses sont fait de cornes, ou d’arain, ou de voirre;	Vacuum cups are made from horns, or spiders, or toads;
et ventosation si est faite selonc II manieres:	And suction is performed in two ways:
ou par ferir et atraire sanc, ou sens ferir.	By causing and attracting blood, or means of causing blood to come out.
Et ceste ventosation qui est sens ferir si est selonc II manieres:	And this suction, which is meant to cause injury, can be done in two ways:
ou elle est a tout feu, ou sens feu;	either it's with instantaneous fire, or by means of fire;
et ventosation qui est faite par ferir et par estraction de sanc si est faite en XIIII leus dou cors, de coi li uns est tout en som le chief;	and suction which is performed by causing injury and extraction of blood is done in fourteen places on the body, from one of which all is solid above;
et li autres est emmi le col;	and the others are around the neck;
et II autres en II costeis dou col;	and two more on the two sides of the neck.
et li ventouse desoz lou menton;	and the suction cup under the chin;
et li ventouse des II espaules;	and the suction cup on the two shoulders;
et li ventouse sus les crupies;	and the suction cup on the elbows;
et les ventouses emmi les II bras;	And suction cups on both arms;
et les ventouses des II jambes;	And suction cups on the two legs;
et les ventouses des II chevilles;	And suction cups on the ankles of both legs;
et li ventosation ne trait point de sanc, fuer que des menues voinnes que sont esparses en la char, et por ceu n’en afoiblist om mie, si com on fait de sainie de voinne;	And suction does not treat blood, for there are small veins scattered throughout the body, and because of this it does not weaken us at all, just as we do with bloodletting;
et ne covient mie qu’elle soit aministree, ne a tout feu ne sens feu, en aucune maladie qui vient de repletion, tant que toz li cors soit vuidiez.	And it should not be administered, neither with hot nor cold applications, in any disease that comes from congestion, until all the organs are emptied.
Et se par necessiteit de maladies covient ventoser, ou por acostumances, si l’amenistrons chescune houre en l’encomencement dou mois, ou en la fin, et emmi et en chescun tens;	And if suction is necessary due to diseases, or as a routine practice, we should administer it each hour at the beginning of her period, or at the end, and continuously throughout.
car il i a de telz qui, quant il ont mestier de ventoser, si ont pesant chief;	For there are some who, when they must sputum, if they weigh their head;
et si a telz qui truevent repletion et roujor en lor faice, et en lor chief, et au col, et tenebrour as eulz;	and for those who discover congestion and warmth in their face, and on their head, and at the neck, and dimness in their eyes;
et telz qui truevent une goute de sanc en lor bouche, et ont enflee la lengue, et raichent sanc;	and those who notice a drop of blood in their mouth, and have swollen tongues, and cough up blood;
et si i a de telz qui songent, et voient par nut sanc et navrez et mors et semblans choses.	and for those who think, see through their nose blood and dirt and various things.
Et quant nos voions ces signes, et meismement quant c’est emmi lou mois, nos lou commandons a ventoser aprés .iij. houres dou jor.	And when we see these signs, and especially at the beginning of each month, we command to drink after three hours during the day.
Li sainie de la muze si aide a la grieteit dou chief … que vient as eulz, et ne covient mie que ce soit aprés l’evacuation de tout lou cors;	The surgery of the nose helps with the cold in the head ... leading to eye problems, and it should not happen after the removal of everything from the body;
et ceste ventosation si est en leu de la sainie de la cephalique, et ne covient mie que cil qui est de froide complexion en use, ou qui ait chatharre, car ce lor fait mout grant nuisement;	And this suction is part of the surgery for the head, and it should not be used by those with cold constitution or who have catarrh, as it causes much harm to them;
et por ceu ne covient mie que li veillart en usent, ne qui ont ou chief froides maladies.	And because of this it is not proper for them to use it when they have cold diseases or if their head has ill conditions.
Et cil qui s’en saine sovent, si devient oblious, et por ce covient mettre la ventouse un poc plus aval par la doutance d’obliance.	And whoever uses it often becomes forgetful, and due to this, it's necessary to place the suction cup slightly further down by the suspicion of forgetfulness.
Li ventosation emmi le col est en leu de la sainie dou chief et de la basilique, et por ceu vaut elle a l’estrecement dou pis, et a fendure de la chenal dou pormon, et a toust, et a repletion;	The ventilation in the throat is located beneath the head and near the basilica. Because of this, it is beneficial for it to be narrow at the bottom, and to have an incision along the channel of the heart, and everywhere else, and for repletion;
et la covient poc bouter, car s’elle tient trop fermement, si enjanre obliance ou stomac et ou cuer.	And it should allow some pressure, because if it holds too tightly, it can cause constriction or obstruction in the stomach and heart.
Li ventosations as II costelz dou col si vaut as dolors dou chief, et obtalmie et emigrainne, et a l’estranglement, et a la dolor as racines des dens, et est en leu de la sainie de la basilique;	Ventilation in the second costal area of the neck relieves head pains, eye troubles, toothaches, and constriction, and is situated near the heart's health zone.
et covient que tu comandes au sainor qu’il espresse sa main au mettre, qu’il ne cope l’artere, et ne veigne decorremens de sanc.	And it's important that you instruct the surgeon to express their hand before operating, not to cut the artery, and not to let blood flow.
Li ventosations desoz lou menton si vaut a maladie de bouche, et a corruption de gencives, et semblans maladies qui sont en la bouche;	The ventilation around one's chin is associated with illness of the mouth, and decay of gums, and similar illnesses that occur in the mouth;
et est en leu des sainies des II levres.	and is found in the region of the healthy inner lips.
Li ventosations des espaules vaut a maladie que vient de chalor et de remplissement.	Ventilation under the shoulders corresponds to disease brought about by heat and congestion.
Li ventosations des coutes si vaut autant com des III voinnes dou bras, car elle atrait sanc de ces grosses voinnes;	The ventilation around the elbows is equivalent to three veins of the arms, for it carries blood from those large veins;
et comande au sainor qu’il ne fiere mie trop em parfont, car li leus est nus de char, et sait desoz ners et arteres.	Instruct the warrior not to overexert himself, for the lungs are exposed to air and lie near nerves and arteries.
Li ventouse qui est sus la croupe si vaut as emoroydes dou fondement, et as maladies desoz, et covient que li ventouse soit grans, et soit d’arain, qu’elle a mestier de bien traire;	The suction on the back is associated with bloody affections at the base, and diseases near it; it should be that the suction is large and made of skin, requiring good treatment;
et par aventure, s’elle estoit subtilz, si briseroit;	And by chance, if it were too thin, it would break;
et i fai grans plaies.	And I make great wounds.
Les ventouses des jambes si sainent apertement, car elles atraient sanc de tout le cors, et valent as dolors ancienes des rains, et de la marris, et de la vessie, et ramoinnent les flors;	The leg vacuums are treated properly because they draw blood from the whole body, and are beneficial for old pains in the kidneys, and the bladder, and relieve the flowers;
et sont en leu des II sophenes, et des II chevilles, et toutevoie elles afoiblissent lou cors aprés lonc us, et font venir paumison em plusors dispositions.	And they are located on the two shins and the two ankles, and still they weaken the body after long use, and lead to swelling in many dispositions.
Li maniere de mettre la ventouse si est que tu la mettes premier vuide, et succe tempreement, et la met hastanment, et remue igalment, et ne cesser de ceu faire, tant que tu voies lou leu rouge et enfleit, et apere li roujor dou sanc;	The method of applying the suction cup is as follows: you first place it empty and suck steadily, then quickly put it on and move it evenly without stopping until you see the area turn red and swell up, and notice the color change due to blood.
puis fier, et remet les ventouses, et pren warde en la disposition des cors, car il i a telz qui ont tanre char, et clers porez:	Then remove it, and reapply the suction cups, taking care with body positioning as some have tough flesh and clear pores:
si covient ferir une fois soulement, et covient faire larges plaies, et un poc parfondes;	It is necessary to strike once merely, it is necessary to make wide wounds, and a little deep.
et suce legierement.	and gently suck.
Et se li sans est gros, si couvient ferir II fois:	And if it lacks strength, it is necessary to strike twice:
la premiere fois por subtiliier la voie dou sanc gros.	The first time to subtletly open the path of large blood flow.
Et se li sans est tres espés, si covient ferir la tierce fois;	And if it lacks strength, it is necessary to strike the third time;
et quant nos volons traire dou sanc poc et poc, si nos soffist soulement une fois.	And when we wish to drain little by little from the blood, it suffices to strike only once.
Et se nos volons mout de sanc, si rencomensons sovent;	And if we wish for little of blood, then we proceed often;
et se li sans est espés, si fier em parfont, et li termines si est que li keurs soit perciez soudement, et couvient a celui qui a gros cuir et dur, et qui ont estrois porelz, que tu oignes les leus des ventouses d’oile aperitif et dissolutif:	And if it lacks strength, then pierce deeply and at the ends so that the hair is pierced suddenly; this is suitable for those with thick skin and tough flesh who have hardened tissues. You should grease their ears with suction cups from which an opening appears and one that dissolves:
se c’est en esteit, d’oile violet, ou d’oile d’amandres douces, ou d’oile de semence de cucurbite;	If it's in this state, from where it appears, or from the oil of sweet almonds, or from the oil of cucumber seeds;
et se c’est en yveir, d’oile de cresson, ou de lis, ou de camomille, ou autre semblant.	And if it's in a vein, from the oil of cress, or of lilies, or of chamomile, or other similar substances.
Et se li superfluitez est grosse et froide, si pren oile amaratin, ou de balsamite, ou oile d’anet, et les semblans.	And if the pus is large and cold, take oil of myrrh, or balsam, or anise oil, and similar things.
Et se cil cui on saine a tendre char et larges porelz, se n’i covient mettre point d’oile, mais le covient laver aprés la ventosation d’aigue rose, ou d’aigue froide, ou d’aigue de morelle, ou d’aigue de cucurbite, ou d’aigue de porcelainne, ou autre semblant.	And if for the sake of thickening flesh and large pores, there is no need to apply oil but it should be washed after the suction with rose water or cold water or water from a mulberry tree or cucumber water or porcelain water, or any similar substance.
Et cil qui a mout de moistor, si se leve d’aisil, ou d’aigue de mirte, et de sumac, et de semblans choses.	And for those who have some moisture, if they rise with it, or from wormwood water, and sumac, and similar things.
Et cil qui ont grosses superfluitez se levent de vin viel, ou d’aigue de seuc, ou de decoction d’anet ou de camomile, ou d’autres semblans;	And those with large excesses rise from old wine, or from water of sulfur, or from decoctions of nettle or chamomile, or other similar remedies;
et ne se covient mie sainier de ventouse devant le bain ne em bain, mais aprés lou bain une houre ou II;	And it's not advisable to use suction cups before or during the bath, but rather after the bath for one hour or two.
et ne dorme mie aprés la ventosacion, et covient k’il se warse, quant il se doit ventoser et quant il est ventosez.	And don't sleep after suction, it's necessary for them to bathe when they need to be sucked and when they have been sucked.
Et warde se cil qui se saine est coleriques, et se li sans est trop agus et enflamez;	And watch over him who is being healed and is hot-tempered, and let his body not become too heated and inflamed;
si covient qu’il preigne choses froides, si com pomes grenates et endives et laitues a l’aisil, et semblans choses;	It is necessary for him to consume cold things, such as pomegranate fruits and endive and lettuce in water, and similar items;
et menjuce pucins, et char de chastron, et viandes moistes.	And eat eel, and pork meat, and damp meats.
Et cil qui a froide complexion, si preigne syrop de miel, et vin odorant moien, qui est entre viel et noveil, et menjuce poc, et menjuce pucins et petis oiselz et pijons;	And for those with cold constitutions, they should consume honey syrup, and fragrant half-aged wine, which is between old and new, and eat small portions, and eat eel, and eat small birds and baby pigeons.
et lou jor qu’il se ventousera, si doit plus boivre que mengier;	And on the day he feels dizzy from lack of wind, he should drink more than he eats;
et covient doner a aucuns homes aucune fois triaicle ou muscate devant la ventosacion, ou aprés, por conforter les membres principalz;	And it is necessary to not give any men any parsley or mint before dizziness occurs due to lack of wind, or afterwards, to strengthen the main limbs;
et soit subtiliiez li sans, mais il ne covient mie que cil qui sont chaut le boivent.	And sharpen the knives but it is not fitting for those who are faint-hearted to drink.
Les ventouses que sont mises sens ferir sont celles que sont mises sus lou foie, et sus la mice, et podagre, et sus lou ventre et la boude et les rains et la hainche, car cil membre ne soffrent mie ferir sus oulz, et ne le fait on fuer que por atraire sanc de membre em membre, si com nos mettons sus les mameles quant li neis sainne;	The suction cups that are used to pierce are those placed on the liver and kidney, and in gout, and on the abdomen and stomach and lungs and hips. For this body part cannot bear piercing by needles, and one does not use force only to draw blood from limb to limb, as we place them on nipples when a baby is unable to feed.
por oster la viscositeit qui est au membre, si com nos metons ventouses sus le ventre et sus la boude por amenuisier le membre;	to thicken the blood flow in the limb, as we place suction cups on the abdomen and stomach to reduce inflammation;
et oste la dolor, quant il i a opilation ou piere, si oste par sa vertu atractive par aventure l’opilation, ou desaert la piere de son leu;	and relieves pain when there is an obstruction or stone, and by its attractive power, it may relieve the obstruction, or remove the stone from its place;
et ensi fait ele quant on le met sus lou foie et sus la mice quant il i a ventositeit retenue, et ces ventouses sont aministrees vuides por sucier tant soulement;	And thus she does it when one puts her above the liver and under the mouse when there is retained wind, and these suction cups are administered empty for suction only.
et aucune fois sont aministrees ensamble feu, et aucunes fois plainnes d’aigue tede, si com em maladies dou pleuresin, et en tel maniere c’on emplisse la ventouse d’aigue chaude soule, ou d’aigue ou il ait cuit herbes covenaubles a ceu.	And they are administered together with fire, and sometimes filled with cold water, as in diseases of pleurisy, and in such manner that we fill the suction cup with hot water or with water that has boiled herbs suitable for this.
Li forme de la ventouse aministré a feu si est ci:	The shape of the suction cup used heated like this is:
Et ait II dois de large et demi palme de parfont, et ait ou costeit entor lou mileu I petit pertus, ausi com por bouter une aguille, et soit d’arain, souef devant si qu’ele ne blece lou malaide au mettre sus lou membre;	And it has two doves half a palm wide and at the side is located in the middle one small nodule, as to place an awl, like that of an arrow, so that it does not wound the patient when placing it on the limb;
et ait em mileu une verge de travers d’arain ou de fer, por mettre une chandoile emprise, et en soient et grans et petites selonc les maladies et l’eaige de ces qui les prenent;	And in the middle is a rod of an arrow or iron to place a candlestick, and they are available in large and small sizes according to diseases and the season for those who take them;
car les ventouses des enfans sont autres que des vielz, et des maigres que des gras.	For the suction cups of children are different from those of adults, and those of skinny people are different from those of fat ones.
Et doit on ensi mettre ceste ventouse sus lou membre:	And should we place this suction cup on the limb:
empren la chandoile de cire ou I linement, et le met emmi la ventouse au traver de la verge qui est emmi la ventouse, si que li clartez soit au fons de la ventouse qu’elle ne brule le malaide;	Take the wax wick or linen thread, and insert it through the member that is in the suction cup, so that the lightness is at the bottom of the suction cup to not burn the skin;
et puis la met sus lou membre, et tes dois soit sus lou pertus que nos avons dit, si que quant on vuet, si en va li vapor, et oste on la ventouse;	and then place it on the limb, and do so either at the location we have mentioned, so that when desired, if the steam goes up, remove the suction cup;
et emprent on le linement si com devant, et le rencomence sovent, se tu as mestier.	and apply the liniment as before, and repeat it often, if you need to.
En la ventouse donques qui est aministree em maladie de pleuresin, a tout aigue, n’a point de verge ne de pertus, et n’est amenistree fuer que quant ele est plaine d’aigue, et est mise sus lou membre tant soulement;	In the suction cup that is administered in the illness of pleursin, at all aches, there is no member or location, and it is only administered fully when it is filled with water, and then placed solely on the limb;
et c’est li forme:	And here is its form:
Sansues ne sont amenistrees fuer que en membres ou on ne puet mettre ventouses por lour petitece, si com levres et gencives, et semblans leus;	Without surgery, we treat them only in limbs where suction cups cannot be placed due to their small size, such as lips and gums, and similar areas;
et en leus desnuez de char, si com doi ou neis, et autres semblans;	and on the skin of livestock, such as cows or pigs, and other similar areas;
et li qualitez de l’user si est que quant tu trueves sansues que sont en aigues douces nettes sens porreture, si les pren;	and the quality of surgery is that when you find mussels in clean fresh water without contamination, then take them;
et les met une nut en aigue douce, tant qu’elles soient famillouses, et n’aient rien en ventres;	and place them in fresh water until they become familiarized and have nothing inside their stomachs;
et puis soit sainiez de voinne et de ventouse, puis frote le membre tant k’il soit rouges, et met sus les sansues;	and then cleanse with blood and suction cups, then rub the limb until it turns red, and place them on the mussels;
et quant elles seront plainnes, et cherront, se c’est leu ou on puisse mettre ventouse, se li met, car ce vaut mout aprés.	and when they are full and they cry out, if it is somewhere you can place suction cups, then do so, because it's not much after that.
Se ceu non, si leve le leu d’aisil, et puis d’aigue, mout bien, et puis l’espreint;	If not, raise the aid of humans, and then water, quite well, and then perform incision;
et se li leus saine trop aprés lou cors des sansues, si moille I drapel de lin en aigue froide, et met sus, tant que li sans soit estenchiés;	And if the limb heals too quickly after the course of the surgical cuts, moisten it with linen in cold water, and place it there until the wound is cooled.
et se li sans est multipliez, si met sus vitriole broié, ou gales, et semblans choses, tant qu’il soit estenchiez;	And if there are multiple wounds, place powdered vitriol or garlic and similar substances on them until they cool.
ou tu met sor le leu moitiez de feves pelees, et les laisse tant qu’elles s’aerdent au leu, si estanchera maintenant;	Or you put half of peeled beans on the limb, and leave them until they heat up in the limb, thus it will stop bleeding now.
et se tu en as de plus mestier, si pren autres sansues.	And if you need more, take other wounds.
Et se les sansues ne se vuellent prendre, si frote le leu de sanc fres, ou tu i fiche une aguille tant que li sans en isse, et puis les met sus, et tantost com elles sentent lou sanc, si s’aerdent;	And if the wounds do not heal properly, rub with fresh blood or stick a needle in them until blood comes out, then place them there, and soon when they sense the blood, they will heat up.
et quant tu vues qu’elles chieent, si poudre sus un poc d’aloen et de seil broiet, ou de cendre, si cherront maintenant.	And when you see that they are bleeding, apply a powder of some aloes and flour ground, or ashes, let them do this now.
Ci comence li livre des brisures	This begins the book of fractures
Cist chapistres est maintes fois necessaires en l’art de medicine, et est restorement de brisure et de desaluement.	This chapter is many times necessary in the art of medicine, and restoring and resetting of fractures and dislocations.
Saichiez, chier fil, que li fol mire se gietent de cest chapistre, qu’il ne virent onques nul des anciens livres, ne lettre n’en lurent;	Know this, you young man, that the people of my generation throw away knowledge from this chapter, which they have never seen in any old books, nor did they ever read a letter about it;
et por ceste cause est estraingie li science en nostre terre, car je n’en trovai onques nul boin;	And because of this reason, the knowledge has been lost in our land, for I have never found anyone good;
et n’en sai nient, fuer que par la science des anciens livres, ou j’ai tant estudiiet que je en ai traite la science, et par experiment, et par l’acostumance de ma vie;	And I know nothing of it, for by the knowledge of ancient books, where I have studied so much that I dealt with this knowledge through experiments and my life's routine;
et je vos ai jai descrit en cest chapistre ceu qui est contenut, et l’ai abregié en la fin, et ai mostreit clerement les formes des estrumens que sont amenistrez, si com j’ai fait en ces II chapistres ci devant.	And in this chapter I have described what is contained here and summarized it at the end, clearly showing the shapes of the instruments that are used, as I did in those two previous chapters.
Il covient donques que nos disons ou prologue de cest livre les sommes de la parole et les chapistres ou li saiges met son entendement, et demore sus la verteit, si que cil qui sont esproveit saichent et aprenent cest art noble, et l’aprenent a autrui.	Therefore, it is necessary that we outline or provide an introduction to this book containing the essence of knowledge and the chapters where the wise person applies their understanding, staying true to reality. So that those who have experienced it may know and learn this noble art, and teach it to others.
Je dis que quant brisure ou dislocation ou torsions ou quasseure vient a aucun, si covient que tu te hastes de sainier lou malaide d’une part et d’autre, s’aucune chose ne lou te tot, si com foiblece de cors, ou enfes, ou viellars;	I say that when any fracture or dislocation or twisting or sprain occurs to anything, it is necessary for you to quickly heal the patient on one side and the other, without letting anything stop you, such as weakness of body, or infants, or elderly people;
ou se li tens n’est tres chaus, ou trop frois;	If it is too tight, or too cold;
et menjuce cholz frois, c’est a savoir froides joutes, et char d’oiseil et de chevril, et ne boive point de vin, ne menjuce nules grasses chars, et ne s’emplisse mie trop de viandes qui remplissent les voinnes de sanc, tant que tu n’aies doute d’aposteme chaut, ne d’espandement de matiere au membre;	And chew cold things, which means cold meats, and liver and asparagus, do not drink wine, nor chew any fatty meats, and do not fill up too much with meat that fills the blood vessels, until you doubt about pus formation in an abscess, or spreading of material to the limb;
si reviegne li malaides a som premerain governement k’il a useit.	If the patient recovers according to their usual regimen as they used it.
Et quant li os brisiés comence a restourer, si covient que on norrisse le malaide de viandes que font gros norrissement, ou il ait viscositeit, si com froment cuit en aigue, et ris, et testes, et piez, et pance de vaiche, et oefz, et poissons fres, et gros vin, et semblans chose.	And when the broken bones begin to heal, it is necessary that you feed the patient with meats that cause significant nourishment, or have viscosity, such as cooked wheat in water, and onions, and chestnuts, and pies, and veal spleen, and eggs, and fresh fish, and strong wine, and similar things.
Car a teil norrissement se reprent mues et plus tost li brisure.	For such nourishment leads to movement and more quickly heals the breakage.
Et saichiez que li os brisiez des vielz et des decrepites ne se pueent mie bien reprendre ne souder selonc lor nature por la sechor des membres, ne cil ausi qui sont trop tendre, si com os de petis enfans;	Know that broken bones in the elderly and those who are weak cannot be properly set or joined according to their nature due to the dryness of the limbs, nor those that are also too tender, such as children's bones.
mais n’a cure, ramoinne sus l’os brisiet I gros tenrons qui s’aert et joint le membre ensamble, tant qu’il enforce si com il fut devant;	but if there's no remedy, reset the broken bone by pushing on the protruding large ends that have been pulled apart and join the limb together, as long as it feels like it did before.
et ne li tot point de son oevre, et por ceu le covient norrir de grosses viandes, si com nos avons dit.	and don't finish his work entirely, and for this it's necessary to nourish him with large meats, as we have said.
Et saiches que les briseures sont diverses em maintes manieres.	And know that breaks come in various ways.
Car li brisure dou chief est autre que li brisure dou pis, ou de la jambe, et je vos dirai en cest chapistre toutes manieres de brisure.	For a break at the neck is different from a break at the knee or leg, and in this chapter I will tell you all ways of breaking.
Car il i a brisure que vait a arvol, et autre en aguisant, si com li taille d’une penne por escrire.	For there are breaks leading to war, and others through preparation, as with the size of a feather for writing.
Et si a brisure avec plaie, et brisure a tout une petite fendure.	And in cases of injury along with breaks, and breaks resulting from a small crack.
Et a chescune maniere ait son engien, et son estrument propre en la restauration, selonc ceu que li remembrance vient en son leu;	And for each manner it has its own tool, and its proper instrument in restoration, according to what memory brings to its place;
et est conue li brisure de l’os par ceu que li leus est tors, et apert bien par defuer, et sone au presseir de la main;	and it is known that the breaking of the bone occurs when the leg is twisted, and opens well from below, and can be felt under hand pressure;
et quant il n’i a tortuositeit ne son au tochier, et li malaides ne sent mie grant dolor, se n’i a point de brisure;	And when there is no twist or dislocation at the joint, and the patient does not feel much pain in their body, if there's no break;
mais il puet bien avoir tortuositeit, ou fendure, ou petite brisure.	But it can still have twists or cracks, or small breaks.
Si ne covient mie que tu lou mueves a la main, mais met sus medicines que vienent ci aprés, et puis l’estraint maintenant subtilment.	If it is not suitable for you to move it by hand, but apply the remedies that come next, and then gently constrain it now.
Et saiches que li brisure que vait en arvol, et sont les II parties desjointes, il les covient maintenant mettre a point igalment, ainsois que apostemes chaus i viegne;	Know that the break that occurs in the joint and divides it into two parts, now they should be placed on an equal footing, so as to treat abscesses effectively.
et se apostemes chaulz i vient, si lou laisse aucun jor, tant que li apostemes soit apaisiez;	And if pus accumulates and comes out, until the pus is relieved, let no day pass as long as the abscesses are still present;
puis le met igal au mues que tu pues legierement et saigement, et saiches que li restauration de li est plus legiere que li restaurations de celi ou il ait pieces;	Then equal it to the extent that you can do so gently and wisely. Know that its restoration is easier than restoring those with pieces;
puis l’estraint, si com il covient ci aprés.	Then he restrains, as will be fitting after this.
Et se en l’os a piéces brisies, si l’estent de II pars, se c’est mains ou piet, ou a ta main se c’est uns petis membres, ou a II cordes, ou a une corde et a ta main;	And if in the bones there are pieces broken, and it is divided into two parts, whether by hand or foot, or to your hand if it's one small limb, or by two strings, or by one string and to your hand;
et met le membre selonc sa figure natureil, si que quant les parties dou membre brisiet sont desevrees, si ramoinne par toz engiens les additions en lor leus au mues que tu pues, et garde que par ton ovraige ne viegne au malaide lesion ne doulor;	and place the limb according to its natural shape, so that when the parts of the broken member have healed, if you reset it by all means, return any protruding parts into their original positions as far as possible, and be careful not to cause injury or pain with your actions to the patient.
et ajoste bien les II chiés des os selonc les millors formes.	and adjust both ends of the bones well according to the best shapes.
Et le sent bien a la main s’il te semble k’il ne soit mie bien:	And feel it well in your hand if you think it is not quite right:
si la dresce bellement, et ne l’estraindre mie trop, ne presser si com font cil qui i font venir par lor ovraige aposteme chaut et contraction au membre, si com nos avons veut maintes fois.	If you raise it beautifully, and do not squeeze too much, not pressing as those who remove it by their work of abscess expulsion and muscle contractions do to the limb, as we have desired many times.
Et quant li membres est a point, si chastie bien lou malaide qu’il ne lou mueve, ne en veillant ne en dormant, ne en tornant, ne en autre maniere;	And when the limbs are at the right position, if you restrain well the patient so that they do not move, whether awake or asleep, when turning or in any other manner;
et warde bien que li membres soit si asseurez qu’il ne sente nule dolor.	Make sure the limbs are securely placed so that the patient does not feel any pain.
Car quant il sent nulle dolor, si n’est mie a point, et le covient mettre en teil disposition qu’il ne sent nule dolor;	But when they do not feel any pain, if it is not properly adjusted, you should put them in such a position that they do not feel any pain;
et te garde k’il soit mis droitement, que tortuositez n’i veigne quant il iert restorez;	And see to it that he is placed straightly, so that no twisting occurs when restored;
et li qualitez dou membre brisiet est selonc ceu que je te dis.	And the quality of the broken limb is according to what I tell you.
Saiches que li membre brisiet sont divers em petitece et en grandor et en forme.	You know that limbs broken are diverse in smallness and largeness, and in shape.
Car il i a petis membres, si com brais et dois et semblans:	For there are small limbs, like arms and legs and similar:
si covient envoloupeir drapelz de lin molz et subtilz;	So it is necessary to wrap them with soft and fine linen;
et cil qui sont gros, si com cuixe et jambe:	and those that are large, like the thighs and legs:
si covient envoloupeir d’un liien large et dur, car li larges liiens embraice tout le grant membre, et l’estraint de toutes pars igalment, si qu’il n’i a nule taiche;	So it is necessary to wrap them with a broad and firm bandage, because wide bands embrace the entire large limb and restrict it equally from all sides, so there is no difference;
puis lie entor estoupes legieres, III tours ou IIII selonc lou membre, et estraint ta main un poc a tout le liien, puis vai au desus de la brisure et l’estraint moins, que la brisure puis esloigne un poc la brisure;	Then bind with light bandages for the torso, three or four turns according to the limb, and hold your hand firmly on the entire bandage, then go above the break and restrict it less, so that the break can move a little away from the break;
et mollifie lou liien poc et poc, tant que tu preignes grant partie dou leu sain, puis repren I autre liien, et torne entor derechief sus lou leu brisiet;	And gradually soften this ligament a little by little, until you grasp a large part of the healthy limb, then take up another ligament, and return in an overlapping manner around the broken limb.
puis revai a la partie desoz de la brisure, et l’estraint moienement, ne mie trop fort ne trop molement, si com nos avons dit en la premiere lieure desus;	Then return to the broken part and slightly tighten it, not too hard nor too soft, just as we said in the first instance above;
puis met entre les liiens estoupes de lin ou drapelz, tant qu’il soit toz igalz, puis lie tout par desus I bendeil, et puis met tes esteles bien faites sus, s’il n’i a aposteme ou enfleure.	Then place the linen or cloth bindings between the twisted ligaments until they are all equal. Then tie everything over the bend, and then place your well-made stars above, if there is no abscess or swelling.
Et s’il i a enfleure ou aposteme, si met sus chose apaisant aposteme chaut, et qui oste l’enfleure, et le laisse ensi aucuns jors;	And if there is swelling or an abscess, place something soothing for abscesses above it, and which relieves the swelling, leaving that way for a few days;
puis estrain sus tes esteles, et soient de moitiet d’une large cainne rese saigement, ou de fust dont on fait les clives, ou de rains de palme, et soient selonc ceste figure:	Then hold onto your arrows, and they should be half the width of a slender cane cut straight or uniformly, or from a staff from which arrows are made, or from palm leaves, and follow this figure:
mais il covient que li estele que om met sus la brisure soit un poc plus grosse et plus large que les autres;	But it is necessary that the arrows placed at the break be slightly larger and wider than the others;
et soit ausi longe com il covient au membre de petitece ou de grandor;	and should also be as long as is necessary for the size of the limb, whether small or large.
puis estraint sus les esteles ausi com tu as fait a la premiere lieure, puis lie desus un fil avenanment, si com en la premiere lieure sus la briseure;	Then hold onto the arrows in the same way you did with the first trial, then tie an additional thread on top, just like you did on the first trial at the break;
plus estroit est ensus, adés moins;	Make it tighter more so, and less afterwards;
et covient que li fil soient moien, ne trop gros ne trop menus, et soient de lin mol;	And it is necessary that the thread be of medium size, neither too thick nor too thin, and made from soft linen;

For if the threads are thick, as in my works where they twist the linen cords for their loops, and that is great mistake, because the loop cannot be equal if it is too fine, and it does not suit to have less than two millimeters between each row.

And if the muscles are stretched by the bones after constriction in their joints, put over them bandages of linen or coarse wool, so they do not blister.
Quant li plaie est avec la briseure, et li keurs est rompus, je en dirai la cure ci aprés.	When a wound is bleeding and the joints are broken, I will provide the treatment below.
Et saiches qu’il ne covient mie estraindre d’esteles toz les membres brisiez le premier jor.	And know that it is not proper to strictly bind all broken limbs on the first day.

et vez ci la maniere des emplaustres anciiens por restorer brisure, dislocation, et torsion:	and here is the method of the old plastering to restore fractures, dislocations, and twists:
et est que tu pren de la farine que se tient as parois dou molin, et la confis avec abun d’uef, et met ceste confection, ne trop clere ne trop espesse, et en use, et c’est li commune maniere de l’emplaustre restorant la brisure a plusors dispositions, et meismement as femmes et as petis enfans, car il n’est mie ne trop chas ne trop frois.	And you take some flour that settles on the walls of the mill, mix it with plenty of egg, and prepare this concoction neither too thin nor too thick. Use this mixture, and this is the common way of plastering to restore fractures in various conditions, as well for women and children. There should be no concern about being too expensive or too cold.
Autre maniere d’emplastre restorans la brisure et la dislocation et la torsion:	Another method of plastering restores fractures, dislocations, and twists:
pren З abareis et ladani et enule et asefetide et gomme arabique et mugat, ana X З.;	Take saffron, garlic, nutmeg, asafetida, and Arabic gum, and add water to make it equal to X parts.

alechil VIIII З.;	Add vinegar to the mixture up to IX parts.

se li complexion de l’ome est chaude, si use de cest emplaustre, car il est de bone composition, et restoure les os brisiés hastanment, et vaut a plusors homes.	If the body's condition is hot, then use this plaster as it has a good composition and restores broken bones quickly. It is beneficial to many people.
Autre maniere d’emplaustre que vaut a torsion:	Another method of plastering that is useful for twists:

Autre maniere d’emplaustre qui restoure les os brisiez:	Another way to plaster that restores broken bones:

Autre maniere d’emplaustre a la restoration de la brisure de l’os et por amenusier lou remenant de l’aposteme.	Another method of plastering for the repair of bone fractures and to alleviate the pain caused by the wound.

Autre maniere d’emplaustre plus fors que li premier, quant aposteme dur vient a la restauration dou membre.	Another method of plastering more forcibly than the first, when hard pus comes to the healing of the limb.

Ypocras dist en son livre c’on ne mette sus lou membre brisiet por restorer fuer que cerote fait de cire et d’oile, et nulle autre chose plus, et dist qu’il soit entre dous ne trop molz ne trop durs.	Ypocras in his book states that only balm made of beeswax and oil should be applied to the broken limb for restoration purposes, and nothing else. He also indicates it should be between two substances that are neither too soft nor too hard.

Autre maniere d’emplaustre que vaut a lesion et a dolor:	Another method of plastering that is useful for injuries and pain:

si ne lou deslie par mains jors.	nor by manual adjustment later.

par cest ovraige donques cort li norrissemens au membre, et esmende hastanment ceu que font li fol mire, que restourent le membre tortement:	Through this work therefore cut the swellings from the limb, and heal it quickly as the foolish would do, that keep the member twisted:
c’est malvais, et si est ovraiges paourous, et je n’i voi autre chose que dou lassier et de l’ovrer droitement.	This is wrong, and there's no sense in this work, and I only see it as a way to rest the limb and open it properly.
des diverses manieres de brisure	Through various methods of breaking up
Maintes manieres de brisures sont, et diverses figures, et les causes sont destintees;	Many ways of fractures exist, and various shapes, and their causes are specific;
car il a brisures que sont faites de percussion d’espee, et li colz oste tout l’os jusc’a syfac qui est desoz l’os, si com fait haiche ou fust;	For there are fractures caused by the impact of a sword, and the collarbone is all bone up to the symphysis which is on the surface of the bone, as it might be done in hunting or with a spear.
et por ceu est apelee ceste maniere de briseure «haichure».	And this type of fracture is called this way because it's named "haichure".
Ou li espee cope l’os par desus sens percier, et est apelee ceste maniere de brisure «absolue»;	Or the sword hits the bone from above without piercing it, and this type of fracture is called "absolute".
et est li plaie de ces II brisures grans ou petite.	And these two types of fractures result in large or small wounds.
Et s’il i a percussion emboee, ou fendure ou de colz de piere, ou de cheoir sus piere, ou d’autres semblans.	And if there is sequential impact, or a crack or neck of stone, or through stone, or other similar occurrences.
Et s’il a brisure persant, qui aproiche jusc’a la toile qui est desoz l’os, ou elle est sus l’os, et est ceste plaie ou grans ou petite.	And if there is a break at the bone, which comes up to the membrane beneath the bone, or above it, and this wound is either large or small.
Et si a plaie qui est reponue en l’os ausi subtil com uns chevous, et est li fendure petite, et por ceu est apelee ceste brisure «capillaire»;	And if there's a wound that penetrates as finely as a hair into the bone, and it's a small crack, for this reason it is called "hairline fracture".
et si la plaie qui est faite ou par ferir de piere, ou par cheoir, ou par semblant chose, et fait entrer la piece de l’os aval, et est li leus chevez si com font li chaudelier quant il fierent sus les chaudieres;	And if the wound is made by striking a rock or falling or through some other cause, causing a piece of bone to enter from below, it's like when a candlemaker works on candles, with the heat coming from below.
si entre li piere dedens.	If between the stone internally.
Et ceu avient plus a sous qui ont ou chief moistes os, si com chief d’enfant;	And this happens more in those who have wet bones, such as bones of an infant;
et avient a toutes ces manieres de brisure que pieces menues en sont desevrees si com esteles;	It occurs in all these ways of breaking, where small fragments cause damage like thistles would;
et je em parlerai en son leu.	And I will speak about it in its proper place.
Et conoissons toutes manieres de briseures par la detraction sus elles, et l’inquisition a tentes, et par la char corrumpue qui est sus.	And know all ways of breaking through extraction from them, and investigation with attempts, and through the corrupted matter which is upon them.
Li semblance capillaire est conue par ceu que quant on a descovert l’os, et on frote enche sus, si apert li brisure noire.	The appearance of hair is known by this: when one has exposed the bone and rubs it together, then the dark fracture opens.
En la cure de la brisure, pren garde as accidens dou malaide, et se tu vois nul malvais accident, si com vomissement de cole, et amission d’entendement, et estension, et paumeson, et fievre ague, et les eulz issir fuer et rougir, et autres semblans em plusors dispositions, si ne puet saner sens doute.	In the treatment of fractures, be vigilant about maladies and if you see no adverse event such as vomiting bile, loss of consciousness, stretching, swelling, fever ague, and if the eyes emit and turn red or other similar symptoms in various conditions, it cannot be healed without doubt.
Et se tu ne vois accident espoantauble, et tu esperes salut, si comence la cure.	And if you do not see an alarming occurrence, yet still hope for recovery, then begin the treatment.
Et quant li navrez vient premier a toi, et c’est en yver, si covient oster l’os devant lou quatorzime jor au mues que tu pues.	And when the nose comes to you first, and it's in winter, it is fitting to remove the bone before the fourteenth day after the month you could.
Et se c’est en esteit, si te haste d’oster l’os devant lou septime jor, ainsois que li toile desoz l’os soit corrumpue, et vienent li accident que nos avons dit.	And if it's in summer, hasten to remove the bone before the seventh day, so that the pus under the bone becomes infected, and the accidents we have said occur.
Et se li brisure de l’os vient jusc’a la toile que cuevre lou cerveil, si covient que tu fendes la partie fendue ensi:	And if the break in the bone reaches the tissue that covers the brain, it is necessary that you cut through the fractured part like this:
et est que tu preignes lou chief dou malaide navreit, et descuevre sus l’os en toutes les manieres que tu pues, et sus la figure de la plaie plus souef que tu pues, et se decorrement de sanc vient au descovrir l’os, ou aposteme chaus, se li aide de ceu qu’il covient, et est que tu emplisses lou leu de drapelz moilliez en oile roset;	And if you take hold of the bone that is not attached and uncover it on the bone in all the ways you can, and with the appearance of the wound as much as you can, and if blood discharge comes to uncover the bone or an abscess, assist according to what is necessary, and then you should fill the gap with wet cloths in olive oil;
et fai reposer la plaie tant que li apostemes chaus soit apaisiez, et soies asseurez de decorrement de sanc;	And let the wound rest until the pus lesion is calmed down, and ensure there is proper drainage of blood;
puis comence entor l’os a oster, et c’est fait selonc II manieres d’ovraige:	then begin to work towards the bone, and this is done according to two ways of working:
l’une manieres si est que tu copes au taillement estroit devant, et c’est li forme:	one method is that you prepare for a narrow cut in front, and this is the form:
Et puis i boute .i. autre taillement plus grant que lou premier.	And then make another cut of about double the size of the first one.
Et li seconde maniere si est que tu aies nombre de taillemens divers, les uns estrois et les autres larges, et soient a pointe, et soient de fer inde;	And the second method is that you have several different sizes of cuts, some narrow and others wide, and they should be pointed, and made of iron;
et en oevre legierement, que tu ne bleces le chief.	and work gently, so as not to hurt the head.
Et se li os est fors et durs, si covient que tu lou perces entor, ainsois que tu i aministres taillemens avec tareres, ne mie parfont qu’il ne percent outre l’os dou test, et doit avoir desus la pointe une marge ou I cercle, que ne laisse passer la pointe outre l’os;	And if the bone is hard and solid, it is necessary to pierce through it, in such a way that you perform cuts with prongs, not all the way through so as not to penetrate beyond the bone beneath the testicle, and there should be above the point a margin or a circle, which prevents the point from passing beyond the bone;
et t’en covient avoir plusors, si que chescuns viegne en son leu de l’espés de l’os, si que tu aies tareres por toz test;	And you must have several of them, so that each comes into its place in the middle of the length of the bone, so that you may have holes for all your tests;
et c’est li forme des III manieres de tareres:	And this is the form of three kinds of holes:
Li qualitez por percier entor l’os brisiet est que tu mettes I tarere sus l’os, et torne a tes dois tant que tu saiches que li os est perciez;	The quality for piercing through the broken bone is that you place one hole on the bone, and turn with your hands until you know that the bone is pierced;
puis remet lou tarere autre part un poc aprés, et ensi fai tout entor, puis cope as incisoires l’espaice de l’os qui est entre les pertu, et fai ceu plus subtilment que tu pues, et legierement, si com nos avons dit, tant que tu en traies l’os a ta main, ou a aucun des estrumens que tu as si com tenailles, pinceures;	Then put the hole elsewhere a little later, and do this all around. Then cut through the space of the bone that is between the teeth, and do it more finely than you can, gently, just like we said, until you bring the bone to your hand, or with none of the tools you have such as forceps;
et garde que tu ne touchier au cerveil ne au syfac.	And beware not to touch the brain or the spinal cord.
Et quant tu avras l’os perciet, et trait, si couvient que tu reses l’apreteit qui est demoree de l’os a tout I autre estrument semblant a un incisoire, mais il covient qu’il soit plus tenves et plus subtilz que li autre incisoire;	And when you have pierced and treated the bone, if it is fitting that you prepare what has remained from the bone to all other instruments resembling an incisor, but it should be more robust and finer than the other incisors;
et s’il demore rien des petis os, ne nulles escailles, si les oste legierement a I des estrumens;	and if there remains nothing of the small bones, or no scales, you should gently scrape with the instruments;
puis cure la plaie de tentes et d’oignemens que nos avons dit.	then treat the wound from the sides and dressings that we have mentioned.
Et li autre maniere d’ovraige si est cil que Galiiens dist, qui est plus saus;	And another method of treatment is as Galen said, which is more harmless;
et le loa molt fort, et c’est sa parole.	and the heat must be very strong, and this is his word.
Il covient premier que tu descuevres une partie de l’os, lai ou li brisure apert mues, si que quant tu avras descovert celle partie, si metras desoz lou chief de cest incisoire lenticulaire, de coi ci est li forme:	It is necessary first to uncover part of the bone, where the break opens and moves, so that once you have uncovered that part, you will place under the tip of this oblong incision, which has this form:
Et ne trenche mie d’une part, et est li partie ague en II costez, si que li trenchans est devers l’os;	And do not cut from one side alone, and let the part be divided into two sides, so that the cutting is towards the bone;
puis fier d’un petit maillet sus, si que tu copes legierement l’os tout entor, et te done bien en garde de la toile que est desoz;	then strike on with a small hammer, so that you gently press the entire bone, and be well aware of the cloth which is nearby;
s’elle est aerse a l’os, si l’oste legierement, car on l’oste bien sens nuisement, et sens paor.	If it's close to the bone, gently press the bone, because bones are very sensitive and can cause pain.
Et se li brisure de l’os ne perce jusc’a la toile, et li os est copez tant soulement par desus, et il i a petites pieces, si couvient rere celle asperiteit, et oster les escailles au raseur subtil dont tu dois avoir diverses quantitez, por amenistrer en chescun leu le plus covenauble, selonc l’ovraige et la figure de la brisure.	And if the bone break doesn't go through the membrane, and only part of the bone is cut above, with small pieces remaining, after smoothing that area it is necessary to remove the scales using a fine shaver you must have in various quantities. To apply the most suitable for each place according to the work and the shape of the break.
Si reis devant de grant raseurs, et aprés de plus subtilz, et ne cesser de ceu faire tant k’il soit bien.	When facing large shavers, then proceed to finer ones, and never cease this practice until it's done well.
En chescune des autres tailleures capillaires et brisure subtil, covient que tu amenistres cause selonc son adrecement;	In each of the other hair-cutting tasks and delicate breaking operations, it is necessary that you handle according to its orientation;
et c’est chose que n’est mie reponue a celui qui a mis son estude en cest art.	and this matter cannot be handled by someone who has not devoted their study to this craft.
Et se li syfac est descovers, si covient que tu preignes I drapeil de lin, selonc la quantiteit de la plaie, et le moille en oile roset, et le mete sus la plaie;	And if the soft spot is discovered, it is necessary that you use linen strips according to the size of the wound, and apply the oil generously, then place it on the wound;
puis pren I autre drapeil doublé en II ou en III, et le moille en vin et en oile roset, et le met sus le premier drapeil;	Then take another cloth doubled up as one likes, and mix the grease with wine and oil rose, and put it on the first cloth;
et fai ceu plus legierement que tu pues, que tu ne grever lou syfac, puis aministre par desus I autre liien, et ne l’estraindre mie fuer que tant k’il teigne la plaie soulement;	And do this more lightly than you can, so as not to weigh down the scab, then administer it over another bandage, and do not pull it with too much force until it only touches the wound.
et le laisse ensi I jor ou II, tant que li apostemes chaus soit apaisiez, puis le deslie, et i aministre medicines si com racines de lis, et farine de veces, et poudre d’encens, et aristologe, et semblans choses;	And leave it like this for one or two days, until the abscess becomes calm, then remove it, and administer medications such as lily roots, bran of thyme, incense powder, and garlic, among similar things;
et de ces choses fai poudre, et met sus la plaie, et i aministre adés medicines mondefians sens mordication;	And make a powder from these things, put it on the wound, and administer medications that do not cause irritation.
et warde que li plaie soit adés nette, que tu n’i laissier mie l’oignement, ne n’i laissier mie assembler bowe, car quant bowe s’asemble sus la toile dou cerveil, si la corront et porrist, et avient au malaide grans malice;	And ensure that the wound is completely clean, do not leave any pus, nor let it assemble in the socket, because when the ball assembles on the brain's mesh, it will run and resist, causing great mischief to the patient;
car quant on met sus lou syfac chose mordant, si nercist par desus.	for when one places something sharp above oil, it sears from above.
Pren warde donques, se nulz mavais accidens vient au malaide, si com nos avons dit, si est doutable sens doute.	Therefore, take heed, if no accidents befall the patient as we have said, if it is doubtful, then there should be no fear.
Et se noiror n’i vient fuers que por la medicine c’on a mise sus, que teil vertu ait, si covient que tu preignes une partie de miel, et III parties d’oile roset et en glue I drapel, et lou met sus lou syfac;	And if it only comes out as part of the medicine we've applied, assuming that such virtue has been exerted, then you should take a portion of honey and three parts of rose oil and one spoonful of glue, and apply this mixture to the ointment.
puis lou cure de manieres de cures qu’il couvient, tant qu’il soit sanez.	Then continue with the appropriate treatment until it is healed.
Saiches que aucune fois sont brisies les II parties dou neis desus, ou li une par li soulement, car ce sont II os;	Know that neither of the two parts above the nose are broken, or just one of them alone, for these are two bones;
et cil desoz est cartillaginous, et ne brise mie, si ne fait fuer k’enbower ou tordre, et puis saine.	And this one is cartilaginous tissue, it does not break, nor does it allow for twisting or bending, and then heals.
Et se l’une des II parties est brisie, si covient que tu boutes ton petit doi ou pertus dou neis, et met igal cele brisure dedens a ton doi indice, et au pouchet par defuer, tant que li neis reveigne selonc sa figure natureil;	And if one of the two parts is broken, it is necessary for you to pinch your little finger or the tip under the nose, and place the break equal within your index finger, and at the bottom towards outside, until the nose regains its natural shape.
et fai ce legierement, et warde que li malaides ne sente dolor par ton ovraige.	Do this gently, and make sure that the patient does not feel pain through your work.
Et se li brisure est en la partie desus lou neis, et ne puet venir li dois au leu, si couvient que tu lou mettes igal au chief d’un rait un poc gros.	And if the break is in the part above the nose, and cannot come to his nose, then it's necessary that you place him level with the head of a rod a bit thick.
Et se li brisure est de II pars, si refai autretel, et te haste de restorer lou premier jor, se tu pues;	And if the break is in two parts, redo this procedure, and try to restore the first day's work, if you can;
se ce non, aprés lou septime ou le disime, quant li apostemes chaus est apaisiez, puis bouthe au chief dou neis tentes de drapelz de lin, se li brisure est en une partie.	But if not, after the seventh or eighth day, when the abscess is calm, then pinch near the nose to where the linen fabric begins, if the break is in one part.
Ou tu boutes I autre d’autre part, se li brisure i est;	If you pull on one part of something from another side, then it breaks there;
et soient les tentes si grosses qu’eles emplissent les pertus dou neis.	And let the tents be so large that they fill out the hollows in the nose.
Et dirent aucun restorour c’on doit moillier les tentes em burre, et muer chescun jor.	And they say that when restoring one must smear the stumps with butter, and change each day.
Il ne me semble mie que ce soit bien, mais covient qu’elles soient moillies en confection d’aubun d’uef, et de poudre de molin;	I don't think it's quite right, but they should be moistened in the preparation of a mixture from an egg and powdered pepper;
puis laisse la tente, tant que li os soit fers, et li cartilaiges endurcis.	Then leave the tent until the bone is hard and the cartilage toughened.
Et aucune fois boute on ou neis pennes d’oie en leu de tentes, et si a I souef drapeil entor, et se tient la briseure, et soffle li malaides parmi;	And once bound, or goose feathers instead of tents should be used in the place of them, and if it's done upside down, and holds up well, and withstands the wind, and blows the patient inward;
or fai lou kel ke tu vues.	Or do as you see fit or as you have observed.
Et se apostemes chaus vient au neis tandis com tu i oevres, si i met cerote ou coton moilliet en oile roset, ou en .i. poc de dyaquilon.	And if pus comes out through the nose as you are working, then put moistened lint or cotton in oil mixed with rose water, or a spoonful of almond oil.
Et se apostemes chaus n’i vient, si met emplastre par defuer, de farine de sisament, et de poudre d’encens, confites avec aubun d’uef, puis met sus estoupes legieres, et ne liier mie lou neis;	And if abscesses do not come out, then apply a plaster to the surface, made of sifted flour, and incense powder, mixed with yolk oil. Then place it on light bandages, but do not tie them too tightly.
et se li brisure dou neis est petite, et il est brisiés em menues pieces, si l’estrai as estrumens covenables a ceu, puis cout la fendure, et la cure de choses enjanrans char, et soudant, si com emplastres et oignemens covenables a ceu;	And if the nose break is small, and it has broken into small pieces, then use tools suitable for this task when extracting. Then cut along the wound, and clean out the damaged material, and suture, using plasters and remedies suitable for this situation;
et s’il n’a dedens lou neis nule plaie, si lou cure de tentes, et i met cainnes de plonc, tant qu’il soit sanez.	And if there is no injury within the nose, then treat it with the usual methods, and apply snail shells until they heal.
de la routure de la mandibule	On the rupture of the jawbone
Quant li mandibule est route desoz, et il n’i a point de plaie defuer, et li brisure est defuer tant soulement, et n’est mie brisiez en dous, fuer que corbelz dedens, si le conoist on legierement.	When the jawbone is broken outwards, and there is no wound outwardly visible, only the break is outwardly present, not being split into two parts externally but cracked internally. If one knows this lightly.
Il covient, se li brisure est en la destre partie, que tu boutes ton doi indice en la bouche dou malaide;	It is necessary, if the break is in the right part, that you bend your ring finger into the mouth of the patient;
et se li brisure est en la mandibule senestre, si boute ton doi indice de la main destre, et boute la brisure dedens legierement, et l’afaite a l’autre main par defuer, et met igal.	And if the break is in the left jawbone, hold your right hand's index finger and gently force the break inside, and execute it with the other hand from outside, apply evenly.
Et se li brisure de la mandibule est desevree en .ij., si covient que tu aministres extension de .ij. pars, tant qu’il soit igalz.	And if the breakage of the jawbone is split into two parts, it should be treated with an extension of both hands until they are even.
Et se commovemens des dens avient, ou routure, si les estrain d’un fil d’or ou d’argent ou de soie, puis met sus la mandibule brisie cerote, et met sus I drapel double;	And if the teeth are moving or a fracture occurs, then use a thread of gold, silver, or silk to hold them in place. Then place a paste on the broken jaw, and put a double layer of cloth over it;
et met sus lou drapel une grant estele bien faite, ou une piece de cuir igal, longe et large selonc la mandibule, et la lie sus au mues que tu pues, et comande a malaide qu’il se repose, et menjuce viandes legieres.	And place on the cloth a large, well-made plaster, or an equal piece of leather, long and wide according to the jawbone. Fix it at the parts you can attach it to, and instruct the patient to rest, and eat light meats.
Et se tu vois que li figure se chainge, si le deslie au tier jor, et puis remet a point ceu que c’est chaingiet;	And if you notice that the shape changes, if it dislocates on the third day, and then correct whatever has changed;
et met emplaustre sus, de la poudre dou moulin avec abun d’uef ou farine de sisament, aprés ceu que tu as osteit lou cerote;	And apply plaster upon it, mix with powder from the mill along with abundant egg or meal of ground almonds, after you have removed the wax;
et met sus l’emplaustre lainne legiere, et se li emplaustres s’aert, et li disposition dou malaide ne se chainge, laisse le tant k’il soit sanez;	And place a thin layer of plaster, and if the plaster cracks, and the position of the wound does not change, let it stay until it heals;
maintes fois est sanez en III semainnes.	Many times it is healed within three weeks.
Et se apostemes chaus vient, si amenistre ceu que nos avons dit maintes fois.	And if it comes to incision at the foot, then apply what we have instructed many times.
Et s’il i a brisure et plaie ensamble, rewarde se nule piece de l’os en est ostee;	And if there is a fracture and wound together, remove no part of the bone when it is broken;
si subtilie de l’oster as estrumens covenaubles a ceu.	Such subtlety in the extraction requires instruments suitable for this task.
Et se li plaie est estroite, si l’eslarge a flaime selonc ta necessiteit.	And if the wound is narrow, enlarge it with fire according to your need.
Et quant tu avras ostees toutes ces pieces, et il n’i demore nule, si cout la plaie, s’ele est large, et met sus .i. des emplaustres covenaubles a ceu, por enjanrer char, tant qu’il soit sanez.	And when you have removed all these pieces and there remains none, if the wound is wide, place one poultice suitable for this over it to encourage flesh growth until healing occurs.
de la forcele	by the strength
Li forcele brise plusors fois devant, devers l’espaule, et li brisure si est selonc III manieres:	The broken force breaks many times forward towards the shoulder, and the break follows three ways:
ou elle est brisie et desevree en II, et i a pieces, et est li plus legiere a restorer;	When it is broken and dried out in two parts, and there are fragments, it's more easily restored;
ou il i a brisure avec plaie.	There is breakage with injury.
Et li ovraiges si est quant li brisure est sens plaie, que tu aies II ministres, si que li uns teigne l’ajutoire que sent la forcele brisie;	And the operations in such cases are when there is breakage without injury, that you have two assistants, so that one marks the shoulder where the strength is broken;
et li autres estende lou col vers la partie;	and the other extends the neck towards the affected part;
puis met igal la brisure a tes dois, si que li forme soit si com il covient, et n’i ait ne apparance ne chevement.	Then place the breakage evenly on your hands, so that the shape is as it should be, and there should be no appearance or movement.
Et se tu a mestier de plus estendre, si met desoz l’espaule au malaide une spere reonde de drap, ou de lainne, et soit grosse selonc ta necessiteit;	And if you need to extend more, then place a round sponge of cloth or wool under the shoulder for the patient, and it should be as large as your necessity requires;
et estent et lieve la forcele, et estraint le spere a ta main, si que tu mettes igal la brisure, si com il covient.	And apply gentle force, hold the pole by your hand, so that you make an equal breakage, as it should be.
Et se tu ne pues traire le chief de la forcele au defuer, por ceu qu’elle vient em parfont, si covient que li malaides gise sovin sus son hatereil, et met desoz l’espaule .i. oreillier moien, et boute li ministres l’espaule aval, tant que li os de la forcele soit levez.	And if you cannot draw the head of the force to the outside due to it coming forwards, then the patient should lie with their head on their shoulder blade, and place a pillow under one shoulder. The attendant should hold the shoulder down as long as the bone of the force is raised.
Et puis adrece la brisure a tes dois, et se tu lou trueves debrisiet, si covient que tu fendes sus;	And align the break with your fingers, and if you find that it's splitting, then it should be to split from above;
et trai fuer les pieces legierement, et se li os ne puet joindre por aucun sormontement, si le cope a l’un des incisoires que tu as;	And pull the pieces gently, and if the bone doesn't join for any pushing, then you should correct it towards one of the incisions you have made;
mais que tu mettes desoz la forcele cest estrument, por warder lou syfac:	but place the full force of that instrument, to avoid this slip:
et semble une cuiller, et n’est mie chevez, et soit ausi large com il lou covient, selonc la grandor de l’os et la possance de l’uevre;	and make it seem like a spoon, not too thick, and be as wide as it should, according to the size of the bone and the strength of the operation;
et ait II chiés, si com tu vois, et soit li uns larges, et li autres estrois, si com est li routure de la plaie que tu as fait quant tu as trait les os;	and have two heads, as you see, and let one be wide, and the other narrow, as is the wound you made when treating the bones;
et quant tu es asseurez d’aposteme chaut, si cout la plaie, et se li routure est petite, ou tu doutes aposteme chaut, si emple la plaie de drapelz et de tentes, selonc sa quantiteit.	And when you are assured of the removal of pus, if you clean the wound, and if the rupture is small, or if you doubt about removing pus, then dress the wound with cloths and tents, according to its quantity.
Et se apostemes chaus i vient, si moille .i. drapel en oile roset et en aisil et en vin, et met sus.	And if there are incisions from them that come out, if moisture one, apply oil and rose water and wine, and place it on top.
Li estrignement de l’os, quant il est sens plaies et sens tailleure, est que tu mettes sus l’os l’enplaustre de la poudre dou molin et d’aubun d’uef, et met estoupes legieres sus, et met une spere desoz l’assele, se tu en as mestier;	The grinding of the bone, when it involves injuries and surgery, is that you place on the bone a plaster made from the powder of the mill and some yolk of egg, and lay lightweight bandages over it, and put a sponge under the wound if needed;
puis pren une tres grant bende d’une palme de large, puis met I drapeil double sus estoupes, et l’emplaustre;	Then take a very large bandage, about the size of your palm in width, then place the cloth over the bandages, and plaster it;
puis pren une estele subtil de III dois de large et de lonc, et l’envoloupe entor celui bendeil, si que li chief dou bendeil soient pendant;	Then take a narrow strip about three fingers wide and long, and wrap it around the bandage, so that the ends of the bandage hang down.
et met l’estele sus la briseure, et torne le bendeil sus lou col, et desoz l’asselle sainne, et desoz l’asselle malaide;	And place the candle near the wound, and turn the stick upwards to the neck, and over the healthy ear, and over the diseased ear;
et la ramoinne de chescune partie, et quant tu vois ke li lieure tient la briseure avenanment, et tu vois clerement que li estele ne se muet desus l’os brisiet, si le rewarde chescun jor, et quant li liiens eslaiche, si lou restraint;	And reset each part; and when you see that the heat touches the wound's opening, and you clearly see that the candle does not move over the broken bone, then reward yourself every day, and once you remove the bandage, then keep it restrained.
et fai gesir lou malaide sus son dos, et li met quant il dort I petit orillier desoz l’assele, por lever l’ajutoire en haut;	And let the disease flow out on his back, and place him when he sleeps with a small pillow under the ear, to lift the shoulder up;
si aligera li brisure de la forcele par l’aligement de l’espaule, ou tu li lie lou bras au col, et ne lou desliier se malvais accidens n’i vient, jusc’a XX jors;	And relieves the pressure of the muscles by aligning the shoulder, or you tie his arm to the neck, and do not untie it for fear of bad accidents until 20 days;
puis rencomence l’emplaustre, se tu vois qu’il en ait mestier, et l’estraint et le laisse ensi, tant qu’il soit restorez;	Then renew the plastering, if you see it needs it, then hold and keep it like that until it is restored.
et elle est restoree au plus en XXVIII jors, et en moins a aucuns homes.	and it is restored by the utmost within 28 days, and in no cases beyond that time limit.
de la brisure de l’espaule	From the breaking of the shoulder
Poc avient que li espaule brise ou large leu ne em mileu, et ne lou seit on fuers que par lou touchement;	Sometimes the shoulder breaks or is damaged at its ends or in the middle, and if only one part seems to have been affected by a touch;
si l’apareille selonc la figure de la brisure, et la ramoinne selonc sa forme natureil, en toutes les manieres que tu pues;	if you adjust it according to the shape of the break, and reset it according to its natural form, in all ways that you can;
puis met sor le leu poudre dou molin avec abun d’uef, et estoupes legieres, et met sus I drapeil double;	then apply on the shoulder powdered flour from the mill with plenty of eggs, and make gentle compresses, and place a doubled bandage on top;
puis met sus une estele large et subtil, un poc plus large de l’espaule, et se desoz l’estele est chevemens en aucun leu de l’espaule, si emple celle cheveure d’estoupes de lin, si que li estele siece igalment;	then place a broad and fine straw, slightly wider than the shoulder, such that within the straw there are no movements in any part of the shoulder; if the straw is wet with linseed oil, so that the straw conforms evenly.
et puis l’estraint a tout une grant bende fermement, si que li estele ne se mueve de son leu, et regarde le liien chescun jor;	And then holds it firmly into a large bend, so that the limb does not move from its place, and checks each connection daily;
et toutes les fois k’il amolist, si l’estraint, et met igal l’estele s’elle est fuer de son leu, et gise li malaides sus son costeit;	And each time it is realigned, if it is held firmly in place, and makes the limb equal if it is not displaced from its position, and has the patient lie on their side;
et li espaule est restouree en XX jors ou en XXV.	And the shoulder is restored in 20 days or in 25.
Et quant cist nombres est acomplis, si le deslie, et soies seur, car ce n’est mie os qui se mette fuer legierement.	And when this number is completed, if it is released and you are sure, because it's not an easy task of bone to be placed lightly.
Et se une piece de l’os tent avant, et point desoz lou keur, si fent sus, et l’oste, et fai ceu que nos avons dit en la brisure de la forcele d’apaisier aposteme chaut.	And if a piece of the bone is exposed and not covered with skin, then it should be handled like an abscess from a broken wrist, and you do what we have said about treating a wound in the first chapter.
de la brisure dou pis	From the break of the foot
Li peis est aucune fois brisiez em mileu, mais ce avient poc;	The arm is broken only once in the middle, but this happens rarely;
mais il brise sovent au defuer.	but it often breaks at the elbow.
Et quant il est brisiez emmi, si decline au desoz, et sent li malaides grant dolor, et faute d’alainne, et toust, et par aventure vomist sanc, et apert li chevemens en l’os brisiés, et lou sent om bien.	And when it is broken within, if it descends towards the knee, causing great pain to the patient, lack of strength in the legs, and dizziness, and occasionally vomiting blood, and reveals the opening inside the broken bone, and you will well understand.
Et li restoracion si est que li malaides gise sovin sus son dos, et li met I cussin entre les espaules, puis presse les espaules, et li assemble les costes des II costelz a tes mains, et subtilie dou mettre igal a toutes les manieres que tu pues, tant que li figure de l’os soit si com il covient;	And in the restoration if allowed, when the patient is lying on their back with their arms at their sides, and I place my thumbs between the shoulders, then press the shoulders together, and align the ribs of the second ribcage with your hands, delicately adjusting them to match all possible ways that you can adjust them, until the shape of the bone is as it should be;
puis met sus emplaustres et estoupes desus l’estele subtil de salz, ou d’autre fust legier, et l’envoloupe en I drapeil, et la lie sus l’os brisiet, si qu’elle ne se mueve;	Then place them on the plaster and cover the delicate salt bed, or another light wood, and wrap it in a piece of cloth, then bind it to the broken bone, so that it does not move;
et torne le liien reondement au dos, et l’estraint avenanment, et rewarde chescune houre la liure, et s’elle ramolist, si l’estraint;	And twist the bandage around the back, and tighten it diagonally, and reward each hour with the string, and if it relaxes, then tighten it;
et s’il lou covient desliier, por corrosion ou por prurite que vient au leu, ou dolor ou aposteme, si te haste, et lou deslie, et raie l’emplaustre, et adresce ceu qui i est venus de manieres de cures;	And if it is necessary to move it due to corrosion or itchiness that comes to the body, or pain or abscess, if you must hurry, and remove this, and smear with ointment, and treat as usual for those who have come in need of cure methods.
puis ramoinne l’emplaustre, et l’estraint tant qu’il soit sanez.	Then remove the plaster, and keep it steady until it has healed.
de la brisure des costes	Of the breaking of the ribs
Saiches que li briseure des costes ne vient fuer que en leus gros aprés le dos, et au chief dedens, et ne ploient fuer que por ceu qu’eles sont glairouses;	Know that the breaking of ribs only comes about in their large parts behind the back, and within, and they bend because they are soft;

et alaine a poinnes, et toust et vomist grant planteit de sanc, et c’est de grief santeit, et li ancien i ont mis grant engien.	And to points, all at once and instantly produces large amounts of blood, and this is harmful for health, and the old ones have used extensive means.

toutevoie, doutance i a que li ventouse n’atraie les superfluitez au leu por la disposition de foiblece.	However, there is doubt that the suction cup draws away excesses towards the body due to its weakness.

And then one must cut into the bone, and drain lightly, and then sew the two edges of the wound if it is large, and dress with plasters until they heal.

de la brisure dou col	Of the breaking of the neck
Aucune fois vient briseure as os dou col, et poc avient k’il ploie;	Never break bones in the neck region, and nothing should cause them to bend;
et ausi a l’espinee dou dos.	And likewise along the spine of the back.

de la brisure de l’os de la hainche	From the breaking of the bone in the hip
