de la brisure de l’ajutoire	of the breaking of the shoulder
Li adjutoires est ceu qui est entre lou coute et lou chief de l’espaule, et s’il est brisiez, si le doit on restorer selonc l’une des II manieres:	The assistants are those that lie between the knife and the head of the shoulder, and if they are broken, should one restore it according to one of the two methods:
dont l’une est que tu pren I fust plain de moiene groissor, selonc ceste forme:	One method is that you take one thickened stick, according to this shape:
Et lie as II chiés II liens, et les pent en haut, et siece li malaide sus I siege;	And fasten the two heads with two strings, and place them up high, and have the patient sit upright;
puis li giete som bras brisiet sus le fust, tant qu’il viegne a l’aissele, et ait em mi une corbeure de fust, puis pent sus aucune pesant chose ou li ministres l’estende aval;	Then place his broken arm on the staff, until it reaches the elbow, and have half of a staff's length in your hand, then can ascend onto any heavy thing or let the attendants extend him downwards;
puis mette li mires la briseure igal a ses mains ensamble, tant que li briseure retorne si com il covient.	Then set the injury equal to both his hands together, until the break returns as it should.
Et li autre maniere si est que on sovine le malaide sus son hatereil, et li lie la main a son col, puis comande a .ij. ministres que li uns teigne ceu qui est sus la briseure a ses mains, et li autres teigne desoz a tout .i. liien, et estende chescuns a sa partie.	And the other method is that one arranges the wound on their buttocks, and ties their hand to their neck, then instruct two attendants that one shaves where there's a breakage at their hands, and the other removes from each side up to half an inch, and extend each person to their respective sides.
Et se tu vues que li estraction soit plus fors, si estraint I liien desoz la briseure, et sus la briseure, et estende chescuns des ministres a sa part.	And if you see that the extraction is more forceful, hold to the bandage across the wound, and above the wound, and extend each of the ministers to their share.
Et se li briseure est prochiene au chief de l’espaule, si covient que tu mettes I liien moien desoz l’assele, et I autre vers lou coute, desoz la briseure;	And if the break is near the top of the shoulder, it must be that you place one half of the splint at the elbow and the other towards the knife, over the break;
et ausi se li briseure est devers lou coute, si i covient mettre I liien legierement, sens labor, tant que li briseure soit igalz sus lou leu, et sus lou coute;	And similarly if the break is towards the knife, it must be to place one half lightly, without effort, until the break is equal on the side and on the knife;
puis met igal la brisure, si com il covient, et l’estraint, se apostemes chaus n’i vient.	Then make the break equal, as it should be, and restrain it, if abscesses do not come.

et met le drapeil, et estraint sus l’ajutoire, et sus lou bras, si que li bras soit en leu d’esteles, s’aucune chose ne le te deffent, ou se li os n’est muez. Et se tu doutes que li os ne se mueve, si use d’esteles, et met sus la brisure une estele plus large et plus fort des autres, et ait entre chescune estele I doi d’espaice, et soit chescune estele si grans qu’elle passe la briseure III dois de chescune part;	And if you doubt that the bone isn't moving, use braces, and place a larger and stronger brace over the injury compared to the others, with one inch of space between each brace. And make sure each brace is as large as it can be while still allowing passage for three inches on both sides of the injury;
puis estrain sus les esteles, ensi com j’ai dit au comencement dou chapistre sus la briseure, plus fort et moins en aloignant.	Then hold onto the stumps firmly, as I said at the beginning of this chapter on bruising, more forcefully and less by pulling away.
Et se tu vois l’assise des esteles, et l’estrignement, si com nos avons dit, en l’oure que tu restoures le membre brisiet, et tu doutes l’aposteme chaut, si le laisse a liier jusc’a septime jor, si com nos avons dit;	And if you see the stump of the stumps and the tension, as we have said, during the time you are restoring the broken limb, and if there is doubt about the abscess swelling, leave it bound until seven days, as we have said;

Et se nulz telz accidens n’i vient, si ne lou desliier fuer que aprés III jors ou plus, et dorme li malaides sus son dos, et ait ses mains sus son stomac;	And if no such incidents occur, or if it is not released until three days or more later, and let the patient lie on his back, and have his hands on his stomach;

de la brisure du bras	"Of the breaking of the arm"
Li bras est compos de II os, qui sont apelez li dui «foscile», de coi li uns est petis, et est cil qui enseut le pouchet;	The arm is composed of two bones, which are called the 'fossicle', from one of which the lesser bone is smaller, and it is this that supports the elbow;
et li autres est grans, et est cil qui est desoz, devers lou petit doi;	And those are large, and this one is on the ground, towards the little knee;
par aventure brise li grans foscile soulement, ou li petis, et par aventure andui ensamble.	By chance it may only break the large bones, or the small ones, and by chance they may come together.
Quant li petis fosciles est brisiez, li restaurations est legiere, et li sanations;	When the small bones are broken, the recovery is light, and the healing;
et quant li grans est brisiez, si est li sanation male, et plus griés que quant il sont brisiez andui ensamble.	And when the large bones are broken, the healing is bad, and more painful than when they break together.

de la brisure de la main	Of the breaking of the hand
Saiches que au dos de la main et as nous des dois avient poc de briseures, et n’i vient mais que ploieure maintes fois.	You know that on the back of the hand and with us the bones suffer little breaks, and no more than bend many times.
Et quant li plante de la main est brisie ou ploie, si covient que li malaides siece croisiet, et siet droitement devant lui igalement;	And when the hand is broken or bent, it is necessary that the patient keep their arm straightened and aligned directly in front of them;

et soit envoloupee en I drapeil de lin.	and be wrapped in an I cloth of linen.
Et se li briseure est au pardedens entor lou ventre de la plante, si fai une spere de drapelz, et comande au malaide qu’il l’estrigne a sa plante brisie;	And if the splinter is at the heel between the front of the foot and the belly, make a poultice from linen, and instruct the patient to press it onto their broken heel;
et puis l’estrain d’un lonc drapeil, et soit li estele de keur souef ausi grans com li plante de la main, et l’estraint, si com il covient.	and then press with a long linen cloth, and make the poultice as thick as the heel of the hand, and press it, as it should be done.
Et se li brisure est au defuer, si covient que tu mettes une estele sus, et une autre desoz en la plante, si que li mains soit overte et droite, puis le lie tot entor la main, et estanche lou liien entre les dois.	And if the break is at the front, it should be that you place a splint above and another underneath in the foot part, so that your hand is opened and straight, then bind them entirely around the hand, and seal off the connection between the fingers.
Et se li briseure vient a aucun des nous des dois, se c’est li pouchés, si le met igal, si com il covient;	And if the splinter comes to neither of your toes, it's embedded, so place it evenly, as it should be done;
et l’estraint avec la plante, et se tu vues si met une estele droite petite por lever la briseure, et ne se mueve;	And he holds it with his foot, and if you see that placing a small stick straight upward eases the pain, and doesn't move;
et se li brisure est as autres dois, si com en l’indice ou l’un des autres, si le met igal, et lou lie avec lou doi sain qui est aprés;	And if the pain is felt on other fingers, such as in the index or any of the others, place it evenly, and secure it with a healthy finger that comes next;
ou tu les lie toz en I tenant, que mues vaut, ou tu met sus une estele, si com ou pouchet;	or tie them all together in an "I" shape, that one is enough, or place them on a stick, like when you have a walking stick;
et pren warde en la restauration et en la disposition d’aposteme chaut, et secor ceu qui i vient, si com j’ai dit.	and always take care in the restoration and positioning of each incision, and support those that come next, as I have explained.
de la cuixe brisie	Of the broken thigh
Li os de la cuixe est maintes fois brisiez, et bien le voit on quant elle torne devant et derrier;	The bone of the shin is often broken; and one sees it well when it turns in front and behind;
et li restauration si est c’on lie I liien desus la briseure, et I autre desoz.	And for its restoration involves securing it above the fracture, and the other below.
Et li malaides gise sus sa faice, puis estende chescuns ministres son lien a sa part igalment;	And the sick lie on their face, then extend each minister's connection to its equal part;
et c’est quant li brisure est emmi l’os.	And this is when the fracture is within the bone.
Et se li brisure est prochiene a la racine de la cuixe, si soit li uns des liiens devers lou poignil, et li autres liiens desoz la briseure.	And if the splint is close to breaking at the base of the foot, then one should direct some of the straps towards the knife and the other straps beneath the splint.
Et ausi s’elle est prochiene au genoil, et adonques soit li liens delez lou genoil, et soit li extension aval;	And similarly if it's close to the knee joint, then place its connections above the knee joint, and allow its extension downwards;
puis mette li mires l’os igal a ses II mains, tant qu’il soit selonc sa figure natureil, et puis met l’emplaustre, et lou lie, se apostemes chaz n’i vient.	Then place the sights of the bone equally with his two hands, as long as it follows its natural shape, and then apply the plaster, and the bandage, if abscesses do not come about.
Et s’il i a aposteme chaut, si le laisse apaisier puis revien a ton ovraige et a ta cure;	And if an abscess appears then let it heal and return to your work and treatment;
li lieure est faite en teil maniere.	The birth is performed in this manner.
Il covient que tu envoloupes sus la briseure I bendeil dur doublé en II ou III, et en demoure li superfluitez, puis torne la jambe tant que li talons veigne a la racine de la naige, et boute I fil lonc entre la cuixe et la jambe, delez lou genoil desoz, et veignent li chief dou fil au desus;	It is necessary that you wrap around the wound with strips of leather doubled in two or three layers, and retain the excess. Then bend the leg until the heels reach the base of the shin, and place one thread longitudinally between the knee and the leg, beneath the knee, and guide the end of the thread over the top of the head.
puis torne sus la jambe et sus la cuixe le bendeil, puis met sus la briseure esteles, et met une estele sus l’os de la jambe;	Then bend the bandage upwards on the leg and on the knee. Place pins on the wound, and place a pin on the bone of the leg;
puis emple le leu vuit entre la jambe et la cuixe de drapelz souef por mettre igal l’estrignement, puis comence a liier forment III tors ou IIII sus la briseure;	Then use five threads between the leg and the knee of the same material to ensure equal tension. Then start binding in a form of three or four turns around the wound;
et quant plus vas en sus de la briseure, et moins l’estraint;	And when you go further than the incision, and do not restrict it less.
puis enten as II chiés dou fil que tu as bouteit entre la jambe et la cuixe, et en lie III esteles que sont desus, puis revai au desoz au chief dou fil, tant que tu veignes delez le piet;	Then take two threads from the bundle that you have held between the leg and thigh, and secure three pins above them. Then return under the thread at the tip of the thread, as long as you see beyond the foot;
et l’estraint, si qu’il ne se mueve de son leu, puis le laisse ensi, puis k’il n’i vient ne aposteme ne enfleure n’autre semblant.	And hold it so that it does not move from its place, then leave it like this. Then if there is no pus or swelling or any other indication, it should be left as such.
Et s’il i avient, si le deslie, et adresce ceu que i vient, si com nos avons dit maintes fois;	And if there does occur something, loosen the thread and address whatever comes about, as we have said many times;
et se il i a pieces de l’os que poigne, si le covient ewer, s’om puet;	And if there are pieces of bone that are caught, then it is as one should do, if one can;
et s’on ne puet, si covient fendre le leu, et traire fuer;	And if one cannot, then it is necessary to cut the limb, and drain the blood;
et le cure si com nos avons dit, tant k’il soit sanez.	And treat it as we have said, until it becomes clean.
Et aucune fois est brisie li cuixe ensi c’on i met esteles, si com en l’ajutoire et ou bras;	Every once in a while, the cook should add garlic inside the cut if one puts them during the process, as in the shoulder and arm;
toutevoie, en la restauration ensi faite ne cloche mie li malaides.	Nonetheless, after such preparation, there is no complaint from the patients.
Et saiches que li cuixe est restoree en .l. jors, ou poc moins ou poc plus, selonc les diversitez des complexions.	Know that the egg is restored in one day, or somewhat less, or somewhat more, depending on the diversity of body types.
de la ruelle dou genoil	from the garden alley
Saiches que en la ruelle dou genoil avient poc brisure, mais elle ploie maintes fois.	Know that in the knee joint there is some cracking noise, but it bends many times.
Et s’elle brise, si n’est mais c’une fendure, ou I pertus, et avient a tout plaie, et sens plaie, et ce sent om bien.	And if it breaks, except for just a crack, or if it wears out, and affects all injuries, and feels like an injury, and this is felt very well.
Et li restauration si est c’on mette igal ceu qui est rons a ses dois, tant qu’il soit assemblez mues c’on puet;	And in this preparation, one should put what burns well on its parts until all can move as they should.
puis met l’emplaustre, et i met une estele reonde, se tu en as mestier, et l’estraint si com il covient, puis rewarde toutes les dispositions que nos avons dit ens autres briseures, si com aposteme chaut et autre semblant;	Then apply the plaster, and if necessary, put a round bandage, and tighten it as needed. Then reposition all other preparations we have mentioned for other injuries, such as pus-filled abscesses and similar things.
si met a chescun accident ceu k’il li covient, tant qu’il soit sanez.	If you meet with each incident as it suits him, while he remains sound.
de la brisure de la jambe	of the breaking of the leg
Saiches que en la jambe ait II os, de coi li uns est apelez par droit non «mustelz», et li autres est apelez «foscile»;	Know that in the leg there are two bones, from which one is called straight by right "tibia", and the other is called "fibula".
et avient tout auteil briseure com il vient au bras, et por ceu est li restauracion si com celle dou bras igalment, et li ovraiges est tout i. Et se li dui os sont brisiet ensamble, si torne li jambe de toutes pars.	And any damage or injury that occurs in the arm happens here too, and because of this, the restoration process is similar to that of the arm, uniformly applied, and it involves all aspects. If both bones are broken together, then the leg turns in every direction.
Et se li os subtilz est brisiez, si torne devant.	And if the delicate bones are broken, then turn in front.
Et se li gros os est brisiez, si sent on grant dolor, et le voit on bien;	And if the large bone is broken, one feels great pain and can see it clearly;
et torne desoz.	And it turns inward.
Adonques amenistre extension, et le met igal, et lie les esteles igalement;	Therefore, apply the extension and make it uniform, and secure the pins uniformly;
mais toutevoie, il covient se li brisure est laide, et il i a plusors pieces, que li extension soit menor et plus legiere;	However, nevertheless, if the fracture is ugly, and there are more than a few parts, then the extension should be gentler and of less force;
et l’alige selonc ta vertu.	and align it according to its virtue.
Et quant tu as tout acomplit ton ovraige, si pren II faixes de fust chevees que porpreignent la jambe d’une part et d’autre, et soient dou lonc de la jambe des le genoil jusque desoz;	And when you have completed all your work, take wooden splints that can be rubbed onto the leg on both sides, and let them be as long as from the leg to the knee down.
puis envoloupe en II leus I bendeil desus et desoz, et le lie em mileu ausi, et a ceste lieure ne pora li jambe decliner a destre ne a senestre, et ensi est bien;	Then wrap two bandages around the ends of each splint, both above and below them, and tie them in the middle as well. Also during this time, make sure the leg does not bend to the right or left, and thus it will be done properly.
et aucun i aministrent I bers dou lonc de la jambe, et s’est de fust, et i met on la jambe por warder de movement, et proprement fait on ceu en la brisure ou il a plaie;	And no one administers anything from the length of the leg, and it is made of wood, and you put the leg to rest in order to avoid any movement, and this is properly done where there is a wound during the fracture.
et remue chescun jor la jambe, por veoir s’il i a aposteme chaut n’autre accident;	And move each leg every day to see if there is pus or any other incident;
si le cure tant qu’il soit sanez.	if the treatment continues until it becomes clear.
de la brisure des os dou piet	From the breaking of bones due to injury
A la cheville ne vient point de brisure, mais as os dou piet vient aucune fois brisure et as dois poc, et n’i avient fuer que quassure em plusor dispositions.	Ankle injuries do not come from breaking bones, but rather due to certain positions that the feet can be in, and there is only strength when in multiple dispositions.
Et s’il avient as os dou piet brisure, et tu vois ces os sormonter l’un l’autre, si mette si malaides som piet sus la terre, ausi com s’il voloit aler, et puis met maintenant ton piet sus lou sien, lai ou li os sont levez, puis le presse tant k’il reveignent en lor leus;	And if it happens to the bone with a fracture, and you see these bones rising upon each other, place your hand on the earth like the bone would want to go, and then put your foot on his foot, where the bones are raised, press it so much that they regain sensation in their limbs;
puis met l’emplaustre et estoupes sus, et met desoz lou ventre dou piet une petite tauble a II chiés plains, puis l’estraint au piet avenanment, puis que tu as envoloupez drapelz entor, et autres choses dont tu as mestier.	Then apply the plaster and wrap it up, place a small table of two full shoulder boards under his foot, then squeeze him onto the board in the appropriate position, then when you have covered him with blankets and other things you need.
Et quant .iij. jors ou .iiij. seront passez, si deslie lou liien, car tu troveras les os igalz, soient brisiez, soient desaluez.	And when three or four days have passed, if you release the bandage, because you will find that the bones are even, whether broken or dislocated.
Et s’il i a aucuns des dois brisiez, si les restoure, si com nos avons dit as dois de la main;	And if any of the two bones are broken, repair them, just like we have said about the bones of the hand;
puis met au doi brisiet une estele selonc la longesce dou doi, et soit un poc plus large, puis met desoz le piet celle tauble que j’ai dit, et l’estrain avenanment;	Then place the bone fragment with an angle according to the length of the bones, and make it slightly wider; then put under it the plate that I said, and tighten it diagonally.
et s’il en i a II ou III, ou plus, brisiez, si met sus chescun doi une estele selonc sa quantiteit, envoloupee en I drapeil de lin, et estraint la tauble desoz lou piet;	And if there are two or three or more, and they are broken, place on each one a fragment according to its quantity, wrapped in one layer of linen, then tighten the table under it.
et soit estans sus lou chief de la tauble defuer lou ventre dou piet, si qu’il le teigne bien.	And stay on top of the table above the stomach of the plate, so that it presses well.
Et covient que tu n’oblier mie les autres choses que j’ai dit as autres briseures, des que nos avons dit;	And you must not forget the other things I've said about other breaks, once we have discussed them;
et secor chescun accident si com il covient.	And assist every incident as it should.
de la brisure de l’os dou poignil	regarding the breaking of the bone in the hand
Quant li os de la nature la femme est brisiez, si la fai seoir enlargie, puis l’encline a la partie dou dos, et soit tenue par derrier;	When the bone of nature in a woman is broken, if she is made to stay enlarged, then she is inclined towards the lower back area, and held from behind;
puis emplisse li baile la nature de la malaide de couton, et en i mette ausi gros com I sto;	Then fill the void of nature with cotton, and also place it as large as necessary;
puis deboute la femme, et lieve lou dos poc et poc, et adonques saut li coton, tant qu’il vient a l’entree de la nature, et revient li os avec lou sto;	Then stand the woman up, and gently lift her back little by little, and then jump the cotton until it reaches the entrance of nature, and return the bone with this action;
et quant elle vuet pissier, si oste lou coton, et quant elle a pissiet, se li remette, et ensi faice VII jors ou entor:	And when she wants to urinate, if you remove the cotton, and when she has done so, have her rest again, and do this for seven days or about that time.
si sera restoree li brisure, et se tu vues, pren une vessie de berbis, et lie au pertus une cainne, et boute toute la vessie en la nature;	If the break is healed, and if you see fit, take a goat bladder, tie it at its opening with a rope, and fill the whole bladder inside nature;
puis soffle en la cainne forment, tant que li vessie soit enflee dedens:	Then blow on the fire rod until the bladder is inflated inside:
la nature si revenra li brisure;	The nature will return the break;
puis soit emplie de coton, et le laisse ensi aucuns jors, tant qu’il soit sanez.	Then fill it with cotton and leave it like that for some days until it heals.
Et quant li os dou poignil de l’ome est brisiez, ou de la femme, si le restoure ensi com nos avons dit en l’os de la hainche;	And when the bone of the elbow or knee of a man is broken, or in a woman if it's left like we have said about the hip bone;
et ne sont mie occultees ces briseures prochienes a celui qui i met son estude et son us, et entent mon livre.	And these nearby fractures should not be overlooked by someone who devotes their study and use to it, and listen to my book.
Car li brisure li signifie em plusors dispositions la droite voie de la restauration:	For the break means in many positions the right way of restoration:
enten le donques.	Understand it then.
En la verge, quant elle est brisie, pren une gorge d’oie et i boute la verge;	In the case of a broken penis, take an ointment from a goose and apply it to the affected area;
puis envoloupe drapelz entor, et le laisse III jors ou enqui entor, et il sera sanez hastanment.	Then wrap it with bandages around, and leave it for three days or until the wound has healed, and it will heal quickly.
de brisure avec plaie	Of breaking with injury
Il covient a celui qui a brisure avec plaie, meismement s’elle est grans, si com li os de la cuixe ou de l’ajutoire ou semblant, qu’il soit sainiez maintenant, si que les sainies que nos avons dit le tesmoignent.	It is necessary for the one who has a break with an injury, even if it's large, as with bones of the wrist or shoulder blade or similar, that they be now treated, so that the treatments we have mentioned testify to.
Et se li plaie saine, si la restainche de vitriole, se tu n’as autre chose, puis rencomence a restorer la briseure en cele meisme houre, ou celui jor, se apostemes chaus n’i vient.	And if the wound has healed, you should reapply vinegar, and if there's no other remedy, then start restoring the break in the same hour or day. If abscesses occur, apply them immediately.
Et se apostemes chaus i vient, si laisse la restauration jusc’a nuevime jor, tant que li apostemes soit apaisiez, et n’i touchier ne au tier jor ne au quart, car tu i feroies venir malvais accident.	And if abscesses occur, allow the restoration up to a new day, until the abscesses are pacified. Don't touch them on the third or fourth day, for you would bring about bad accidents.
Et se li os brisiez est aparans sus lou keur descovert, si covient que tu lou mettes a point legierement a tes mains, a extension petite.	And if the bone is broken and visible through the uncovered thigh, it must be gently placed with your hands, in a small extension.
Et se li extensions ne t’est apareillie por mettre igal a tes mains, si le ramoine a cest estrument qui est de fer, qui a VII dois ou VIII de lonc, et li largesce est selonc la quantiteit de la plaie;	And if the extension does not allow you to make it equal with your hands, then use this iron tool if you have it, which should be seven or eight inches long, and its width should match the size of the wound;
et por ceu est mestier au mire qu’il empreigne III ou IIII, selonc ceu qu’il en ait mestier en chescune cure de briseure;	And for that, the surgeon must insert it three or four times, depending on how many times he needs to do so in each fracture treatment;
et soit rons et un poc gros, k’il ne ploie mie a la compression sus lou membre a ton ovraige, et soit agus devant, et gros des le mileu en avant, ensi:	And make it round and a little thick, so that under the pressure on your limb when you are opening it up, it does not bend at all, and have roughness at the front, and be thick in the middle ahead.
Et est apelez «palainche», por coi il covient que li chiés corbes soit mis sus lou chief de l’os apparent;	And it is called "palainche", because it must have the crooked head placed on the top of the visible bone;
et le boute a une fois, tant k’il reviegne, et soit igalz l’un encontre l’autre.	and beat it once, until it regains consciousness, and ensure that each side is equal against the other.
Et se li brisure est subtilz, et li estrumens ne puet bien prendre l’os, si covient que tu copes lou chief de l’os, tant que li estrumens en ait possance.	And if the break is subtle and the instruments cannot properly take hold of the bone, it is necessary that you grip the top of the bone as long as the instruments have control.
Et se tu ne pues ramener l’os, si com nos avons dit, si lou cope d’un estrument covenable a ceu, ou incisoire ou soieure, a ton pooir;	And if you cannot bring the bone back, as we have said, using a suitable tool for this purpose, such as an incision blade or awl, with your strength;
puis reis ceu qui est demorez en l’os d’aspreteit et de menues escorces.	then rub the one that is stuck in the hard bone and small scabs.
Et quant li os est ramenez, et li malaides sent grant dolor aprés, saiches qu’il n’est mie en son leu natureil.	And when the bone is returned, and the patient feels great pain afterwards, know that it has not been placed in its natural position.
Si fai tant qu’il soit en son leu, puis moille I drapeil en vin stiptique noir, et proprement se c’est en esteit;	Do it until it is in its place, then moisten the wound with black vinegar and properly if it is in health;
et ne mettre mie sus la plaie cerote ne autre chose ou il ait oile, qu’il n’i faice venir porriture et corruption;	and do not put wax or any other thing over the wound that could cause gangrene and decay;
puis aministre esteles quant tu as restoreit l’os, et laisse la plaie descoverte, et cope la coverture tout entor, selonc la quantiteit de la plaie, et te done bien en garde que li plaie ne soit estrainte avec la brisure;	After administering these treatments when you have restored the bone, and leave the wound open, and cover it completely according to the size of the wound, and make sure to protect that the wound is not strained with breaking.
et maintes fois ont ce fait li fol mire, et ont fait venir sus le malaide ou mort ou corrodent aucune fois;	And many times this has happened to the foolish patient, and there is no occasion where they have caused death or corrosion on the body.
et soit li estrignemens plus molz et plus souef des autres brisures.	And may the crushing be softer and more effective than other breakages.
Et se li plaie est male ou grans, et tu doutes que mavais accidens n’i veigne, si com nos avons dit, et tu trueves dolor au leu, si n’i covient mie mettre sus esteles;	And if the wound is deep or large, and you doubt that past accidents have caused it, as we said, and you find pain in the limb, then it would not be appropriate to apply these treatments;
mais envoloupe entor, en leu d’esteles, drapelz durs, et les lie.	But instead of applying these treatments, wrap the area tightly, and secure it with hard bandages.
Et quant tu vois aprés I jor ou II enjanrer bowe a la plaie, si oste ceu que tu as mis sus a tout vin, et i met oignement sanant plaies, si com oignement tetrafarmaçon et semblans.	And when you see after one or two days that the wound has begun to heal, remove what you had placed with all the wine, and apply a healing ointment for wounds, such as the four-formula ointment and similar.
Et covient que tu deslies lou membre .ij. fois le jor, lou matin et au vespre, tant qu’il soit soudez et sanez.	And you must dislocate the limb twice a day, in the morning and at vespers, until it is united and sound.
Et covient que li membres soit aparilliez en teil maniere que li bowe corre aval legierement.	And it should be that the limbs are placed so that the wound heals in such a way that the bone comes together lightly.
Et se maint jor trespassent, et il ne puet souder mais rent adés bowe, saiches k’il i a petites pieces d’os, por coi il covient que tu quieres la plaie avec tente, et oste toutes ces pieces desevrees que font venir celle dolor.	And if the days pass and it cannot heal otherwise than at once with the bone, know that there are small fragments of bone, which is why you should work on the wound with traction, and remove all these unnecessary pieces that cause pain.
Et se fistule vient au leu, ou autre maniere de corruption, si covient que tu le cures, selonc ceu qu’il dist en son chapistre ci devant.	And if a sinus appears in the head or any other form of infection, it is necessary to treat it according to what he instructs in the chapter mentioned earlier.
Et quant li os est brisiez, et apert sus lou membre, si com li os de la cuixe ou de l’ajutoire, et autres semblans des grans membres, si ne le traire mie, car maintes fois en vient li mors, mais le laisse tant qu’il porrisse;	And when the bone is broken, and opened on the body part, like the bones of the elbow or shoulder, or other similar large body parts, if you do not treat it immediately, for many times death results from this, but let it until it heals.
par aventure cherra par lui aprés XX jors ou XXX, puis cure la plaie, se tu pues;	By chance, it may heal on its own after 20 days or 30 days, then treat the wound, if you can;
et se tu ne pues, si la laisse.	And if you cannot do so, leave it as it is.
des brus qui vienent sor la sodure	The blows that come from sweat
Nous vienent maintes fois aprés la santeit de la briseure, meismement quant c’est pres de la jointure, et laide chose est a veoir li figure dou membre;	Many times after the healing of the bruising, especially when it is near the joint, comes a difficult thing to see in the figure of the limb;
et par aventure ne puet faire li membres ses ovraiges naturelz.	And by chance, the limbs may not be able to do their natural tasks.
Pren warde donques se li nous est fres:	Therefore, take care when it is fresh:
si li aministre medicines stiptiques, si com aloes, encens, et mirre, et sarcocolle, acaice, et semblans autres, ensi que tu preignes aucune de ces choses, ou toutes ensamble, et les confit avec vin stiptique ou avec abun d’uef ou avec aisil;	If he administers strong medicines such as aloes, incense, and myrrh, sarsaparilla, carob, or similar others, you should use any of these substances alone, or all together combined, and mix them with a stomatic wine, or an abundance of egg white, or honey.
et les met sus le nout en estoupes, et l’estraint bien, et ne la desliier en mains jors;	and place them on the wound as poultices, and bind it well, and do not loosen it with your hands during the day;
et puis la desloie, et rencomence une autre, tant que li nodations soit ostee;	and then reposition it, and start another poultice treatment until all the swellings have subsided;
ou tu estrain sus une piece de plonc bien faite;	or you bind with a well-made piece of plaster;
car li proprietez dou plonc si est qu’il oste toutes les enfleures desus les membres;	because the properties of plaster are such that it relieves all swellings on the limbs;
et se li nodation est ja convertie en durteit ausi com piere, et il est besoing de l’oster, si la cope desus, et fent la superfluiteit apparent;	And if the dislocation has already become like stone hard as a bone, and it is necessary to extract it, even when cut open, then remove the excess that becomes noticeable.
ou tu la reis a aucun raseur, tant qu’ele soit ostee, et la cure tant qu’ele soit sanee.	Or you would take it out at no small cost, until it is extracted, and the treatment until it is healed.
dou membre qui est foibles aprés la garison	The limb that is weak after a siege
Quant li brisure de l’os est restoree, et demoure aprés li membres foibles et subtilz, si avient por mout de causes:	When bone fracture repair is restored and after that the limbs remain weak and subtle, if this happens due to various reasons:
de coi l’une est por ceu qu’il fut liiez trop estroit, et ne fut mie liiez si com il covenoit;	Of which one is because it was tied too tightly and not tied as it should have been;
ou por ceu qu’il i ot trop de liiens, et ne pooit venir li norrissemens au membre;	Or because there were too many ligatures, and the movements could not come to the limb;
ou por multitude d’arosement;	Or due to an abundance of bleeding;
ou por trop grans movements, ne mie en son houre;	for too great movements, not at their time;
ou por ceu qu’il a poc de sanc en son cors, si est foibles.	because they have little blood in their body, if they are weak.
Et li cure si est que tu faices mengier le malaide, et faire le cors tendre, tant que li sans soit multipliiez en lui;	And the treatment is that you feed the sick, and make the body tender, until the pus has multiplied in him;
et li aministre bain, et li done joie et liesce;	and he administers baths, and gives him joy and delight;
puis met poix sus le membre, si que li poix atraie a li grant norrissement, et l’arose sovent d’aigue tede, tant que li norrissement corre au membre;	then put grease on the limb, so that the grease attracts to the large artery, and frequently washes it with tepid water, until the bleeding corresponds with the limb;
et reviegne a sa figure natureil.	and restores him to his natural appearance.
dou membre tort aprés la santeit	If the member is twisted after recovery.
Quant li membres est tors aprés la restauration, et li os brisiez apert, et li forme dou membre est laide, toutevoie ne pert mie son ovraige natureil:	When the limb is twisted after restoration, and if the bone is broken openly, even though the form of the limb may be ugly, it does not lose its natural substance:
si ne croire mie les folz qui dient c’on doit brisier lou membre tout de noveil, et maint fol mire ont ce fait en nostre terre;	If you do not believe those who say one should break the limb entirely anew, and many a person has done this in our land;
et cist ovraiges est blamez, et en vient grans malz, et par aventure li mors;	And these actions are criticized, causing great harms, and indeed death befalls the person.
toutevoie, se li nodations et li torture sont fres, si covient k’il soient arosez d’aigue chaude, ou herbes mollifians soient cuites, si com foilles de vismalve, et racines, et mellilote, et semblans choses;	Nonetheless, if the nodations or tortures are fresh, they should be treated with hot water, or by cooking soothing herbs, such as leaves of marjoram, roots, and clover, among other similar things;
et li fai I emplaustre mollificatif, si com dyaquilon bien fait, et tu pren le muscillaige de vismalve, et la confit avec graisse de geline ou oile de sisament, et fai emplaustre sus;	And make an application of a soothing paste, such as well-prepared duck fat, and take marjoram's extract, mix it with fat from geese grease or saffron oil, and apply this paste.
ou tu pren figues graisses, et les broie avec fien de colon, et semblans medicines que amenuisent le soudement.	Or take dried figs, grind them with cow's dung, and similar remedies that alleviate inflammation.
Et aucune fois est ostee li nodacion por froter continuelment et longement a mains moistes.	And never let the dislocation occur by rubbing constantly and for long periods with wet hands.
Et soit amenistrez movement au membre chescune houre.	And allow some movement in the limb every hour.
Et se li tortuositez est enveillie et endurcie, ausi com piere, et besoins est de l’oster au fer, si la covient coper jusc’a l’os, a l’incisoire subtil legierement;	And if the hardness and stiffness have developed and become like bone, so it is with stones, and requires removal by the iron tool; thus, if necessary, one must cut up to the bone, carefully and slightly in the delicate incision.
et mettre cusenson et estude en la cure.	and apply attention and study to the treatment.
Ci encomence li livres des dislocations	This begins the book of dislocations
Dislocations est issue d’aucune jointe de son leu, por coi il ne se puet muevre, et est li membres mal figurez, et sent li malaides grant dolor et grant lesion.	Dislocation occurs when a joint moves out of its place, because it cannot move then, and the limb is misaligned, causing great pain and injury to the patient.
Quant dislocation vient a aucun, si le covient maintenant ramener sens targier.	When dislocation affects none, if it suits now to bring back without hesitation.
Car s’on tarde, si enfle li leus, et par aventure si le remet on a poines au leu;	For if one delays, they swell the limbs, and by chance they reattach to the bone in their current position;
por ceu ne covient mie c’on le mueve a l’oure k’il est enflez:	for heaven forbid that one should move it at the time when it is swollen:
maintes fois fait venir spame et autres dolors;	often bring about discomfort and other pains;
toutevoie, quant ce avenra, si fai sainier lou malaide, puis le laisse, tant que li apostemes chas soit apaisiez;	however, when this happens, if you make the patient see a surgeon, then let them rest until all the abscesses have subsided;
puis arose le membre d’aigue chaude et d’oile, puis le ramoinne legierement, et cure chescun membre si com li cure venra en son leu.	Then apply the member of hot water and oil, then gently remove it, and treat each limb as if its treatment comes naturally in place.
Et j’ai ordenez les chapistres des dislocations des lou chief jusc’a piez.	And I have ordered the chapters on shoulder dislocations up to this point.
des mandibules	of the jaw
Poc avient que les mandibules soient desaluees andous, et li dislocations d’ambedous est selonc II manieres:	It often happens that the jaws are dislocated backwardly, and the dislocations of both occur in two ways:
ou elles sont un poc ostees de lor leus, et mollifies un poc;	or they have a slight stiffness at their joints, and become slightly softer;
ou elles sont desaluees entierement, et pendent vers lou pis, et cort li salive de la bouche qu’il ne la puet tenir, ne ne puet clore sa bouche, et envoloupe sa langue avec la parole.	or they are completely dislocated and hang towards the back, causing saliva from the mouth to spill out that they cannot contain it, nor can they close their mouth, and their tongue wraps around with speech.
Quant li dislocations est petite, si revient par li em plusors disposicions.	When a dislocation is small, it can return through various positions.
Et s’elle est entiere et acomplie, si covient que tu la ramoinne hastanment, et ne targier mie;	And if it is complete and accomplished, you should reset it quickly without hesitation;
et en tel maniere que li ministres teigne le chief dou malaide, et boute li mires som pochet de l’une de ses mains en la racine de la dislocation de la mandibule dedens la bouche, se li dislocations est de II pars;	and in such a way that the attendants cut the head near the injury, and push the pins of his pocket into the root of the jaw dislocation inside the mouth, if the dislocation is on two sides;
et li autre doi des mains soient defuer, por mettre igal;	And let the other hand's fingers be spread out, for setting things equal;
et comande au malaide qu’il les amollisse, ses mandibules, et les mueve de toutes pars.	And instruct the patient to soften them, his jawbones, and move them in all directions.
Et li mires la mete igal, tant qu’elle reveigne en son leu.	And hold the thumbs in place until they settle back into position.
Et se li ramener est griés, meismement se ce sont les II mandibules ensamble, si les arose d’aigue chaude et d’oile, tant que les ramoinnes legierement;	And if it hurts when he returns them, even if they are the two jawbones together, if they are immersed in hot water and oil, as long as you gently reset them;
ne ne targier mie dou ramener, si com nos avons dit.	Do not hesitate to return them, as we have said.
Et quant elles sont ramenees igalment, et li bouche dou malaide clot bien sens mollifiier, si met sus drapelz moilliez en cerote fait d’oile roset et de cire, puis le lie legierement de molz liiens;	And when they are returned equally, and the mouth of the patient closes well with softening, then place it on wet cloths in a poultice made of oil rose and wax, then gently bind it with moist bandages;
et dorme li malaides sus son dos, et ses chiés soit estans entre II cussins, si qu’il ne lou mueve ne a destre ne a senestre, ne ne s’efforce mie de maixier, mais preigne legiere viande, tant que les dolors soient ostees, et soient noees les mandibules;	And let the patient sleep on their back, and keep their head between two cushions, so they do not move left or right, nor strain at all, but only eat light meat, until the pains are relieved, and bind the jawbones;
et puis menjuce ce qu’il vuet legierement, et ne se travaille mie d’ovrir la bouche au mengier et au boivre, tant que li mandibule soit bien noee et sanee.	And then test it to see if it can be moved lightly, and not allow any opening of the mouth for eating or drinking until the mandible is well healed and healthy.
Et se les .ij. mandibules ne pueent estre remises a point a une houre, et ne sont mie converties a lor leus, si en vient fievres et sode acostumees, et par aventure solution de ventre, et par aventure vomist cole pure.	And if the two jaws cannot be placed in their proper position within an hour, and are not returned to them, it leads to fevers that become habitual, and at times abdominal pain, and at times vomiting of clear contents.
Et quant tu verras ceu, adonc saiches que c’est perdicions;	And when you see this, then know that it's destruction;
et maintes fois muert cil cui il avient, en VIIII jors.	And many times, death has befallen the one to whom it happened, within nine days.
de la forcelle	from the forceful (context unclear without more information)
Li forcele ne puet desaluer dou costeit dedens la continuation de li et dou pis, et est desaluee aucune fois au defuer, et bien le sent on.	The forces cannot relieve the pain from within the body's continuity or from its backside; it can only be relieved once outside, and this is clearly felt.
Et li restauration si est que li malaides gise sovin sor son dos, et estende ses bras;	And the healing is that the patient lies supine on their back, and extends their arms;
et puis presse le leu forment a ta palme, et elle revenra;	And then press the body shape to your palm, and it will return;
puis met sus l’emplaustre et lou bendeil, et l’estraint;	Then place on the plaster and the bandage, and tighten;
et li chiez qui est devers lou coute ne puet desaluer;	And the head which is towards the knife cannot be moistened;
se poc non, et se il desalue aucune fois, si le ramoinne a son leu, si com nos avons dit;	If it's not dislocated, and if it does dislocate once, then reset it to its place, as we have said.
puis met sus l’emplaustre et le bendeil, et l’estraint, et coumande au malaide qu’il se repose tant qu’il soit sanez;	Then apply the plaster and bind it tightly, and secure it. Instruct the patient to rest until their wound has healed.
et ensi meisme est ramenez li chiés de l’espale, quant il est desevrez de son leu.	And similarly, bring back the shoulder blade when it is dislocated from its place.
de la dislocation de l’espaule	Of the dislocation of the shoulder
Saiches que li espaule n’est desaluee fuer que selonc III manieres:	Know that the shoulder is dislocated according to three methods:
de coi l’une est qu’ele desalue a la partie de l’assele au desoz;	The first method is when it dislocates at the part of the humerus under the axilla;
et li seconde est a la partie dou pis;	And the second type is when it dislocates near the base;
et par aventure desalue a la partie desus, et ceu avient poc;	And sometimes it dislocates above that part, and this happens rarely;
et ne desalue mie derrier por l’espaule, et ne desalue mie dedens por les ners;	And does not dislocate behind for the shoulder, nor dislocate within for the nerves;
et plusors fois desalue desoz vers l’assele, meismement a ces qui ont poc de char, car a ces saut ele fuer hastanment;	And it repeatedly dislocates from above towards the elbow, even for those with little muscle, because in these cases force acts quickly;
a ces qui ont assez char, saut ele a poines, et rentre a poines.	For those with enough muscle, it jumps to the bone and returns to the bone.
Et par aventure avient a aucuns homes percussion ou casseure, et enfle li espaule d’un aposteme chaut, et cuide qu’elle est desaluee par ceu.	And by chance happens to some men through impact or bruising, and swells the shoulder with an abscess, and they think it is dislocated due to this.
Il covient donques que tu l’esprueves, tant que tu en soies certains;	Therefore, you must experience it, as long as you are certain;
et adonques encomence la cure.	And then begin the treatment.
Et est conue li dislocations quant il est aval vers l’assele, et met difference entre l’espaule malade et la saine, et tu troveras entre lor diversiteit manifeste;	And when it moves inward towards the elbow, you will recognize the dislocation, and distinguish between the diseased shoulder and the healthy one, and you will find a clear manifestation of their diversity;
et troveras au chief de l’espaule une fosse, et desoz l’assele au tochier le chief de l’espaule, ausi com se ce soit uns oes;	And you will find a hollow at the top of the shoulder, and as it goes from the elbow to the wrist, the top of the shoulder resembles that, just like if it were an eye;
et ne puet li malaides ramener sa main a son neis, ne movoir de nulz movemens;	And the patient cannot bring his hand back to his nose, nor move it with any movements;
et ausi, s’elle est desaluee en haut, si n’est mie occultee, car tu le trueves manifestement au tochier;	And similarly, if it is dislocated at the top, even if not entirely hidden, because you clearly find it at the nape;
et ceste maniere de dislocation n’est mie fors a ramener, quant elle est novele, ou se li enfes est malaides.	This manner of dislocation can only be remedied through realignment when it is new, or when the child has just been born.
Et li maniere est que li ministres lieve la main dou malaide en haut, puis met tes peuchas desoz l’assele, et lieve la jointure a force en haut au leu;	And the method is that the ministers lift the hand from the skin at the top, then place their thumbs under the arch, and lift the joint upwards forcefully at its natural position.
et li ministres lieve la main, et l’estende en haut, pues le mette desoz;	And the ministers lift the hand and extend it upwards, then place it under;
si venra hastanment.	If it comes quickly.
Et s’elle ne vient si com nos avons dit em mains jors aprés, si covient ke li malaides soit baigniez en aigue chaude;	And if she does not come as we have said after a few days, it is necessary that the patient be bathed in hot water;
et li amenistre arosement mollifiant et assouajant, si com decoction de altee et de fenugrec et de mellilote en aigue, et soit amenistree;	and the attendant should gently soothe and alleviate it, as in decoctions of rue, fenugreek, and melilot in water, and be administered;
puis soit sovinez li malaides sus son dos, et mette on desoz l’assele un sto de lainne igal, ne trop mol ne trop dur, puis mette li mires son talon sus le sto, et lieve le chief de l’espaule vertuousement, et traie la main dou malaide;	then sew the patient on their back, and place a cushion of equal wool under them, neither too soft nor too hard, then place the heel on the cushion, and lift the head off the shoulder, and lift the arm away from the side.
et uns autres ministres teigne lou chief dou malaide, si qu’il ne se mueve aval;	and have another attendant hold the back of the patient's head so that it does not move downward;
celle espaule revient tout maintenant, et se tu vues si le ramoinne selonc ceste maniere:	this shoulder is now coming back, and if you see whether lifting it follows this manner:
et est que tu faices estre present I home qui soit plus grans que li malaides;	And make it so that you ensure the presence at home, which is larger than the patient;
et soit drois devers lou costeit, et boute s’espaule desoz l’assele dou malaide, et lieve l’assele en haut, si que li malaides pende en l’ar;	And have them face towards the costeit, support their shoulder above the patient's side by the bone beneath the skin, and lift the bone upwards so that the patient hangs down.
et uns autres ministres traie la main dou malaide aval devers lou ventre.	And have another person guide their hand from below towards the belly underneath the patient.
Et se li malaides est trop legiers, si pent avec lui aucune chose pesant, et li dislocation revient maintenant.	And if the patient is too weak, so he cannot bear any weight with it, and the dislocation returns immediately.
Et le ramoinne on ausi en autre maniere:	And it can also be reset in another way:
et est c’on fiche I lonc tison en terre, dont li chiés soit ausi reons com I pistal, et ne soit ne trop gros ne trop graile;	And consider putting the long stick in the ground, so that the shoulder is also bent like a bow, and neither too large nor too slippery;
puis soit mis desoz lou malaide, mais k’il ait drapelz souef sus, et li malaides soit estans dou lonc dou fust;	Then place it under the patient, but so that there is dirt underneath, and have the patient lying on their back.
puis soit estendue sa main aval d’autre part forment, et li jointure revenra en son leu hastanment;	Then extend his hand up to the other side, form it into a position, and the joint will return to its place quickly.
et s’elle ne vuet revenir por toutes ces choses que nos avons dit, si fai ceste cure:	And if she does not want to return through all these things that we have said, then perform this treatment:
pren I tison de II bras de grant et IIII dois de large, qui ait le chief reont por mues entrer em parfont desoz l’assele, selonc ceste forme:	Take two large thorns from the second branch and four broad sticks, which have their tips rounded to easily enter over the armpit, according to this shape:
puis lie sus le chief dou fust drapelz souez, que li fust ne blece lou malaide, puis le met desoz l’assele dou malaide;	Then bind the tip of the shaft under a cloth so it does not burn the skin of the patient, then place the shaft over the armpit near the sore.
et estende som bras sus le fust dou lonc, et lie l’ajutoire sus le fust, et lou bras au chief de la main, puis met le bras sus I eschillon d’une eschiele dou large, et soit estendue li mains aval, et soit laissiez li cors pendans d’autre part:	And extend your arm above the shaft for its entire length, and attach the shoulder to the shaft, and place the arm at the tip of the hand's wrist, then place your arm on one side of a large board, and keep the hand extended downwards, leaving the body hanging from the other side:
li jointure reva ens maintenant.	The joint moves now.
Et quant elle est ens, en quel maniere que ce soit, si covient que tu mettes desoz l’assele une spere de laine igal, puis met l’emplaustre aparilliet de poudre dou molin, avec encens et aubun d’uef, sus toute l’espaule et entor, puis l’estrain desoz l’assele avenanment, et torne le liien sus l’emplaustre, et embraice la main a son col, et soit li mains demorans ensi.	And when it is done, no matter how it was done, if it should be that you place upon the joint a rod of hair equal, then apply an adhesive plaster with ground powder from the mill, along with incense and egg yolk, over all the shoulder and around, then remove from the joint addition, and rebind over the plaster, and hold your hands in this way. And let your hands remain like this.
Et covient qu’il menjuce poc, tant que li membres soit confortez, car il sanera plus tost;	And it must be eaten little at first, until the limb is strengthened, because it will heal faster;
et puis menjuce plus aprés V jors ou VII, et le mueve;	and then eat more after five or seven days, and move it;
et s’il est fermeis et il n’est mollifiez, si est sanez.	and if it is firm and not made soft, it will be healed.
Et se li jointure est fuer de leu por moistor que i est venue, ou por autre cause, si covient que tu i aministres cauteres a III pertus, si com il est mis devant ou chapistre des cauteres.	And if the joint has moved out of its place because of moisture or for another reason, it is necessary that you apply three burnings to it, as was explained in our previous chapter about burnings.
Et se tu fais tout ceu, et il deslie aprés VII jors, et li jointure ne se tient, et ne puet lever som bras amont, adonc saiches que li nerf au chief de l’espaule sont copeit ou estendut ou amollis;	And if you do all this, and it dislocates after seven days, and the joint does not hold, and cannot lift your arm upwards, then know that the nerve at the head of the shoulder are torn or stretched or softened;
et saiches que li jointure n’iert jamais fichie en son leu.	and know that the joint will never be firmly placed in its place.
Li dislocation qui est devers lou pis, et les mameles, ou derrier, si est faite par impulsion, et estendement de mains, et i aministre on autre lieure;	The dislocation that is towards the buttocks and breasts, or behind, if it's caused by pushing and stretching of the hands, and is administered elsewhere;
et cure tant qu’il soit sanez.	And treat until it has healed.
Et se aprés la sanation vient grietez au membre, et tardemens em movement, si use li malaides bain maintes fois, tant que celle grietez soit alegie, et reviegne a sa premiere nature.	And if after the healing comes redness to the limb, and delayed movements, then immerse the patient in hot baths many times, until that redness is alleviated, and returns to its original state.
de la dislocation dou coute	of the shoulder joint issue
Saiches que li jointure dou coute est desaluee a poinnes, et a poinnes revient;	The joint of the shoulder is dislocated by pricks, and by pricks it returns;
et s’est desaluee de toutes pars, et meismement devant et derrier, et li dislocations n’est mie reponue, car on la voit bien et sent bien;	And it is dislocated from all sides, both in front and behind, and the dislocation does not respond, for you can see it clearly and feel it well;
et desalue selonc chescune figure.	And dislocates according to each figure.
Et quant tu joins le coute malaide avec lou sain, si le pues veoir apertement.	And when you connect the cut wound with healthy tissue, if you can see it clearly.
Car li jointure est chevee, et ne puet ploier lou bras, ne touchier son espaule a tout.	For the joint is broken, and cannot bend the arm or reach his shoulder at all.
Et covient que tu le ramoinnes ainsois que apostemes chaus i viegne, car se apostemes chaus i venoit, si seroit grief li ramener;	And it is necessary that you reset it in this way when the pus bursts and spreads, for if it bursted and spreaded, it would be a complaint to bring back;
et par aventure ne puet estre ramenez dou tout en tout, meismement quant ele est au derrier;	And by chance cannot be brought back entirely, even when it is at the back;
si vaut pis que les autres dislocations, et est de plus grant dolor, et par aventure i vient li mors.	It is worse than other dislocations, and causes more pain, and by chance it leads to death.
Et li restauration si est, quant elle est telz c’on la puet ramener, que tu li estendes sa main a tes II mains;	And this restoration occurs, when it's such that we can bring it back, you extend his hand to your two hands;
et ses bras soit espandus, et les mains dou mire selonc le coute entor, desor et desoz, et boute la jointure a ses peuchas ensamble, ou a la racine de sa palme, tant qu’ele reviegne a son leu.	And his arms be spread outwards and inwards towards the elbow joint from both sides, forwards and backwards, then set the joint to its place or at the base of his palm, until it returns to its normal position.
Et se li dislocations est au devant, si revient quant il double sa main a sa main, et fier de la racine de la palme lou coute qui est desaluez.	And when it comes to dislocation in front of the body, it returns as soon as he doubles his hand on his own and holds the joint at the base of the palm with a tool that is set back.
Et s’il ne vuet revenir au leu, si aministre fort extension;	And if it does not return to its original position, administer strong extension;
et est que dui ministre estendent le bras, et le teignent dui ministre, si qu’il ne se mueve a l’estension;	And if two people assist in extending the arm and support it together, so that it does not move during extension;
puis torne le bras de chescune part, puis que tu as envoloupeit un drapeil double lonc et large;	Then turn the arm in each direction, then when you have enveloped it with a long and wide double band;
et quant li mires a jointe la jointure a sa main, si l’oigne d’aucun oile por amolir la jointure, puis boute la jointure forment, tant qu’ele reviegne;	And when you place the joints at their joint with your hand, if you smear them with some oil to soften the joint, then bend the joint properly, until it heals;
et quant elle est au leu, si met sus emplaustre sec avec aubun d’uef, et l’estrain forment, et pent le bras au col dou malaide, et le laisse aucuns jors, puis le deslie.	And when it's in place, put it on dry plaster with an egg yolk, hold it steady, bend the arm at the neck to the side, and leave it for a few days, then release it.
Et se li jointure est ferme en son leu, si deslie lou liien, et le laisse;	And if the joint is firm in its place, release the tie, and leave it;
et se tu vois que li jointure n’estrigne bien, si rencomence l’emplaustre et lou lien, et le laisse ensi aucuns jors, tant qu’il soit fermement mis;	And if you see that the joint is not fitting well, redo the plaster and the tie, and leave it like this for a few days, until it is firmly set.
puis le deslie.	Then release it.
Et se il sent grieteit aprés le ramenement de la jointe, et elle se muet, si le baigne et frote bellement, et presse tant qu’il soit assouagiez;	And if it feels sore after the return of the joint, and it moves, should it be bathed and well rubbed, and squeezed until it is soothed.
ou tu met sus la jointure une naige de mouton grasse, puis la laisse I jor et une nuit, puis l’oste, et lou fai entrer ou bain;	Or you place a fat sheep's fat on the joint, then leaves it for a day and a night, then apply the plaster, and let him bathe in or enter the bath;
et quant il sue, se li frote la jointure tempreement, puis remet la naige sus, et puis entre ou bain;	And when it sweats, rub the joint gently, then put back the fat, and then let him bathe in or enter the bath;
et ensi fai II fois ou III, tant qu’il soit sanez;	And do this two times or three, until it heals.
et se tu vues, si met sus fien de vaiche moiste chaufeit avec burre, et l’estrain sus;	And if you see that, put wet cow manure heated with butter on it, and apply it;
si revenra a sa disposition.	If it returns to its place.
li dislocation de la main	the dislocation of the hand
Li jointure de la main desalue, et li revenue est legiere, plus que les autres jointures.	The joint of the hand dislocates easily, more so than other joints.
Toutevoie, il la covient ramener au leu hastanment, en l’oure meisme qu’ele est desaluee, ainsois que li leus soit enflez, ou qu’il i viegne aposteme chaut.	Otherwise, it is necessary to return it to its place immediately while it is dislocated, as soon as it becomes dislocated. It should be noted that the limbs swell or an abscess forms.
Et li ramenemens si est que tu mettes la main malaide sus une tauble, et estende li ministres la main, et li mires la mette igal, ensi que il mette sa paume sus l’aparance de la jointure, et la boute tant qu’elle reviegne.	And the repositioning is done by placing the painful hand on a board, stretching out the assistant's hand, and guiding them to make it equal. You should have your palm facing towards the appearance of the joint, and hold it until it becomes normal again.
Toutevoie, il covient que vos regardez s’il est bien a leu;	Otherwise, you must check if it is properly in place;
adonc mette li malaides lou dos de sa main sus une tauble a l’estension et au ramenement.	Therefore, have the patient lay down their palm of their hand on a board during stretching and repositioning.
Et se li dislocations est au dos de la main, si mette li malaides son dos de sa main sus la tauble, et li mires mette sa main sus cele apparance de la jointure.	And if the dislocation is in the back of the hand, then have the patient place the back of his hand on the table, and you look to place his hand at the appearance of the joint.
S’elle revient maintenant, c’est bien.	If it returns now, it's simply so.
Se ce non, si l’estrain d’emplaustres apaisans apostemes chaus, et lou laisse ensi sens rencomencier.	If not, if the removal of plaster dressings that calm abscesses is done, and he leaves like this without needing to start again.
Et s’il ne le puet soffrir, et tu ne la pues mettre au leu aprés aucuns jors, si demore li jointure torte;	And if he cannot bear it, and you do not put him in the right place after a few days, if the joint remains bent;
et ne nuist niant au malaide fuer que tant que li mains est amoillie, et ne puet estraindre aucune chose a tout:	And it does no harm to the patient as long as his arms are immobilized, and he cannot strain anything at all:
adonc saiches que li nerf sont copez, ou li artere;	So know that the nerve is cut, or the artery;
si n’i a autre engien fuer que d’estraindre par cautere delez le cas, et par aventure n’i vaut autre chose.	If there is no other way than to apply the cautery for removal, and by chance there is no other remedy.
Et quant li mains est au leu, si met sus l’emplaustre que nos avons dit, puis l’estrain et le laisse .v. jors, puis le deslie et laisse ensi.	And when the hands are in plaster, apply what we have said on plaster, then apply it and leave them for five days, then remove it and leave them as is.
Et s’il ne la puet bien movoir, et il i a aucune grieteit, si la moille d’aigue chaude, et le frote tant qu’il soit sanez.	And if he cannot move it well, and there is no pain, if the water is warm, and rub it until it becomes clean.
de la dislocation des dois de la main	Regarding the dislocation of the fingers of the hand.
Aucune fois sont desaluez li doi de la main a chescune part, aucune fois au dos de la palme ou au ventre;	No dislocations are ever done to either hand, each part alone, or on the back of the palm or belly.
adonques estent le doi, et boute la dislocation a tes pouchés tant qu’il reviegne, puis sostien lou chief dou doi, et le pent vers la partie ou il est desjoins;	Therefore treat the shoulder, and maintain the dislocation in your hands until it heals. Then support the head of the shoulder, and guide it towards the side where it was dislocated;
et le laisse II jors, et puis le met igal celui jor;	and leave it for two days, then set it evenly on that day;
et de nut le lie, si com nos avons dit, et lou deslie de jor, et lou fai movoir, et le relie la nut;	and fasten it as we have said, and loosen it each day, let it move, and fasten it again the next;
et fai ce sovent, tant qu’il soit estroit, et tout ausi fai, se il est desaluez au ventre de la main, et fai si com tu as fait ci devant, tant qu’il soit sanez;	and repeat this often until it is tightened, and do the same if dislocated in the hand's belly, perform as shown here until it heals;
et tout ausi fai, quant il est desaluez d’autre part.	And do exactly the same thing when it has dislocated on another side.
dou desaluement de l’eschinee dou dos	Dislocation of the ankle, dislocation of the back
Quant l’eschinee dou dos ou dou col est desaluee, ou il en i a plusors desaluees, si n’i a point de cure, car li mors haste le malaide.	When it is dislocated in the back or neck, or when there are multiple dislocations, if no cure is applied, because time rushes the patient into harm.
Et li signes si est que li egestions saut fuer sens volunteit, ne ne la puet tenir, et maintes fois sont mollifiez aucun membre, ou les II cuixes ou li dui bras ou I.	And the signs are that the discharges go against one's will, cannot be held back, and many times they soften some limbs, or both legs, or both arms, or the neck.
Et maintes fois se muet li eschinee a IIII pars;	And many times the buttocks move to four sides;
celle qui se muet au derrier si est apelee «gilbositez»:	That which moves at the backside is called "gibbosity":
li cure si est que tu rewarde se li gilbositez est venue d’enfance:	The treatment consists in returning the gibbosity, which has come from childhood:
si n’i ait point de cure ne de sanation dou tot.	If there is no cure or healing throughout.
Et celle que vient de cheoir ou de percussions ou de semblans choses, dirent li ancien manieres de cures par grans paroles, ou il n’a mie en toutes grant profit;	And that which comes from childbirth or impacts or similar things, according to the old methods of treatment using big words, is not benefited in all great ways;
mais je l’ai abregiet selonc mon entention, et ai formez estrumens en diverses manieres.	But I have summarized it according to my intention, and formed instruments in various ways.
Je dis que en la gilbositeit que vient au pis devant, nen a engien ne santeit;	I say that when in pregnancy there is a disturbance before the anus, no one remains healthy;
et ausi cele que vient droitement en II costez, et ne puet on curer fuers que celi proprement qui vient au dos, si com je dis;	And similarly that which comes directly to the two sides, and one can only cure inside what comes to the back, as I say;
et est que li malaides soit estendus sus sa faice en I leu igal, et ait de l’estrain desoz lui, qu’il ne se blece;	And it is that the patient stretches on his back evenly to the first part, and there is no strain on him, so he does not blister;
puis fiche I tison au chief en terre forment, et I autre as piez, et lie un liien pardesoz les asseles dou malaide, et I autre as hainches, et as genous, et as chevilles;	Then place the first stick in the ground and form it, and the other at the ankles, and tie a string under all the knees of the patient, and the other at the hips, and at the knees, and at the ankles;
et dui ministre saichent les liiens, li uns au chief et li autres as piez, parmi les II tisons;	And two helpers know how to bind them, one at the head and others at the joints, among the two pokers;
et soient bien fermez, li tison si com nos avons dit, et li mires mette ses paumes sus l’espinee forment, tant qu’ele reviegne.	And be well closed, the poker as we have said, and the mirror place her palms on the spine form, until she recovers.
Et s’elle ne revient par ceste cure, si pren une tauble de III bras de lonc, et chevé desoz la paroit, et li malaides soit en costé, et boute le chief de la tauble desoz la paroit, puis met le mileu de la tauble sus l’espinee;	And if she does not recover from this treatment, take a plank of three spans long and set it over her back, and if the patient is on their side, place one end of the table under the spine. Then lay the middle part of the table on the spine;
et mette li mires ses piez sus l’autre chief de la tauble, et presse bien, tant qu’il reviegne au leu;	And have the mirror place her feet at the other end of the table, and press well until she recovers to her usual state;
et se tu vues, si le fai au tornet qui torne a la main.	And if you notice that it twists at the elbow which turns towards the hand.
Et est que tu fiches II tisons au chief dou malaide d’un bras de grant, et devers les piez II autres, et ait entre chescun tison, desoure et desoz, une paume d’espaice de lonc;	And you should place two sticks at the head of the sufferer's arm from half a span long, and in between each stick, there is an area of about one palm's width.
et ait en chescun tison I pertus, ou li tornet corre, et soient li tison fermement en terre, si qu’il ne se muevent;	And place a notch in each stick, or where the elbow corresponds, and have the sticks firmly set into the ground, so they do not move.
et entre chescuns II tisons ait I tison tornant, sor coi li liien tornent, et ait en II tornans II petis tisons d’une paume de lonc, por torner le tornet;	And between each pair of sticks place another stick turned, at the point where they would normally turn, and have two small turning sticks, about one palm's length, to help turn the elbow.
et puis lie lou lien qui est parmi les asseles au tornet devers le chief, et l’autre liien devers les piez a l’autre tornet, et chescuns des ministres torne son tornet a tout le liien, et li maistres mette l’espinee igal si com nos avons dit.	And tie the junction point between elbows at the elbow towards the head and the other joint towards the feet on the other elbow. Each servant turns their elbow to all the joints equally, as we have said, and the master applies the spine evenly in this manner.
Et quant elle est igalz, si met sus emplaustre desiccatif avec abun d’uef, et puis les estoupes, et puis l’estele d’une tablete de III dois de lonc, que porpreigne lou leu de la gilbositeit et la partie de l’espondile sainne, puis le lie d’un liien, si com nos avons dit, et use li malaides de norrissement subtil, tant qu’il soit sanez;	And when they are even, place on it a desiccating plaster with plenty of egg whites, then coat it, and then apply turpentine, and then rub it with a tablet of three inches long, which penetrates the fatty part and the healthy portion of the spine, then bind it with a bandage, as we have said, and use the patient to endure slight blisters until they are healed;
et s’aucune chose vient en la fin de la santez, si covient aministrer medicines amollissans et asouajans, avec l’estele que nos avons dit ci devant;	And if nothing comes at the end of healing, it is necessary to administer softening and soothing medicines, with the turpentine that we have mentioned before;
et aucune fois i aministre on une piece de plonc, et aucune fois vient li apparance en la derriere spondile dou dos, et cuide on que ce soit dislocations;	And each time one administers a piece of cork, and every time there appears the appearance behind the spinal bone in the back, and be careful that it is dislocation;
et c’est li os qui apert, por coi on n’i doit mie avoir presumption:	And it is the bone that opens, for which one must not have presumption:
par aventure feroit venir la mort.	By chance death might come about.
des dislocations de la hainche	dislocations of the hip
Saiches que as jointures de la hainche et as jointures de l’espaule ne vient fuers que dislocacions soulement, ne n’i vient mie si com as autres jointures;	Know that the joints of the hips and the joints of the shoulder come only from dislocations alone, not like other joints.
et li jointure de la hainche est desaluee selonc IIII parties:	And the hip joint is dislocated according to four parts:
dedens et defuer ,et devant et derrier;	Inside and outside, in front and behind;
et plus dedens c’aillors, et poc desalue devant et derrier.	And even more inside there, and only partially dislocated forward and backward.
Et li conoissance de sa dislocations dedens si est que quant on joint la jambe malaide avec la sainne, si est plus longe, et apert plus li malaides genous que li sains, et ne puet li malaides doubler son genoil au feu;	And the knowledge of such a dislocation inside is that when you join the diseased leg with the healthy one, it becomes longer, and the diseased knee opens further than the healthy one, and the diseased knee cannot bend over the fire;
et est li leus qui est delez enflez d’aposteme chaut, por ceu que li chiés de la cuixe vient lai.	And it is where the limb is swollen due to an abscess, because the joints of the shoulder come there.
Et li signe de celui cui il vient au defuer, si est que cist accident sont contraire a ces devant.	And the sign of him who approaches death, so it is that this event is contrary to what was before.
Et li signes de celui cui avient au devant, si est qu’il estent bien sa jambe selonc l’acomplissement;	And for those who have it in front, if their leg is well according to completion;
toutevoie, ne double mie le genoil sens dolor, et s’on le vuet faire aler, si ne puet avant, et retient son urine, et enfle li angre, et quant il vait, si passe sus le talon.	Otherwise, don't double the calf without pain, and if you want to make it stand up, it can't before and holds its urine, and swells the leg, and when it walks, it passes over the heel.
Et li signes de celui cui il avient derrier, si est qu’il ne puet espandre son genoil, ne doubler, et est celle jambe plus torte de l’autre, et li angre est mollifié, et est li chiés de la cuixe au leu desoz les costes.	And the signs of him who is behind are such that he cannot spread his knee or double it, and that leg is more curved than the other, and his ankle is flattened, and that shoulder comes up under his back.
Li ramenemens de ceste semblance de dislocation si est que tu rewarde se li dislocations est anciainne, et elle demore selonc sa disposition, si n’i a nule cure;	The process for this simile of dislocation is that you reward it when the dislocation is old, and it stays according to its position, if there is no treatment;
et n’i covient mie qu’il ait presumption.	And it should not have any assumption.
Et en celi dont li dislocation est fresche, et c’est des IIII manieres de dislocation, si te haste que tu tornes la jointe, et l’esten dedens et defuer, et la muef a destre et senestre;	And in those whose dislocation is fresh, and there are four ways of dislocation, if you rush to correct the joint, stretch it inside and outside, and move it right and left;
par aventure si revenra, et n’a mestier d’autre cure.	If by chance it returns, and there is no need for another treatment.
Et s’il ne revient en ceste maniere, si covient que tu apareilles I ministre fort, et esten la jambe fort a II mains, ou a I liien que soit liiez sus lou genoil;	And if it does not return in this way, then you must apply great force, and hold the leg strongly with both hands, or with one tie under the knee.
et uns autres ministres estende sa main desus en teil maniere qu’il boute ses mains desoz ses asseles, puis l’estrigne d’un souef liien sus la cuixe;	And stretch out another's hand over it in such a way that they push their hands under their armpits, then pull it with one strong tie up to the thigh.
et uns autres tigne lou chief dou liien;	And hold the head with the other hand of the rope;
et estendent amont et aval tuit a une fois, tant que li malaide soit levez de terre a une fois, et demoure pendans.	Stretch both upwards and downwards at once, until the patient stands off the ground at once, and remains hanging.
Ceste maniere d’estension si est commune as .iiij. semblances, et se li dislocation est revenue, si com nos avons dit, c’est bien.	This method of extension is typical for four similar situations, and if the dislocation has returned, as we have said, it's correct.
Se ceu non, si covient mettre cure a sa semblance.	If not, then you should treat it according to its appearance.
Quant li dislocations est au pardedens, si covient que tu sovines le malaide sus son costeit sain, puis met le liien sus la racine de la cuixe, et le leu qui est desoz l’angre, puis estent le liien en haut devers l’angre, et devers la forcele;	When a dislocation is in the pardedens area, it is necessary for you to recall the condition on their healthy side, then put the tie on the root of the leg, and the part which is around the artery. Then adjust the tie above the artery, and against the force.
puis preigne uns autres ministres ses bras, et embraice le gros leu de la cuixe malaide, et l’estende au defuer forment:	Then take hold of another attendant's arms, and hug the thick part of the leg on the diseased side, and extend it to the rear in formation:
si revenra a son leu maintenant;	if it returns to its place now;
et ceste maniere de dislocation est plus legiere des autres.	and this way of dislocation is easier than others.
Et se tu ne la pues serrer en ceste maniere que nos avons dit, si covient que tu lies les II piés dou malaide ensamble d’un fort liien souef sus les II talons, et sus les II genous, et soit li jambe malaide estendue II dois plus que li autres;	And if you cannot compress it in this way as we have said, then it is necessary that you tie both feet of the diseased side together with a strong ligature around the two ankles and the two knees, and let the diseased leg extend two hands more than the others;
puis soit pendus sus le chief d’un fust, et soit en sus de terre II bras de lonc;	Then have them hung by their head on a pole, and above the ground two feet long;
puis comande a I ministre qu’il embraice le chief de la cuixe, et soit uns autres ministres pendans avec le malaide, qui embraice forment la cuixe, car li jointure revient maintenant hastanment.	Then command the minister to embrace the head of the goose, and have other ministers hanging with the patient, who embraces firmly the goose, because the joint is now returning quickly.
